Report on the results of parallel inspections of the administration of value added tax between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introductory word
The submitted material informs on the course and results of parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the area of value added tax administration and the use of the VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) information system.
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so revenues from value added tax affect not only the state budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
Parallel auditing activities were mainly aimed at controlling the procedure of tax administrators when scrutinizing the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions carried out between individual Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of VIES has enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of VAT payers in the various Member States of the European Union and on the commercial transactions carried out by those payers.
The discrepancy between the data in the VIES system and the data in the VAT return filed by the payer should alert the tax administrator to suspicious cases and enable the detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The benefit of the parallel checks carried out consisted not only in the exchange of information on the procedures of the tax or tax authorities for administering value added tax, but in particular in the examination of the use of the VIES system in monitoring the exercise of the right to exemption from value added tax in intra-Community transactions.
The knowledge gained during the implementation of parallel controls is beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of other parallel controls in cooperation with the audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel inspections of the administration of value added tax for the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6th 2005
Introduction
05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Administration of value added tax, (SK) Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) closed on 12. 9th 2005 Agreement on cooperation in control activities.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel auditing actions - Administration of Value Added Tax - included in the 2005 Audit Plan of the SAO, the Czech Republic under No. 05/19 and - Audit of the procedures of tax authorities in the administration, control and recovery of taxes from the added value and the fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between the member countries of the SAO - included in the Audit Plan of the SAO of the Slovak Republic under No. 22/2005.
The parallel control actions carried out were coordinated controls.
The result of the joint coordinated inspection was processed in accordance with European Enforcement Regulation 31 for INTOSAI inspection standards.
The cooperation consisted in exchanging information to the extent provided for in the contract concluded and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the parallel checks.
The purpose of the coordinated audit was to verify selected cases of delivery and acquisition of goods in suspicious business transactions between value added tax payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "CR") and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "SR").
Both parties contractually agreed to provide each other with information from public sources, from the electronic system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and data on received and sent requests to verify commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The audits were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the audit was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, South Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The audited bodies were the Ministry of Finance and 12 financial authorities: the Financial Authority in Mladá Boleslav, the Financial Authority in Kolín, the Financial Authority in Teplice, the Financial Authority in Karlovy Vary, the Financial Authority in Tábor, the Financial Authority Brno III, the Financial Authority in Znojmo, the Financial Authority in Zlín, the Financial Authority in Šumperk, the Financial Authority Ostrava I, the Financial Authority for Prague 7 and the Financial Authority for Prague 9.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the Exposures of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 9 selected tax offices: Tax Office Bratislava I, Tax Office Komárno, Tax Office Trenčín, Tax Office Prievidza, Tax Office Zvolen, Tax Office Dolný Kubín, Tax Office Košice II, Tax Office Košice V and Tax Office Michalovce.
Objective of inspections:
The aim of the parallel auditing actions was to examine the procedure of the tax authorities in administering value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") after the integration of the Czech Republic and Slovakia into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "EU") and to examine the use of the VIES electronic information system, especially when controlling the application of the VAT exemption.
The audited period of the coordinated audit covered the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6th 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions The electronic VIES system is in place in the EU Member States, which allows tax administrations to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT, and in the country of destination to check whether the customer has properly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
VIES is not centralised within the EU, each Member State is developing its own system.
The audit revealed differences in national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the following areas:
The recapitulative statements indicate the values of deliveries of goods to other EU Member States; the values of services rendered are not included in the recapitulative statements.
In the Czech Republic, data from summary reports submitted by Czech payers are processed at the level of tax authorities, where they are compared with data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States stated in VAT tax returns.
Financial authorities transmit data from recapitulative statements to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In the Slovak Republic, data from summary reports filed by Slovak taxpayers at tax offices are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of supplies of goods and the value of supplies of services to other EU Member States on separate lines of VAT tax returns, which makes it possible to compare the values stated in summary returns with the values of supplies of goods according to VAT returns and to identify any differences between them.
In the Slovak Republic, the values of goods and services supplied to other EU Member States are reported cumulatively on a common line of the VAT return.
As a result, in the Slovak Republic, the system does not allow for automatic identification of differences between the values of supplies of goods according to VAT tax returns and recapitulative statements.
Separate reporting of the values of supplies of goods in VAT returns makes it possible to use the results of data comparisons to control the VAT exemption of supplies of goods to the EU.
Delivered data from summary reports filed by payers in other EU Member States are processed on the CLO and compared with the value of acquisition of goods stated by payers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia in VAT returns.
In the Slovak Republic, these data are sent to the tax authorities and the tax administrators themselves decide which cases of differences to check.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) determines which quantified differences between the values of supplies and acquisitions of goods must be verified by the tax administrators and submits a list of these cases to the locally competent tax authorities.
This ensures that, for the most significant deviations, it is verified whether the VAT on the acquisition of the goods has been declared correctly.
The audit also highlighted some problems in the VAT administration system complications caused by different reporting of intra-Community transactions (i.e. supplies and acquisitions of goods by payers from different EU Member States):
In the EU, recapitulative statements are submitted for each calendar quarter and the maximum time limit for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
The reduction of the period covered by recapitulative statements to one month, together with the reduction of the processing period, would allow earlier access to VIES data.
This would allow tax administrations to check more effectively whether VAT on intra-Community acquisitions has been declared in the correct amount.
At the same time, filing VAT returns and recapitulative returns for the same tax period (month) would allow faster verification of whether the payer declared identical values of supplies of goods to the EU in both the recapitulative return and the VAT tax return.
Differences between the values of deliveries of goods reported by EU payers and the values of acquisitions of goods reported by payers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia were caused, among other things, by different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and acquisitions in individual EU Member States.
These included, for example, the inclusion of received advances in summary reports or the reporting of intra-Community supplies in the supplier's summary report in a different quarter than intra-Community acquisitions in the purchaser's VAT tax return.
Harmonising the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would make the control activities of the tax administrations of individual Member States more effective.
Cooperation between the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was also aimed at examining selected intra-community transactions carried out between the two countries.
Together, a total of 40 cases of commercial transactions carried out between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined, where there were doubts about their implementation or suspicions of VAT evasion.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic found the following facts:
tax subjects have declared in their VAT returns for the purpose of unduly obtaining excess VAT the carrying out of intra-Community transactions which have not actually taken place;
tax subjects declared intra-Community supplies in carousel transactions where the value of supplies was deliberately reduced several times in order to draw excessive VAT deductions;
suppliers declared in their VAT returns and recapitulative statements intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to purchasers who were so-called "lost companies" and did not declare the tax on the goods acquired;
suppliers have made intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to taxable persons who have not been registered for VAT in another Member State.
In such cases, the supply should not have been exempt from VAT and should have been subject to tax in the supplier's country;
suppliers declared intra-Community supplies in their VAT returns at a higher value than that declared by the purchasers of intra-Community acquisitions, in some cases VAT was declared at an incorrect amount.
The findings of the audit showed that VIES provides tax administrations with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
Tax administrations should pay particular attention to the rigorous examination of the differences between the data reported by VAT payers and the VIES data and to the use of all information in tax proceedings.
The issue of value added tax after the accession of the Czech Republic and Slovakia to the EU
Value Added Tax
On 1. 5. In 2004, the Czech Republic and Slovakia became members of the EU.
Following EU accession, internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within the EU were abolished.
He was the VAT administrator until 30. 4th 2004 the relevant tax or tax office, with the exception of the import of goods and occasional bus transport in the Czech Republic, where the tax administrator was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), or Act No. 222/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as Act No. 222/2004 Coll.), the administration of VAT on the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU Member States has passed from customs offices to tax or tax authorities.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., the delivery of goods in the Czech Republic means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as owner.
A supply of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is a supply of goods that have actually been dispatched or transported to another EU Member State.
According to the provisions of Section 64 of Act No.235/2004 Coll., it is an exempt taxable supply with the right to deduct VAT if the goods are delivered to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 8 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll., the supply of tangible property in which the right of ownership is changed is considered a supply of goods in Slovakia.
The transfer of goods which are in the possession of the taxable person from the territory of the country to another Member State shall also be regarded as a supply of goods if those goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
Under Article 43 of Law No 222/2004 Coll., the supply of goods from the Czech Republic to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the customer is a person identified for VAT purposes in another Member State.
According to the provisions of Section 16 of Act No.235/2004 Coll., the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods that are dispatched or transported to the customer by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech payer purchases goods at a price exclusive of VAT and is obliged to declare VAT in the Czech Republic in accordance with the provisions of Section 25 of Act No.235/2004 Coll., if the conditions set out in Section 73 of this Act are met, he is entitled to deduct VAT.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 11 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll., the acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic from another EU Member State means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of movable tangible property sent or transported to the purchaser by the supplier or purchaser or on their behalf to the Czech Republic from another Member State.
Tax liability in the Slovak Republic arises for the payer when acquiring goods in the Czech Republic from another Member State pursuant to the provisions of Section 20 of Act No.222/2004 Coll.
Under the provisions of Section 49 of Act No 222/2004 Coll., the payer may deduct VAT if the tax is applied by him on the acquisition of goods within the country from another Member State in accordance with the provisions of Sections 11 and 11a of this Act.
According to the provisions of Section 17 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., or Section 45 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll., a trade concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States, where the subject of the trade is the supply of the same goods between these three persons.
Intra-Community transactions are supplies and acquisitions of goods made between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intra-community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia are shown in the following table.
VIES system
In order to monitor the application of the right to VAT exemption on intra-Community supplies of goods, a VAT information exchange system has been set up within the EU.
It includes the VIES electronic system, which allows the tax authorities of the EU Member States to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the taxable supply from VAT and, conversely, whether the purchaser duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State is developing its own VIES system.
National systems operate on a common principle and are interconnected through the EU's common communication network, the so-called CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was connected to the automated tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "ADIS") and in Slovakia to the application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "APV DIS").
These systems are used by the tax or tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the administration of taxes and duties.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU Member State obtains information on tax subjects that it would not have been able to obtain on its own without such cooperation.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is the fight against tax evasion and tax losses.
According to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State shall establish a central unit within the internal organisational structure in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the administration of VAT, the so-called "central unit." CLO (Central Liaison Office).
In the Czech Republic, the tasks arising from international cooperation are performed by the Ministry of Finance - the Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (hereinafter referred to as MF CLO) was established.
The function of the CLO in the Slovak Republic is performed by the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic, Department of International Administrative Cooperation (hereinafter referred to as "DR CLO").
These departments, among other things, communicate with EU foreign administrations in particular in the field of information exchange within the VIES system, exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax controls, verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter referred to as VAT numbers) of persons registered for VAT in other EU Member States and communication with the European Commission.
In order to examine a certain intra-Community transaction or to obtain other information relating to a particular tax entity, the tax authorities send requests for information to the EU through the MF CLO or DR CLO.
Through these requests, they obtain information from the requested Member States which they can use to determine VAT correctly.
Requests for information are sent mostly in electronic form between the Customs of the EU Member States, using a standardised SCAC form.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic was focused mainly on the examination of selected intra-Community transactions carried out between the two countries and on the level of use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation by the tax authorities.
The SAO, the Czech Republic required the SAO of the Slovak Republic to examine in 30 cases commercial transactions carried out between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
In 10 cases, the SAO requested the SAO to scrutinize commercial transactions between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
Examination of intra-community transactions revealed, among other things:
o
The SAO of the Czech Republic asked the SAO of the Slovak Republic to examine the procedure of the tax administrator to which the reply to the request for information was sent.
The Slovak tax office applied through the SCAC form for verification of the delivery of the goods (footwear) at 3. quarter 2004 from the Slovak payer in the value of 2 847 thousand Sk.
The Financial Office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer stated the acquisition of goods in this value only in the additional VAT tax return and delivered the same goods back to Slovak tax entities in the value of CZK 2,550,000 by the end of 2004.
On the basis of international cooperation between the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the locally competent tax authority fully acknowledged the Slovak supplier's right to an excessive deduction of VAT arising, among other things, from this supply.
This tax office did not provide information about the suspected re-export to the tax authorities of the locally competent purchasers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
This will trigger further examination of business activities in relation to possible carousel fraud.
o
The Czech tax administrator requested through the SCAC form to examine the supply of a technological line to Slovakia worth CZK 4,850 thousand in 2. 2004 quarter.
The tax proceedings carried out in Slovakia showed that only part of the technological line was delivered, components worth CZK 3,395 thousand were not delivered.
During the examination of this case, the SAO SR found that VAT on the taxable supply was declared by the Slovak tax entity on the amount of CZK 4,850 thousand in the VAT return (hereinafter referred to as "DAP") for the tax period 7/2004.
The SAO, CR also found that the Czech payer reported in its DAP an excessive VAT deduction in the amount of CZK 655,000 for the quarter, which was incurred by applying a VAT deduction from the purchase of this technological line from another domestic payer.
On the basis of the results of the investigation, the Czech Financial Office concluded that the Czech and Slovak tax subjects had established a business relationship for the purpose of unduly obtaining an excess VAT deduction, disputed the taxable performance and did not grant the Czech payer a part of the tax deduction entitlement in the amount of CZK 647,000.
o
In 2004, the Slovak tax administrator applied through the SCAC form for an examination of the supply of goods (copying machines) to the Czech payer in the value of SKK 24,246,000 made in December 2002.
These goods were purchased by the Slovak payer in November 2002 in Slovakia from another tax entity worth 29,667,000 Sk and subsequently sold to the Czech payer.
The Slovak tax entity applied an excess VAT deduction for the relevant tax period.
In a tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic, it was found that the Czech tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator and DAP for 4. did not file for the quarter of 2002 or thereafter.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak tax administrator, on the basis of the results of the tax audit, did not recognise the right to an excess deduction in the amount of SKK 5,541 thousand applied in the DAP for the month of 11/2002 and set the tax liability at SKK 1,750 thousand.
At the same time, that taxable person was not granted an exemption from VAT in respect of the export of the goods in December 2002.
o
The Czech tax administrator received an order from MF CLO to verify the value of the acquired goods for 3. 2004 quarter.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer was to purchase from Slovakia goods (diluent) worth 3,767,000 Sk.
This tax subject did not cooperate with the tax administrator, did not file a DAP and was charged ex officio VAT of CZK 0 for the months 7 to 12/2004.
The Czech tax administrator requested through the SCAC form to verify whether deliveries of goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic took place, in what amount and price (according to invoices).
In reply, the Slovak Tax Office sent a copy of the invoice, the bills of lading and the demand for payment of the invoice.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak payer was granted an exemption with the right to deduct VAT for this supply.
The SAO, CR found that the Czech tax administrator evaluated the response to the request for information delivered from Slovakia as evidence that the company had acquired goods from another EU Member State.
On the basis of further investigation, the Financial Office in the Czech Republic will ask the superior authority to review the tax liability.
o
The Slovak company supplied goods (particle board products) inter alia to an American company which stored these goods in the Czech Republic in a free zone of customs.
The operator of that free zone was indicated on the invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004, for example, an American company purchased particleboard tiles worth USD 57 600 (at a unit price of USD 100 per piece) from a Slovak payer and placed them in a free zone of customs.
Subsequently, the company transferred ownership of the goods to a Swiss company, with a value of USD 14 400 (unit price of USD 25 per piece), and the goods were exported back to Slovakia.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the area of the free zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax authority initiated tax inspections of individual tax periods in 2004 and 2005 at the supplier of goods suspected of carousel transactions.
Examination of the underlying transactions was requested from the Czech locally competent tax authorities via several SCAC forms.
The individual answers gradually created a picture of the trades and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from Slovakia and the Czech Republic in carousel trades.
The SAO and the Czech Republic, in cooperation with the SAO of the Slovak Republic, found that in these business relations there was a deliberately severalfold decrease in the value of goods.
On the basis of the information obtained, the Tax Directorate of Slovakia concluded that the carousel trade in this case is free pricing (i.e. import of undervalued goods and their overvaluation by domestic companies that are in the chain between the importer and the exporter), which is not a violation of the VAT Act in Slovakia.
Under the current legislation, the payment of excess VAT to export companies cannot be prevented as they fulfil all the conditions of the VAT exemption law.
o
The Czech payer was 12. 7th 2005 VAT registration cancelled.
On the 27th. 10 a.m. In 2005, on the basis of a voluntarily submitted application for VAT registration, this entity became a tax payer again.
The Czech tax entity entered in the DAP for the month of 8/2005 (i.e. the period when it was not a VAT payer) the value of the acquisition of goods (printing press) from Slovakia in the amount of CZK 1,174,000 and exercised the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to the delivery of goods from the Slovak payer in the amount of 1,530,000 Sk, which the Slovak payer stated in the DAP as a supply of goods to another EU Member State with the right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax authority requested verification of that supply by means of a SCAC form because the Slovak supplier had not proved how he had acquired the goods delivered to the Czech Republic.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech payer does not cooperate with the tax administrator and is not registered at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the Czech Republic by the locally competent tax administrator in order to verify the data.
o
The Slovak payer said in the summary report for 3. quarter 2004 delivery of goods worth 956 thousand Sk to a tax entity from the Czech Republic.
The VAT number of the Czech entity was identified by the VIES system as incorrect.
Verification in the payer database revealed that such a TIN has never been allocated in the Czech Republic.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it concerned the execution of electrical installation works on real estate in the Czech Republic, not the delivery of goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The services were invoiced without VAT, as the Czech entity informed the Slovak entity that it was registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak tax authorities requested verification of these facts by means of a SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic inquired with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic that the tax subject listed on the invoices as a customer had never been registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic, did not declare the tax on received services from the Slovak entity and did not declare the tax on acquisition of goods.
No local investigation or tax inspection was carried out at the Czech entity, its current residence is unknown.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator learned that the Czech tax entity had become a VAT payer by virtue of its acceptance of the service.
The Slovak tax entity will be tax audited for 1 to 4. 2004 quarter.
o
The Slovak payer said in the summary report for 3. quarter 2004 delivery of goods worth 1,055 thousand Sk to the Czech payer.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it concerned the execution of electrical installation works on real estate in the Czech Republic.
It was not a delivery of goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic, but a provision of services.
The Slovak tax authorities requested verification of these facts by means of a SCAC form.
The SAO, Czech Republic enquired with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of the supply and in order to examine the acquisition of goods from other EU Member States at 3. In the quarter of 2004, an on-the-spot investigation was carried out.
On the basis of this on-the-spot investigation, it was found that the present case did not indeed concern the acquisition of goods, but the acquisition of services, which were also reported by the Czech entity in the regular DAP.
The Financial Office also found that the Czech entity did not pay 3 for the tax period as a result of the wrong VAT calculation procedure. 2004 quarter VAT in the correct amount.
The tax subject submits an additional DAP.
When asked by the local tax office, the SAO SR found that the Slovak payer had incorrectly stated the provision of the service in the summary report and would be subject to a tax audit for 1 to 4. 2004 quarter.
o
The Czech tax entity voluntarily registered as a VAT payer from 10. 3rd 2004.
For 1. quarter 2004 filed DAP with a high turnover in both input and output.
The locally competent tax administrator initiated tax proceedings, the subject did not cooperate with the tax administrator, therefore due to the suspicion of involvement in carousel trade, he was charged VAT in the amount of CZK 0.
This payer has not filed another DAP.
On the grounds of non-compliance with his obligations under the law, his VAT registration was cancelled as of 4 April 2004. 1st 2005.
According to data from the VIES system, this entity should have acquired from the Slovak payer in 3 and 4. quarter 2004 goods worth 7 846 thousand Sk.
In order to verify the realisation of those transactions, the Czech tax authorities sent two requests for information to Slovakia.
In an inquiry to the local tax office, the SAO SR found that the manager of the Czech company denied the execution of the transactions and questioned the authenticity of his signature on invoices and other documents.
On the basis of the tax proceedings carried out in Slovakia, the intra-Community supply to the Czech Republic declared by the Slovak payer was questioned.
The payer will not be recognised as entitled to VAT exemption and will be charged VAT on the above amount.
o
According to data from the VIES system, the Czech payer should have purchased at 1. quarter 2005 from Slovak goods (work clothes) in the total value of 39 970 thousand Sk.
In this quarter, the Czech payer reported the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State only in DAP for the month of 3/2005, in the value of CZK 11,292,000.
The locally competent tax authority carried out an on-the-spot investigation of the entity in order to verify the data in this DAP.
Since the company did not provide any documents or otherwise prove that the taxable transactions had taken place, he assessed it on 9. 6th 2005 VAT administrator in the amount of CZK 0.
Due to doubts about the realisation of the acquisition of the goods, the tax administrator sent two requests for information to Slovakia in May 2005.
According to the response to the requests for information, the tax administrator in Slovakia had doubts about the implementation of business cases as well as about the implementation of the payment.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator sent DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out at the premises of the participating entities.
At the time of the coordinated audit, the locally competent tax administrator carried out further investigations concerning the Czech entity in the Czech Republic and an investigation by the Police of the Czech Republic was carried out at the same time.
o
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of involvement in carousel fraud.
Transactions with goods (work clothes) were carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia at 4. 2004 quarter and 1. 2005 quarter.
Slovak payer No. 1 supplied goods to Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No. 3, who delivered them back to payer No. 4 (see diagram No. 2).
(A)
Czech payer No. 2 was to acquire from Slovak payer No. 1 at 4. 2004 quarter goods (work clothes) worth 4 847 thousand CZK and 1. quarter 2005 goods worth CZK 17,050,000.
As the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the locally competent tax administrator sent the taxes to Slovakia on 25. 5. 2005 request for information.
In reply, the Slovak tax authority expressed doubts about the implementation of the business cases and about the implementation of the payment.
On 8. 6th 2005, a request for information was delivered to the Ministry of Finance (MF CLO) from Slovakia concerning goods worth 16,575,000 Sk, which were to be delivered by Slovak payer No. 1 to Czech payer No. 2 in December 2004.
The Slovak side demanded to verify whether Czech payer No 2 had actually received the goods, declared them in the DAP and paid VAT.
The official record prepared by the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic shows that Czech payer No.2 has not been registered at the address registered in the Commercial Register for a long time.
Although he was a VAT payer with a monthly tax year, he filed the DAP for a quarterly tax year.
In view of this, the Czech tax authorities could not charge VAT.
The realisation of the taxable supply between the Slovak payer No. 1 and the Czech payer No. 2 stated in the application in the amount of 16,575,000 Sk could not be verified due to the above mentioned facts.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel business in order to draw an excess VAT deduction.
(B)
Czech payer No. 3, engaged in the purchase and sale of passenger cars, submitted DAPs for the tax period of months 1 and 2/2005, in which he declared the delivery of goods (work clothes) to Slovak payer No. 4 with a total value of CZK 21,935,000.
These work clothes were to be purchased by Czech payer No.3 from Czech payer No.2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The locally competent tax office sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic, the object of which was mainly to verify whether Slovak payer No.4 had acquired goods worth CZK 1,025 thousand from Czech payer No.3 in December 2004 and at 1. quarter 2005 in the value of 21 935 thousand CZK.
The response to this request for information received from Slovakia showed that in the DAP for the month of 12/2004 Slovak payer No.4 stated the zero value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in the DAP for the months 1 and 2/2005 the value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State only amounted to 1,193 thousand Sk.
Slovak tax payer No 4 did not respond to the request to submit tax documents for the tax period from 10/2004 to 3/2005.
The on-the-spot investigation carried out in Slovakia revealed that the company was not located at the registered address.
The response also stated that this payer meets all the characteristics of the so-called "lost society" and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator sent DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out at the premises of the participating tax entities.
During the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax authority collected documents which would confirm or deny the existence of the goods.
VAT will be assessed according to the outcome of the investigation.
The Czech Police are also investigating the case.
Progress of control action
As part of the preparation of parallel auditing events, a coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO SR took place in the first half of July 2005.
The participants of this meeting got acquainted with the VAT legislation in both countries and the integration of the VIES electronic system into national databases.
The outcome of the meeting was the specification of the scope of cooperation and the determination of the conditions for the selection of control samples.
Both parties agreed that the cooperation will focus on the following areas: a) verification of the validity and correctness of VAT registration numbers of persons registered for VAT in the Czech Republic or Slovakia in intra-Community supplies; b) verification of data on intra-Community acquisitions listed in the DAP by payers in the Czech Republic using information from summary reports (hereinafter referred to as "SH") of payers from Slovakia contained in the VIES system, and vice versa; c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and Slovakia on business transactions carried out.
Furthermore, it was agreed that the selection of tax subjects for inspection will be carried out in relation to the volume of intra-Community supplies between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and Slovakia via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intra-Community transactions
The following diagram shows the procedure of information processing by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia during intra-Community supplies and acquisitions of goods.
5.1.1 Intra-Community supply
If the VAT payer makes an intra-Community supply, he is obliged to file the SH by the 25th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic provides summary information on supplies of goods to another EU Member State exempt from VAT in the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in the Slovak Republic is obliged to state the value of goods that have been exempted from tax and delivered from the Czech Republic to other EU Member States during the calendar quarter.
The information on the value of the delivered goods is always given in the SH in Czech or Slovak currency, broken down by individual tax entities, stating their VAT number under which they were registered in their country.
Service data shall not be included in the SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds that he has entered incorrect data in the SH, he is obliged to file a subsequent SH.
In the event that the payer in the SR finds that the data provided in the SH were incomplete or incorrect, he submits a correction to the SH before the expiry of the deadline for filing the SH, after which he is obliged to file an additional SH.
VIES allows the exchange of information on VAT-registered payers" registration data in EU Member States.
Payers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia can check whether the VAT number of the respective purchaser is registered in the given EU Member State.
The data from the submitted SH are grouped on the MF CLO or DR CLO by the VIES system according to the individual DIČ of the purchasers.
The aggregate value of all deliveries for each purchaser's VAT number and the code of the method of performance from all its Czech or Slovak suppliers, the so-called L1QD files, are created.
Data from L1QD files shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intra-community benefits between the Czech Republic and Slovakia (from L1QD files) is shown in the following table.
If VIES in another Member State detects an erroneous originator's TIN in the sent L1QD files, it generates an O_MCTL message containing all erroneous TINs indicating the type of error.
This message is then sent to MF CLO or DR CLO.
The O_MCTL message may contain 4 types of errors: formally incorrect TIN, TIN is not registered in the given state or has never been allocated, the customer with a certain TIN was not a VAT payer in the given quarter, VAT registration of the customer was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, the MF CLO transmits data from the received O_MCTL messages to the financial authorities.
If the wrong VAT number of a payer from the EU is used in one of the sent SH lines or subsequent SH lines, the so-called "Notification of doubts about VAT ID" is generated at the relevant tax office by the ADIS system.
The tax office will check whether the supply to a VAT-registered payer in another EU Member State has actually taken place and will record the result of the verification in the system.
In SR, the DR CLO processes all O_MCTL messages in the VIES system and sends them electronically to the locally competent tax authorities together with the identification of the taxpayers who have entered the wrong TIN in their SH.
Subsequently, the tax authorities invite the payer to submit an additional SH and provide valid VAT numbers, or the tax office will verify the delivery of goods to the respective payer when reporting an invalid VAT number in the submitted SH.
Data on the number of erroneous VAT numbers relating to intra-community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia are given in the following table.
Of the total number of 41 728 VAT numbers of Czech payers listed in the Slovak payers" SH in the period from 2. quarter 2004 to 1. In the 2005 quarter, there were 929 erroneous TINs, i.e. 2.23%.
Of the total number of 62 997 Slovak payers" VAT numbers listed in the SH of Czech payers in the same period, 416 were incorrect VAT numbers, i.e. 0.66%.
When reporting intra-Community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, Czech VAT payers reported on average fewer erroneous VAT numbers in their SH than Slovak VAT payers.
During the examination of the activities of the tax and tax authorities, it was found that the VIES system did not provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of tax entities in all cases.
For example:
- although at the request of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the VIES system confirmed the validity of the registration of the tax entity at 4. The O_MCTL message was subsequently generated due to the termination of the registration of the payer in this quarter.
The investigation revealed that the termination of the marketing authorisation did not take place until Day 1. 1st 2005;
- The SAO SR also found that 6 tax subjects filed SHs in which the incorrect TIN was stated, but the O_MCTL reports did not contain these TINs.
In Slovakia, the submitted SH is transferred to the tax authorities in electronic form and the data from it is sent to the DR CLO.
After subsequent processing of these data in the VIES system, the DR CLO sends to the relevant tax authorities so-called breakdowns of errors in the SH filed by tax entities for the respective quarters.
The SAO SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH to 26. 7th 2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the inspection) and at 2. 2nd 2006 (i.e. data processed after completion of the inspection).
The following table provides a comparison of the data.
It can be seen from the above data that the SAO SR audit had an impact not only on the decrease in the number of SHs with erroneous TIN (on average by 199 SHs per quarter), but also on the decrease in the number of uncorrected errors in SH (on average by 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intra-community supplies stated by the payer in the respective DAP lines is compared with the value of intra-community supplies stated by the payer in the quarterly SH.
ADIS automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should check the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the obtained data when determining the tax liability.
The SAO of the Czech Republic found that the audited financial authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
In these cases, the total difference between the values stated in the SH and DAP amounted to CZK 537,231,000.
From 3. In the quarter of 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values stated in the SH and DAP in the amount of up to 0.5% of the total value of intra-Community supplies according to the SH as a match and to set it in the ADIS system.
In the case of payers with a large volume of intra-Community supplies per quarter, 0.5% of the value represents a not insignificant amount, therefore the tax administrators should not set the correspondence of SH and DAP in these cases without clarifying the causes of the differences.
For example, the tax administrator set a consensus in case of a value difference of CZK 1,561,000 without verification.
Examination of differences in the Czech Republic and Slovakia was complicated by the fact that SH for each calendar quarter was filed by payers within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
In the case of payers with a monthly tax period at the time of filing the DAP for the first two months of the calendar quarter, the tax administrators could not compare the values of intra-Community supplies specified in these DAPs with the values according to the SH.
In these cases, the tax administrators became aware of any discrepancy between the data in the DAP and the SH only at the time when the tax liability or excessive deduction of VAT was assessed, or. returned.
5.1.2 Intra-Community acquisition
The VIES system provides, inter alia, information on the values of intra-Community transactions carried out within EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, delivered data from SH submitted by payers from other EU Member States (delivered L1QD) are processed by the MF CLO.
During processing, the data are converted with the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the respective period and then compared with the value of the acquisition stated by the Czech payers in the DAP for the respective quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods reported by the payer in the DAP should be between the minimum and maximum converted value of L1QD (values L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in the DAP is lower than the L1min value, an authentication command is generated for payers with the most significant discrepancies.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a warning to problematic tax subjects and are handed over to the locally competent tax authorities, which must investigate the data transmitted.
The number of verification orders concerning audited financial authorities in the Czech Republic is given in the following table.
The SAO, the Czech Republic found that in 33 cases the audited financial authorities did not examine discrepancies in the values of intra-community acquisitions referred to in the delivered verification orders.
The total difference between the values stated in the SH of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers in these cases was at least CZK 148,319,000.
The SAO, the Czech Republic selected for audit 533 files of tax entities, for which the audited financial authorities received an order for verification from the Ministry of Finance CLO.
The audit found the following most common causes of differences between the values stated in the DAP of the purchaser and in the SH of the supplier: on the side of the purchaser (Czech payer) in 263 cases the purchaser did not indicate the acquisition of goods in the regular DAP, in 93 cases the payer declared the acquisition of goods in a different tax period than in which he was obliged to declare the tax, in 6 cases the purchaser stated the value of the goods in the wrong DAP line, on the side of the supplier (payer, from the EU) in 88 cases the payers from the EU entered the value of the Czech goods into their SH in other cases. 5. 2004, in 5 cases suppliers included in the SH the value of advances received.
On the part of payers from the Slovak Republic, the erroneous inclusion of the value of services provided in the SS occurred most frequently.
54 such cases were found at audited financial offices.
For example, during the investigation of the verification order, it was found that the difference worth CZK 10,974,000 arose from the fact that the Slovak payer entered the SH for 1. quarter 2005 provision of services (construction works and delivery of goods including assembly in the Czech Republic).
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of received advances in the SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payers reported received advances from Czech payers in the SH, as a result of which an order to verify the difference in the amount of CZK 3,580,000 was generated.
Orders to verify the goods acquired are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where the data from the SH subsequently changes in the EU Member States, such as a change in the purchaser of goods in the Czech Republic or an increased value of the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new verification orders are not generated.
Since the VIES system does not automatically warn of these changes, the locally competent tax administrator of the person acquiring the goods may not, without any other incentive, become aware of the relevant facts for the correct determination of the tax liability of the acquired goods and there is a strong likelihood of VAT evasion.
The SAO audit of the Czech Republic revealed that this situation occurred e.g. in the following cases:
The Slovak payer said in SH for 2. the value of the delivery of goods for the Czech payer in the amount of 1,504 thousand Sk.
On 1. 2nd In 2005, the local tax office sent a request for information to the Czech payer in Slovakia because the Czech payer admitted the acquisition of goods in the amount of CZK 425,000 only.
As a result of the tax proceedings, the Slovak payer filed on 1. 3rd 2005 additional SH, in which he corrected the data on the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic by reducing the value of the delivery for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538 thousand Sk and by increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from 194 thousand Sk to the value of 1,160 thousand Sk.
Four Slovak payers said in their SH for 2. quarter 2004 intra-community delivery to payers from the Czech Republic in the total amount of 10 240 thousand Sk (i.e. CZK 8,183 thousand).
However, Czech purchasers did not report intra-community acquisitions in the DAP.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer who was not mentioned in the SH filed by Slovak payers.
Over the course of 1. quarter 2005 increased Slovak payers in additional SH concerning 2. the value of intra-community supplies for this Czech payer by a total of 10 240 thousand Sk.
In view of the above, the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the accuracy of the data in the submitted DAP for 2. quarter 2004, even though the actual purchaser failed to comply with the obligation to declare an intra-Community acquisition for that quarter.
The SAO, CR found that on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the above-mentioned Czech payer was additionally charged VAT for the tax periods 5 and 6/2004 in the amount of CZK 3,640,000 and 3. quarter 2004 in the amount of 3 305 thousand CZK from the acquired goods in these periods.
It is clear from the above that tax administrations had to examine in tax proceedings not only differences caused by errors in the DAP of the purchaser, but also differences caused by different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and acquisitions in individual EU Member States.
Unification of the conditions for reporting these data would lead to more effective control activities of tax administrators.
Acquisition of goods in Slovakia
In SR, the APV DIS system makes it possible to compare the data on the value of acquired goods obtained through the VIES system from other EU Member States with the data entered in the DAP of Slovak purchasers.
The method by which the data is compared is called the "MIN-MAX method".
This method is used to convert the values of the delivery of goods shown in the SH of payers from other EU Member States at the minimum and maximum exchange rates for the relevant quarter.
A MIN-MAX interval is created, which is used for comparison with the acquisition values given in the DAP of Slovak payers.
DR CLO sends the tax administrators information on the values of intra-Community acquisitions specified in the DAP and the values of supplies from the EU in the VIES system.
The tax administrator will decide for which persons registered for VAT the difference will be checked, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
On the basis of the data provided by DR CLO, the SAO selected 57 files of Slovak purchasers of goods for audit at the audited tax offices, of which 25 payers purchased goods from the Czech Republic, where the highest differences between the acquisition values obtained from the VIES system and the values declared in the DAP were found.
The audit carried out by the SAO SR confirmed the fact that the tax administrators did not thoroughly verify the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and thus did not verify the correctness of the data contained in the DAP of Slovak purchasers.
As part of the audit, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations of specific tax entities.
During the audit of the SAO of the Slovak Republic at tax offices, 31 local investigations were completed.
For Slovak companies, where the VIES system showed significant differences in MIN-MAX values when acquiring goods from EU Member States, the following facts were found:
At the DAP in 4. 2004 quarter, the Slovak payer did not state the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The tax office found that a company from the Czech Republic reported 4. quarter 2004 by mistake the VAT number of this payer, while the goods worth CZK 19,184,000 were actually delivered to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, the Slovak company had 4. quarter 2004 to acquire goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria in the value of MIN 682 692 thousand Sk and MAX 715 105 thousand Sk.
This company submitted DAP for the given periods in which it stated the value of acquisitions of goods from the EU of only 480 599 thousand Sk.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation and found that the tax subject purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP did not indicate intra-Community deliveries according to the date of issue of the invoices, but according to the date of delivery.
Due to further irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU countries, the tax administrator will ask for the value of the delivered goods to be checked by means of SCAC forms.
Acquisition of goods from EU Member States at 4. quarter 2004 the Slovak payer did not mention in the DAP.
According to the VIES system, this payer should have purchased goods with a value of MIN 11 286 thousand Sk and MAX 11 845 thousand Sk.
The tax office carried out a local investigation, which showed that the tax subject at 4. did not procure any goods from EU Member States in the quarter of 2004.
The SAO recommended the tax office to request verification of the delivery of goods from EU Member States using the SCAC form.
The VIES system reported the delivery of goods for the Slovak customer in the value of MIN 557 thousand Sk and MAX 565 thousand Sk.
In the DAP for the tax period from 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not declare any acquisition of goods.
A local investigation by the tax administrator found that the tax subject received on 10. 12. 2004 from a supplier from the Czech Republic invoice for materials consumed during the repair of a hydraulic loader.
The SAO recommended a tax audit of the payer.
During the audit of the SAO of the Slovak Republic in 16 cases, the tax authorities did not complete the local investigation.
In 10 cases, the SAO asked tax administrators to carry out a tax audit of tax subjects.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax inspections shall be submitted by the tax authorities to the SAO SR after they have been carried out.
Examples were:
The Slovak purchaser did not indicate in the DAP for 4. quarter 2004 acquisition of goods from EU member states and did not declare any tax for the tax period 10 to 12/2004 and claimed a refund of excess VAT deduction in the total amount of 1,236 thousand Sk.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation, which showed that the tax subject acquired goods from the Czech Republic worth EUR 683,000 (approximately SKK 27,080,000).
These goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to the customs office in Čiernej nad Tisou, from where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak payer issued an invoice for EUR 683 thousand for customers in the Russian Federation, which he did not mention in the submitted DAP.
The tax administrator carries out a tax inspection of the tax subject.
The difference between the acquisition data shown in the Slovak payer's DAP for 3. quarter 2004 to 1. The total amount of deliveries reported by payers from EU Member States in individual quarters was 4 800 thousand Sk.
The tax office found that the tax subject purchased goods from suppliers from the Czech Republic and Belgium and subsequently sold these goods to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by single export declarations.
The acquisition of the goods in the DAP was not stated by the tax subject, according to the statement of the company's manager, the goods in transit were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine.
The tax subject did not submit any VAT records during the on-the-spot investigation.
A tax audit has been initiated on the payer.
5.2 International information exchange L3
The exchange of information at L3 level is initiated by locally competent tax administrators, who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "ŽOI') or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as "SPI') relating to a particular tax entity or transaction via the MF CLO, respectively.
DR CLO to another EU Member State. The aim of the LI is, for example, to prove the implementation of a given transaction within the framework of intra-Community performance, to verify a certain VAT number, etc.
In the case of SPI, it is a communication of information important for tax administrators in another EU Member State.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum time limit for replying to the RES was set out in Art. 8 of this Regulation for 3 months.
The conditions governing the admissibility of applications are laid down in Decision of the Commission of the European Communities of 15. 11th 2004, which stipulates that, unless otherwise agreed by the Participating States, the SPA must cover commercial transactions of at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
Where the BOI relates to a commercial transaction with a value of less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may refuse to reply in view of its workload.
The procedure of the tax administration of the Czech Republic, including the indication of internal time limits set for processing at individual organizational levels, illustrates the following scheme.
In Slovakia, the deadline for the processing of the LI by the tax authorities was set at 2 months so that the three-month deadline under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 could be met.
MF CLO received from the Slovak Republic from 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6th 2005 a total of 29 ZOIs and 3 SPIs.
Of the 29 RES received, 26 (i.e. 89,7 %) dealt with within the deadline of 3 months and 3 (i.e. 10.3%) were discharged after this deadline.
In the same period received DR CLO from the Czech Republic a total of 71 ŽOI and 7 SPI.
Of the 71 RES received, 64 (i.e. 90,1%) completed within the deadline of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) were dealt with after this deadline (for the other 2 cases it was not possible to determine the processing deadline from the materials transmitted).
The following graph contains more detailed data on the time of processing of LIs received by MF CLO or DR CLO.
The following table contains the reasons for sending the RES, as set out on the SCAC forms.
Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation, compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT and the use of the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States were examined, especially when controlling the exercise of the right to VAT exemption.
International cooperation made it possible to examine selected intra-Community transactions carried out between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Examination of selected transactions revealed that, on the basis of an international exchange of information, the tax administrations of both countries detected cases of companies carrying out fictitious intra-Community commercial transactions in order to obtain excessive VAT deductions, as well as cases where purchasers did not declare VAT on the correct amount of goods received.
The audit also revealed differences in the processing and use of VIES data by tax administrations of both countries.
The audit also pointed to problems caused by different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and acquisitions of goods in individual EU Member States.
Harmonising the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would make the control activities of the tax administrations of individual Member States more effective.
An examination of the procedures of the tax or tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of the VIES system revealed that the tax or tax authorities did not make sufficient use of all possibilities of the VIES system and the relevant legal authorisations.
Furthermore, it was found that VIES did not provide up-to-date information in all cases on the supply of goods and on the validity of VAT registration of tax subjects.
The SAO SR compared data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SA, processed before the start of the audit, with data processed after completion of the audit.
It was clear from the comparison of these data that the SAO SR audit had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with incorrectly stated VAT numbers, but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in SH.
In case of discrepancies in the reported data, the SAO SR asked the tax authorities to carry out local investigations or to carry out tax audits.
The SAO, the Czech Republic did not have such a possibility under the current legislation in the Czech Republic.
The findings of the audit showed that VIES provided tax administrations with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
Given that there is still scope for tax evasion in this area, increased attention needs to be paid to intra-Community transactions when administering VAT.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Chairman of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This information material provides an overview of the course and results of parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which focused on the area of value added tax and excise duties.
Cooperation between the SAIs of both countries was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement on control activities concluded in February 2004.
The topic of parallel control actions was chosen with regard to the fact that indirect taxes significantly contribute to the revenues of the state budgets of both countries.
The structure of value added tax, which allows the refund of excess deduction, provides scope for tax fraud or evasion.
High rates of excise duties, in particular on tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean high profits for those who escape taxation through the illegal sale of these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Due to the need to address this issue comprehensively throughout the European Union, the VAT Working Group was created by the supreme audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union, in whose activities the supreme audit authorities of both countries are actively involved.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but in particular in the joint effort to identify problem areas of indirect tax administration in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion.
The acquired experience and knowledge will be used in the planned inspections of indirect taxes, aimed primarily at the involvement of the tax administrations of both countries in the VIES system, which allows the control of the movement of goods between the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the audit of the administration of value added tax and excise duties for the years 2002 and 2003
1st Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duties
(SK) Control of the tax administrator's procedure for administering, controlling and enforcing value added tax and excise taxes
On 11.2. 2004 The Agreement on Cooperation in Audit Activities between the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO SR) was concluded. The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel auditing operations "Value Added Tax and Excise Tax," included in the 2004 Audit Plan of the SAO under No. 04/07 and "Inspection of the Administrator's Procedure in Administration, Control and Recovery of Taxes from Added Value and Consumption Taxes," included in the Audit Plan of the SAO of the Slovak Republic under No. 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted in exchanging information to the extent provided for in the contract concluded and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
In the contract, both parties undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the customs administration database and from the files of tax entities maintained by the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and the tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the parties could not obtain when controlling the application of value added tax and excise duties on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the respective State.
The audits were carried out in parallel from January to August 2004.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the audit was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of South Bohemia, Northeast Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The audited bodies were the General Directorate of Customs and 12 selected financial authorities: Financial Authority for Prague 1, Financial Authority for Prague 3, Financial Authority in České Budějovice, Financial Authority in Frýdek-Místek, Financial Authority in Hodonín, Financial Authority in Jihlava, Financial Authority in Kostelec nad Orlicí, Financial Authority in Kroměříž, Financial Authority in Písek, Financial Authority in Rožnov pod Radhoštěm, Financial Authority in Ústí nad Orlicí, Financial Authority in Velké Meziříčí.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "SR") was carried out by the Section of Tax and Customs Administration of the SAO SR in cooperation with the Expositions of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 10 selected tax offices:
Tax Office Bratislava before selected tax entities, Tax Office Bratislava III, Tax Office Trnava, Tax Office Pú-chov, Tax Office Banská Bystrica I, Tax Office Liptovský Mikuláš, Tax Office Žilina I, Tax Office Žilina II, Tax Office Košice I and Tax Office Košice IV.
Objective of control
The aim of the auditing activities was to examine the fulfilment of the obligations of financial or tax authorities and customs offices in the administration of value added tax and excise taxes with a focus on the collection of these taxes in the import and export of goods and services.
The aim of the international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic and their subsequent verification in tax returns at the relevant financial or tax authorities.
The audited period covered the years 2002 and 2003.
2nd Recap of control results
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
Within the framework of international cooperation, the SAO handed over 22,206 items of the Uniform Declarations on Imports and Exports of Goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia from the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, while the SAO handed over 30,221 items of the JCD from the Customs Database of the Slovak Republic.
A comparison of selected JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic was performed.
Of the 5,883 selected JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic, a total of 43% of the related JCD items were assigned.
Of the 12 343 selected JCD entries from the SR Customs database, a total of 26% of the related JCD entries were attributed.
On the basis of the unassigned items of the JCD, a selection of files of tax entities was carried out at the tax or tax authorities, where the reported imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Based on the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia and the financial or tax authorities, the implementation of reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia was verified on the territory of the other state.
The SAO and the SAO of Slovakia carried out a joint pilot inspection at the Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma border crossing, during which both parties cooperated closely in verifying the correctness of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The audit did not detect any deficiencies in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation made it possible to examine trade transactions carried out between trading partners from both countries and highlighted shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of control results
In the area of international cooperation, the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic focused on imports and exports of alcohol and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, or other goods.
On the basis of an audit of the files of tax entities at selected tax or tax authorities, the SAO requested verification of the implementation of exports of goods declared for 40 JCDs with a total statistical value of CZK 15,301,093 and the SAO requested verification of exports with a statistical value of CZK 56,989.
The SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic found the following facts:
- trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic,
- errors in data entry in customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports/exports,
- for some exports from the Czech Republic, there was no evidence of corresponding imports to Slovakia.
In such cases, there are reasonable grounds for suspecting fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of improperly claiming deductions of value added tax,
- tax entities failed to comply with certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- Weaknesses have been identified in the activities of the tax authorities in administering value added tax and excise duties and in their interaction with customs authorities.
In the area of value added tax and excise duties, attention will continue to be paid to international trade in order to effectively minimise tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the activities of tax administrators when administering value added tax.
Effective control of excise duties is based on control of the circulation of documents, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information during import and export of goods.
3rd Description of the situation in the field of value added tax and excise duties
Value Added Tax
Value added tax ("VAT") was levied by the tax or tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out within the country and by the customs authorities on the importation of goods.
Tax revenues were determined at the tax or tax authorities by the difference between the collected own tax liability and the refunded excess VAT deductions.
The VAT revenue at the customs offices was determined by the amount of tax collected by them.
In accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, the tax collected by the customs authorities was reflected in the tax deductions applied to the tax or tax authorities.
For most tax authorities, the excess VAT deductions exceeded the tax liability.
VAT is one of the key taxes in terms of state budget revenues, as it accounted for approximately 31% of the tax revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic in 2003 and approximately 42% of the tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic.
Total VAT collection in the Czech Republic reached CZK 162.9 billion in 2003. CZK.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities collected a total of EUR 394.3 billion in VAT. CZK and refunded excess VAT deductions totalled CZK 231.4 billion. CZK.
Total VAT collection in Slovakia amounted to EUR 83.8 billion in 2003. The Sk.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities collected EUR 187.0 billion in VAT. Sk and refunded excess VAT deductions totalled CZK 103.2 billion The Sk.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "SpD") was carried out by the relevant tax or tax authorities and, when importing products subject to the SpD, by customs authorities.
The share of SpD in tax revenues of the state budget in the Czech Republic was approximately 16% in 2003 and approximately 19% in Slovakia.
The total collection of SpD collected in the Czech Republic by the financial and customs authorities in 2003 amounted to CZK 85.6 billion. CZK and reached CZK 38.0 billion in Slovakia. The Sk.
4th Progress of control action
Cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR took place in two stages.
In the first stage, a comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia was carried out; in the second stage, the results of this comparison were used in the mutual verification of the implementation of selected trade transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and in inspections carried out on the territory of both countries.
4.1.
Preparation of control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel audits of VAT and SpD was presented at a working meeting of representatives of the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic in April 2003.
In November 2003, a coordination meeting took place at which, inter alia, a selection of commodities was agreed - types of goods which posed a significant risk in complying with customs and tax legislation: - alcohol and spirits, tariff headings 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, tariff headings 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff headings 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, tariff subheadings 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
Both parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out: a) from unassigned items determined by comparing exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, b) from entities carrying out imports and exports on a regular or one-off basis in large volumes, c) on the basis of findings from inspections carried out by selected financial and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
