In the first stage, the mechanism of mutual allocation of JCD items registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia was tested on a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002.
Subsequently, the part of exports from the Czech Republic was compared with imports to Slovakia in 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:
- 2207 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% vol. or more; ethyl alcohol and other spirits, denatured, of any strength,
- 2208 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80% vol. ; spirits, liqueurs and other spirituous beverages,
- 2401 Unmanufactured tobacco; tobacco refuse,
- 2402 Cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes, of tobacco or of tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 Other manufactured tobacco and tobacco substitutes; homogenised or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and essences,
- 8525 20 91 Transmission apparatus incorporating reception apparatus:
- 8525 20 99 Transmission apparatus incorporating reception apparatus:
- 8529 90 40 Parts suitable for use solely or principally with the apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling in subheadings 8525 10 50, 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
JCD items from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia were mutually assigned on the basis of the conformity of individual paragraphs of the JCD (e.g. invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration number of the vehicle transporting freight, date of crossing the state border, customs tariff item, etc.). ).
The results of the comparison are shown in the following tables and charts.
The mutual allocation of individual imports and exports was hampered, among other things, by the fact that trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides.
For example, exports from the Czech Republic, declared on one export JCD, were declared on the territory of the Slovak Republic on several import JCDs, or the export JCD had a different number of items from the import JCD.
Other factors that influenced the success of the assignment were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia, as well as the time shift between the registration of exports in the customs database of one country and the registration of corresponding imports in the customs database of the other country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples at audited financial and tax authorities.
Priority was given to certain tax entities that carried out imports or exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, which could not be identified in both databases.
Furthermore, for the verification of business transactions reported in the VAT tax returns, some tax entities were selected for which data on imports or exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia were found in both databases.
4.3. Pilot inspection at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma
The border customs crossing for the performance of pilot control was selected on the basis of a joint analysis of unassigned JCD items in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
On the basis of a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia, the use of checklists has been introduced at border customs crossings between the Czech Republic and Slovakia since 1 June 1998.
The aim of this measure was to eliminate, as far as possible, customs and tax evasion, to ensure an overview of the movement of means of transport of goods of a commercial character in the customs area and to create conditions for mutual comparison of customs records.
A joint pilot inspection was carried out on 8. 3rd 2004 to 26. 3rd 2004 and aimed at verifying this customs control system.
Procedure for the use of check sheets at the border crossing point Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma:
1) Weighing the Audi A6, issuing the checklist and handing it over to the driver.
2) Parking in the marked sector in the parking lot.
Customs clearance in the clearance hall by the Police of the Czech Republic, the Police of the Slovak Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic.
The check-in was confirmed by the various components by stamping the control sheet.
(3) Presentation of the vehicle in the physical inspection area.
Presentation of the inspection sheet, JCD, or other documents to the customs administration employee - checking the execution of all prescribed acts and documents.
Physical checks by the relevant services.
Release of the vehicle from the customs area.
Attention: When importing goods into the Czech Republic, the vehicle was weighed directly by employees of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
When importing goods into Slovakia, the vehicle was weighed by employees of an authorized legal entity.
The vehicles were recorded in computer records after weighing.

Exports from Slovakia to the Czech Republic

The remaining 44 cases were identified in their records by employees of the border customs crossing Drietoma and the export of goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic was confirmed.
The SAO and SAO SR did not detect any deficiencies in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods in 2002 at the Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma border crossing.
4.4. Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
Within the framework of international cooperation, the implementation of imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia was verified on the basis of customs administrations and financial or tax authorities in the territory of the other country.
For selected tax subjects, the following were verified:
- whether the submitted JCDs were registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia,
- fulfilment of legal conditions for application of VAT deduction on import, refund of excess VAT deduction and application of VAT exemption on export.
The verification of commercial transactions revealed:
1st The SAO SR requested verification of the implementation of alcohol exports with a statistical value of 56,989 Sk.
The SAO identified the corresponding import in the customs database of the Czech Republic with a statistical value of CZK 42,624.
2nd The company engaged in the import and export of photographic equipment and accessories applied an excess VAT deduction of CZK 3,740,664 in the VAT return for the month of December 2002.
In order to audit reported exports from the Czech Republic, the SAO selected 3 JCDs (16 items) with a statistical value of CZK 1,274,822.
The SAO SR identified 3 corresponding import JCDs (17 items) with a statistical value of 1 724 321 Sk.
The VAT was paid in Slovakia to the competent customs office.
3rd In 2002, the company, which mainly traded in optical instruments, claimed a total excess VAT deduction of CZK 4 1 36 000 higher than the tax liability.
To verify the reported business activity, the SAO selected export JCD (32 items) with a statistical value of CZK 7,154,124.
The SAO SR found that this JCD corresponds to import JCD (12 items) with a statistical value of 9,653,827 Sk.
The VAT was paid in Slovakia to the competent customs office.
4th A company engaged, inter alia, in the purchase of goods for resale and sale did not record any export of goods in the VAT returns submitted in 2002 and 2003.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the statistical value of goods exports totalled CZK 3,439,888 in 2002.
Based on these facts, the SAO selected 5 export JCDs (5 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 669,839.
The SAO SR identified 5 corresponding import JCDs (5 items) with a statistical value of 1,012,656 Sk.
The audit of the SAO SR at the relevant tax office proved the realization of the declared imports and the payment of VAT.
5. In 2002, the company, whose subject of business was, inter alia, the purchase of goods for resale and the sale, manufacture, installation and repair of electrical machinery and appliances, reported in its VAT returns the export of goods worth CZK 12,966,706.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the total value of exports amounted to CZK 14,474,381 in 2002.
The SAO submitted 17 export JCDs (59 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,975,122.
The SAO SR identified in the customs database SR 13 JCDs (50 items) with a statistical value of 3 621 370 Sk.
In the Slovak customs database, it was not possible to identify the corresponding import JCD for 4 export JCDs (9 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 399,776.
The competent tax office in Slovakia verified these imports with the tax entity.
The tax entity, listed on the JCD as an importer to Slovakia, stated in the minutes of the local investigation that it had not made imports declared on the Czech export JCDs.
The SAO therefore asked the local tax authority to carry out a tax audit of VAT and corporate income tax for the tax years 2002 and 2003.
6th According to the Czech Customs Database, the company engaged in the import and sale of cigarettes exported tobacco labels with a statistical value of CZK 7,338,199 in 2002 and CZK 12,228,545 in 2003.
In the VAT returns, the company did not report any exports in 2002 and 2003.
The SAO selected for verification 5 export JCDs (5 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,471,598.
For 4 export JCDs (4 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,246,860, the SAO SR identified in the customs database SR 7 JCDs (7 items) with a statistical value of Sk 2,919,514.
It was not possible to assign the corresponding import to the export JCD (1 item) with a statistical value of CZK 224,738 in the Slovak customs database.
7th The software company did not declare exports of goods in the VAT returns for 2002 and 2003.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, the statistical value of goods exports in 2002 and 2003 totalled CZK 1,630,198.
The SAO selected 9 JCDs (9 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 755,588.
In the customs database of the Slovak Republic, the SAO of the Slovak Republic identified 8 JCDs (8 items) with a statistical value of 915 601 Sk.
It was not possible to assign the corresponding import to the export JCD (1 item) with a statistical value of 68 286 CZK in the Slovak customs database.
In these cases, it was not possible to identify in the Slovak customs database the corresponding imports for 6 JCDs with a statistical value of CZK 692,800.
Of which:
- for 2 export JCDs from the customs database of the Czech Republic with a statistical value of CZK 293,024, the corresponding import JCD could not be identified in the customs database of the Slovak Republic (see points 6 and 7).
Due to some error in entering data into the customs database, it was not possible to identify some registered imports, e.g. in cases where the importer's name was missing or there was an error in the tax identification number (TIN).
Therefore, it cannot be established with certainty that these exports were not made.
- for 4 export JCDs from the customs database of the Czech Republic, imports corresponding to exports from the Czech Republic to Slovakia with a statistical value of CZK 399,776 were not proven (see point 5).
In such cases, there is reason to suspect the fictitious export of goods for the purpose of improperly claiming a VAT deduction.
5. Control of imports and exports of goods and services within the control of selected financial or tax authorities
5.1. Control sample
In order to examine the fulfilment of the obligations of tax entities in the import and export of goods and services and to evaluate the level of cooperation between financial and customs authorities, the files of tax entities were selected at the audited financial and tax authorities according to the following criteria:
1. Tax subjects were selected from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia: a) with the highest volume of imports, b) with the highest amount of VAT charged, c) with the highest volume of exports,
2. tax entities were selected from the records of the tax or tax authorities according to the amount of: a) applied VAT deductions on import, b) applied excessive VAT deductions, c) claim for SpD refund, d) applied VAT exemption on export,
3. taxable persons subject to a tax audit.
Sampling was carried out irrespective of the country of destination with a focus on risky commodities.
5.2. Control findings in the Czech Republic
An overview of imports into the Czech Republic and exports from the Czech Republic of risky commodities in 2002 and 2003 is given in the following table:
5.2.1. Control of selected sample at tax offices
At the audited financial offices, the SAO focused mainly on:
- the procedure of the tax authorities for verifying the correctness of the VAT declared,
- cooperation between the tax authorities and the customs administration,
- comparison of data from the customs database with the JCD database at tax offices with a focus on comparing the declared value, applying the correct VAT rate following the customs classification of goods or services, or comparison of data on JCD and attached invoices with data in the customs database,
- comparison of data from VAT returns on transactions made and received from abroad with data in the JCD database at tax offices or in the customs database,
- the method of verifying the right to VAT exemption when exporting goods or services abroad,
- a comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services declared in VAT returns with data from the customs database.
The JCD database at the tax offices contained only records of those imports and exports for which tax entities were obliged to declare imports or exports in the tax return.
The audited tax authorities scrutinized the files of tax entities that reported imports in the total amount of CZK 60,396,379 thousand and the corresponding VAT in the total amount of CZK 12,644,052 thousand in VAT returns in 2002 and 2003.
Furthermore, the files of tax entities reporting exports totalling CZK 47,323,111,000 in the tax returns for 2002 and 2003 were scrutinized.
According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the tax entities for which imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia were examined carried out in 2002 and 2003 imports into the Czech Republic from Slovakia with a total VAT base of CZK 3,759,352,000, VAT of CZK 767,607,000 and exports from the Czech Republic to Slovakia with a total statistical value of CZK 1,989,090,000.
The observed differences between records in the JCD database at financial offices and in the customs database of the Czech Republic were examined as follows:
- JCD items that were missing from the customs database of the Czech Republic were requested directly from the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic,
- for JCD items that were missing from the IRS database, it was verified that they were not cancelled documents,
- for JCD items where different values were found between the customs database of the Czech Republic and the database of financial authorities, the relevant JCD was requested from the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic in written form, including the attached invoices.
The audit revealed that the JCD database at financial offices did not contain, for example, records of import JCDs with a total VAT value of CZK 3,622,000 and records of export JCDs with a total statistical value of CZK 9,359,000.
5.2.1.1. Differences found
A comparison of the JCD database at the tax authorities and the cumulative tax liabilities for 2002 and 2003 in the VAT tax returns of a selected sample of tax subjects revealed the following differences:
Differences in values were mainly due to:
- The time lag between the realisation of imports and the exercise of the right to deduct VAT charged on the importation of goods.
The tax subject could exercise the right of deduction for the importation of goods within 3 years of the end of the tax period in which the goods were placed under the relevant procedure or, in the case of the temporary importation procedure, within 3 years of the end of the tax period in which the procedure ended.
- Time difference between the realization of the export and the moment when the tax subject received the JCD.
The tax subject was obliged to include data on realized exports exempt from the obligation to apply output tax in the VAT tax return at the earliest for the tax period in which the goods left the country, if he also had a tax document, which was JCD.
- Failure of taxpayers to comply with their obligations when reporting imports and exports in VAT returns.
In some cases, tax subjects did not provide correct data on imports and exports in VAT returns.
As tax subjects did not have to attach lists of JCDs to the submitted VAT returns, the control of the right to deduct VAT or the exemption from VAT by the tax authorities was made more difficult.
5.2.2. Interaction between financial and customs authorities
During the audited period, import or export duties and VAT were reimbursed or remitted on the basis of customs decisions.
Tax subjects were required by law to reduce the previously claimed right to deduct VAT by the amount of tax refunded by the customs office in the tax return for the period in which the tax was refunded.
No legislation provided for the sending of information on changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT from customs offices to tax offices.
Some audited tax offices received this information, but irregularly or with significant time delays and only from some customs offices.
One audited tax office did not receive this information at all.
If the tax office did not receive information about changes in the amount of duty and VAT directly from the customs office, it did not have the data necessary to check the fulfilment of the legal obligation of tax entities.
In 2002, the customs authorities refunded VAT in the amount of more than CZK 319 million and in 2003 in the amount of more than CZK 398 million.
The results of the audit pointed to persistent shortcomings in the activities of tax administrators, some systemic errors in the cooperation of tax authorities with customs authorities and non-fulfilment of some obligations of payers filing VAT and SpD tax returns.
Deficiencies in the administration of VAT and SpD were found in particular in the following areas:
a) in the event of cancellation of VAT registrations, the fulfilment of the obligation of payers to pay VAT on the registered business assets, or which should have been registered on the date of cancellation of the registration, in respect of which the payer applied the tax deduction, was verified only sporadically,
(b) the tax authorities did not consistently make use of the possibility of carrying out a tax audit or on-the-spot investigation.
This led in some cases to insufficient verification of the right to deduct VAT,
c) official records and minutes of the oral hearing did not contain all the necessary data demonstrating the legitimacy of the excessive VAT deductions applied,
(d) the tax authorities have not sufficiently verified the imports and exports declared in the VAT returns.
5.3. Control findings in Slovakia
5.3.1. Control of selected sample at tax offices
For a selected sample, the SAO verified or the tax office carried out a tax audit for the tax years 2002 and 2003.
After analyzing the submitted tax returns and applications for tax refunds at selected tax entities, the SAO SR asked the tax office to secure the relevant JCDs documenting import and export, invoices and tax payment documents.
Subsequently, the SAO scrutinized whether the submitted JCDs registered in the customs database of imports and exports and the fulfilment of decisive facts and legal conditions in the application of the input tax deduction in respect of imports, in the refund of excess VAT deduction, in the application of export tax exemption and in the refund of SpD.
At 10 audited tax offices, the SAO verified selected cases of imports and exports of goods between the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the structure according to the number of JCD items and the sum of statistical values given in the following table.
In total, imports with a statistical value of 856.2 million Sk were audited, which represents 5.11% of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic into SROV.
Exports of selected commodities were audited in the total statistical value of 176 million Sk, which represents 6.87% of the total value of exports of selected commodities from Slovakia to the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, 618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white technology, packaging technology and software) from EU countries to Slovakia were audited with a total statistical value of 532.8 million Sk.
5.3.2. Interaction between tax and customs authorities
The SAO SR found discrepancies between the data registered in the Slovak customs database and the data reported in specific VAT tax returns, e.g.:
- 2 tax subjects (natural persons) declared in their tax returns imports of goods with a total value of SKK 1 589 261, on the basis of which they claimed a refund of excess VAT deductions.
During local investigations carried out on the initiative of the SAO SR, tax entities were unable to prove to the tax office the legitimacy of applying input tax with relevant documents on importation and VAT payment,
- tax entity (s.r. (o.) in the tax return for the tax period January 2003 declared the received taxable supply in the value of SKU 77 167 576, the export of goods in the value of SKU 18 006 041 and claimed an excess VAT deduction in the amount of SKU 17 157 101.
It is apparent from the VAT returns submitted for 2003 that the difference between the volume of purchases and exports, amounting to SKU 59 161 535, which arose in January 2003, was not corrected during the whole of 2003.
In the above-mentioned cases, the SAO asked the relevant tax authorities to carry out a tax audit of the excessive VAT deductions applied.
- in another case, the tax entity (s.r. (o.) for the tax period January to June 2002, declared in the VAT tax returns the export of goods with a total value of SKK 87,199.
Verification in the Slovak customs database revealed that the tax subject carried out an export with a statistical value of 296 747 Sk.
The tax office carried out a number of on-the-spot investigations at the company's headquarters, finding that the company's manager (a UK citizen) had departed and the company had left the rented premises without terminating the lease in August 2002.
At the time of the SAO audit, the tax administrator filed a notice with the criminal authorities on suspicion of committing the crime of non-payment of tax.
Based on the results of the audit at selected tax offices, the SAO of the Slovak Republic states that the biggest problems in the management and control of VAT and SpD occurred mainly in the following areas:
- not making use of the possibility to carry out a VAT tax audit on problematic tax subjects, in particular in cases of application of a high value of excess VAT;
- tax audit reports did not include an inventory of audited documents
- JCD on import and export of goods,
- insufficient verification of declared imports and exports of goods in tax returns,
- lengthy procedures for tax administrations to take decisions, in particular in the context of the assessment procedure, including the loss of the right to impose penalties;
- failure to comply with legal conditions when granting tax deferrals,
- non-compensation of VAT arrears by the refund deadline,
- insufficient use of all forms of security and recovery of tax arrears.
On the basis of the shortcomings detected by the audit, the SAO asked the relevant tax authorities to carry out a tax audit of VAT with a focus on the legitimacy of excessive VAT deductions applied to 14 tax entities.
At all audited tax offices, measures were taken to eliminate the deficiencies detected by the audit, the fulfilment of which will be monitored and audited by the SAO of the Slovak Republic.
6th Conclusion
International cooperation made it possible to examine trade transactions carried out between trading partners from both countries and highlighted shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
The audit also revealed persistent shortcomings in the fulfilment of obligations of VAT and SpD payers, in the activities of tax or tax authorities, in the system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs authorities, which ultimately reduced the effectiveness and efficiency of tax inspections.
The findings also showed that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have at their disposal basic data on imports and exports from the customs database of the Czech Republic as part of the tax information system. In Slovakia, there is no similar system for the transmission of information on imports and exports of goods between customs and tax administrations.
The procedure for verifying the performance of the administration of VAT and SpD was not the same in view of the different legal regulations and conditions in the territory of both States.
The SAO verified the necessary data from information obtained from the Czech Customs Administration and from documents available at audited financial offices. The SAO audited commercial transactions from documents of tax entities requested through tax authorities.
If irregularities were found, he asked the tax authorities to carry out tax inspections.
The parallel audits carried out in the area of VAT and SpD assessed the state of administration of these taxes in the period before accession to the European Union and pointed out the necessity of further cooperation in this area.
Mutual cooperation will be further deepened in the control of the activities of the tax or tax authorities in connection with the adoption of the new VAT Act.
One of the new obligations related to the delivery of goods to other Member States of the European Union is the submission of a so-called summary report.
This declaration must be submitted by all VAT payers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for VAT in another Member State.
Tax administrators are obliged to enter data from summary reports into the VIES (VAT Information Exchange System) system, to which tax administrators from the Member States of the European Union have access.
The tax or tax authorities then have the opportunity to compare these data with the data contained in the submitted VAT tax returns.
This system is also used to verify the validity of the VAT registration number of persons registered for VAT, to verify the validity of the VAT exemption applied when goods are delivered to another Member State and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel audits showed the possibilities of cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR.
The results of these audits will be confronted with the results of the upcoming audits, which will focus, among other things, on the verification of the VIES system, which is supposed to prevent tax evasion in so-called "intra-Community supplies."
Given the importance of VAT and SPD for budgetary revenues, control activities should focus primarily on monitoring and identifying risk areas in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion in indirect taxes.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Report on the results of inspections in asylum facilities in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
State property and funds earmarked for securing the activities of the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior
Control action No. 04/23 - State property and funds earmarked for securing the activities of the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior
Inspection action No. 15/2004 - Inspection of the economy with the property of the state and financial resources intended for the provision of asylum and temporary refuge for foreigners in Slovakia"
1st Introduction
Population migration is one of the phenomena that has a global character and has become an inseparable part of the current development phase of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
In particular, it is caused by the flight of citizens from their country of origin or last permanent residence from persecution, in particular for racial, religious, national, political reasons, as well as from the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
Their aim is to gain asylum and integration into society, especially in some of Europe's advanced democratic countries.
A large group includes foreigners whose reason for migration is unfavourable economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The adoption of the Geneva Agreement of 1951 and the New York Protocol of 1967 relating to the Status of Refugees, by which the governments of the signatory countries undertook to apply them in their foreign-policy orientation, brought about the establishment of specific principles for refugee assistance.
The Czech and Slovak Federal Republics ratified the New York Protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
After the split in 1993, both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic declared their position on the refugee issue by continuing to comply with adopted international documents and confirmed their binding force within the framework of national legislation by means of a legal act.
Both republics have also enshrined the provision of asylum in their constitutional laws.
Parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic focused on the asylum process and related issues, the results of which are contained in the joint final report.
Cooperation between the Supreme Audit Institutions of both countries was implemented on the basis of the "Contract on Cooperation in Audit Activities" (hereinafter referred to as the "Contract") concluded in April 2004.
In the Treaty, both Parties undertook to provide each other with information on the legislation governing asylum procedures in the State of the other Party, selected statistics on the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as information on asylum facilities.
The aim of the parallel control action was to identify the same problem areas and to highlight the consequences for population migration.
Cooperation consisted in harmonising the programme of control actions, exchanging information to the extent provided for by the Treaty and drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the controls.
During the first joint meeting, which took place from 5.4. to 7.4.2004, the same areas of audited issues and control procedures during the preparation of auditing events were determined.
At the second meeting, which took place from 28.6. to 30.6. 2004, the common points for the control action programme were clarified.
During the third joint meeting, which took place during the auditing operation from 8.11. to 10.11.2004, the experience of the ongoing audits was exchanged.
The modalities of the control outputs have been specified and the structure and content of the joint final report, which was drawn up between 14.2. and 17.2. 2005 at the last joint meeting.
The audits were carried out in parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the audit was carried out by auditors from the Department of Defence and Security and selected territorial departments.
The audited bodies were the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as "MoI') and the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as "SUZ').
In the Slovak Republic carried out an inspection of the section of defense, interior and štátnych úradov.
The audited entity was the Migration Office of the Ministry of Interior of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "MÚ").
The audited period covered the years 2001, 2002 and 2003 (hereinafter referred to as the audited period).
In some cases, statistical data covering a longer period of time are also used in the joint report.
2nd Recap of control results
2.1. Assessment of control activities
The subjects of the parallel checks were: - the asylum process, - asylum facilities, - the management of funds and state property, - the internal control system.
The mutual exchange of experience between the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic took place in the phase of preparation and implementation of audit actions.
This exchange allowed for a more thorough evaluation of the submitted documents, to analyse the causes of the identified differences in the security of the asylum process.
In this way, it was possible to focus on the decisive problems affecting the activities of asylum facilities.
Ultimately, this had a positive impact on the quality of the implementation of the control activity.
2.2 Summary of the results of the audit
The harmonisation of the asylum law of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic with the documents of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "EU") was the subject of evaluation reports by the European Commission on the readiness of both countries to join the EU.
Legislation in this area continues to be adopted after the accession of both countries to the EU with a view to further harmonisation with EU law.
The number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants has steadily increased, with a significant increase in applicants in 2001.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security for asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget of both countries is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the length of the asylum procedure until asylum is granted or refused, as well as the state of health of the applicants.
The amount of some levies collected is comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic set up asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of the asylum seekers.
In asylum facilities, asylum seekers are provided with accommodation, food, health care and basic material equipment and sanitary supplies during their stay.
At the same time, courses are organized as part of leisure activities and the conditions for cultural and sporting activities are created for applicants.
Asylum facilities include reception centres and residential centres, and in the Czech Republic also integration centres.
The cost of one day of stay depends on the occupancy and facilities of the centre and is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is broadly stable.
In the Slovak Republic, it is expected to increase by almost 1 000 jobs in the next two years.
The aim is to create the conditions for applicants, whose increasing numbers are expected to continue in the coming years in the context of the application of the Dublin Convention.
In the Czech Republic, the highest part of the approved budget expenditure was spent on the provision of services. Crucial expenditure under this heading was the cost of lodging and boarding applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, the cost of health care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service to protect asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work carried out and insurance premiums also accounted for a significant share of total expenditure.
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the migration policy and asylum process was marked by many budgetary measures addressing legitimate demands related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums, expenditure on materials and services and expenditure on security services accounted for the bulk of current expenditure.
The results of the audit in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic highlighted some similar shortcomings that did not have a major impact on the financial and state property management.
These were shortcomings in particular in the area of the use of state budget funds, contrary to the purpose for which they were designated by the Act on the State Budget, when current expenditures were used to cover actions in the nature of technical appreciation of long-term tangible assets.
The law on accounting in the area of inventory and non-compliance with the chart of accounts was also violated.
In the Czech Republic, minor shortcomings were also found in the handling of state property when it was left to another person without a contract.
Failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in the Land Registry data violated the Land Registry Act and the Waste Act was violated by leaving the waste for disposal to a person who was not authorized to handle the waste.
Furthermore, in the Slovak Republic, weaknesses were found in the provision of disproportionately high advances for the purchase of electricity and natural gas, in public procurement and in the management of state property when its records were not sufficiently secured and the method of liquidating unnecessary assets was not demonstrated.
The internal control system was ensured in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic within the meaning of the generally binding legislation in force governing the method of financial control.
No deficiencies were found in the written documentation submitted.
Despite some shortcomings, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic positively evaluate the progress of SUZ and MÚ in providing services for asylum seekers.
Based on the findings obtained during the audit, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic state that despite a significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years, the respective organizational units of both countries have managed the tasks associated with the care of asylum seekers to an appropriate level.
The evaluation shows that the system is operational and stable.
The results of the audit were discussed with the interested statutory representatives of the relevant state organizational units on both the Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the audit, we recommend that the positive methodological experience from the audit be used in other joint audit actions within the framework of international cooperation of SAIs.
3rd Legislative framework
In both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, asylum law is based on the 1951 Geneva Convention (Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees and the 1967 New York Protocol).
The first legal regulation was implemented by Act No. 498/1990 Coll., on Refugees.
In the Czech Republic it is from 1. 1st 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum and on Amendment to Act No. 83/1991 Coll., on the Police of the Czech Republic.
This Act has been amended five times (by Act No. 2/2002 Coll., Act No. 217/2002 Coll., Act No. 320/2002 Coll., Act No. 519/2002 Coll. and Act No. 222/2003 Coll.).
Two other amendments to Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, are currently in the legislative process and the adoption of other amendments will be tied to European legislation.
At the time of the creation of Act No.325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, the area of asylum was part of the 3rd pillar of the EU and asylum documents were political documents in their binding nature.
Already during the adoption of this law, efforts were made to make it as compatible as possible with EU law.
An important change for asylum policy within the EU was the transfer of asylum issues from the 3rd to the 1st pillar, when the right of asylum became part of Community law from 1 May. 1999 under the Treaty of Amsterdam.
This shift has also necessitated the development of appropriate legislation, i.e. the creation of legal instruments with appropriate legal force.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents has been the subject of regular evaluation reports by the European Commission.
Key Community regulations in the field of asylum were adopted shortly before or after the Czech Republic joined the EU and their transposition period at the time of the Supreme Audit Office audit, the Czech Republic has not yet expired.
Once they have been transposed into Czech law, the Czech Republic will be obliged to notify the European Commission how it has transposed them.
In the Slovak Republic, the procedure of state authorities in the procedure for granting refugee status and determining the obligations of foreigners who have applied for refugee status or who have been granted temporary refuge on the territory of the Slovak Republic was laid down with effect from 1.1.1996 by the Act of the National Council of the Slovak Republic No.
Since 2003, the Refugee Act has been replaced by Act No.480/2002 Coll. on Asylum and on Amendments to Certain Acts, which incorporated the harmonisation of the legislation of the Slovak Republic with Council of Europe Directive 2001/55/EC of 20. 7th 2001 on minimum standards for providing temporary protection in the event of a mass influx of displaced persons and on measures to promote a balance of efforts between Member States in receiving such persons and bearing the resulting consequences.
After two amendments to Act No. 480/2002 Coll., on Asylum, in 2003 and 2004, the third amendment was approved at the beginning of 2005, which means further harmonisation of the law of the Slovak Republic with EU legislation on migration and asylum.
Its important elements are, for example, the establishment of an obligation for asylum seekers to attend a Slovak language basic course during their stay in the integration centre, the appointment of a guardian by the courts for minor foreigners if they are staying on the territory of the Slovak Republic without a legal representative, and the possibility for applicants to enter into an employment relationship under certain circumstances specified in the amendment to the Act.
The harmonisation of the Slovak Republic's law with EU law in the area of migration and asylum process was evaluated in the European Commission's regular reports on preparedness for the Slovak Republic's accession to the EU.
In 2002, the report drew attention to the insufficient staffing capacity of the MoA, which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4th Asylum process
In the Czech Republic, since 1990, matters concerning refugees have been the responsibility of the Ministry of Interior.
Effective from 1. 1st In 1996, the Ministry of Interior established an organizational unit of the state of SUZ. The reason for this was the separation of the performance of the state administration in the area of asylum procedure, which is carried out through the Department of Asylum and Migration Policy of the Ministry of Interior, from the provision of services to asylum seekers.
The task of the SUZ is to provide accommodation, catering, health and other services for the MoI to participants in asylum procedures and asylum seekers.
In the Slovak Republic, the MoA performs decisive tasks in the field of the asylum process, in particular in terms of financial and material-technical security of the asylum process to the extent defined by special regulations.
Priority tasks are issues related to deciding on foreigners" applications for asylum in the first level of administrative proceedings and complex operation of asylum facilities in the field of accommodation, catering, health, financial and material security of asylum seekers.
In addition, it prepares concepts for the migration policy of the state.
The results achieved in the development of the asylum system in the Slovak Republic in recent years have been significantly influenced by the cooperation and support provided by the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).
A particular benefit was his financial participation in the reconstruction of the housing stock for asylum seekers.
The UNHCR also co-financed social, cultural and sporting activities for applicants.
4.1 Evolution of the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process
The development of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is illustrated in the graph.
A significant increase occurred in 2001 due to the Kosovo crisis and in 2003 there was an increased number of refugees from Chechnya.
An overview of the results of the asylum procedure in the Czech Republic is given in Table 1.
In the audited period, asylum was granted in 394 cases, including 83 cases in 2001, 103 cases in 2002 and 208 cases in 2003.
During the audited period, a total of 22 731 cases were not granted asylum and in 22 636 cases the asylum procedure was stopped.
The number of parties to the proceedings as at 1.1. includes both persons who have not yet been the subject of a decision and those to whom the decision has not been transmitted.
It also includes persons who have been waived for missing the time limit for lodging an appeal or whose previous decision has been annulled and a new one has not yet been issued.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers has steadily increased.
If 96 applicants were registered in 1993, it was 10 358 in 2003.
A significant increase in the number of applicants occurred in 2001, when 8 131 applicants were registered, which represented an increase of 423% compared to 2000, in which 1 556 persons applied for asylum.
Data on the results of the asylum procedure in the Slovak Republic during the audited period are presented in Table 2.
A total of 49 asylums were granted in the audited period and their number did not exceed 0.22% of the registered number of applicants in individual years.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
The asylum procedure was halted in a total of 23,088 cases.
The bulk of the applicants, by staying outside the asylum facility without permission, voluntarily left the asylum procedure before it was completed.
In 2002 it was more than 82% of the total number of registered applicants and in 2003 it was more than 94% of persons.
The duration of one applicant's stay in an asylum facility, converted into an average number of days, was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002 and 19 days in 2003.
The findings of the Ministry also show that the majority of applicants entering the asylum process in the Slovak Republic are seeking better living conditions, i.e. so-called economic migration, which is not supported by documents adopted by the international community, to which the Slovak Republic has also signed up.
In such cases, the asylum system is used for a purpose by the applicants.
An application for asylum based on economic considerations, such as seeking employment or better living conditions, is not a ground for granting asylum.
Such an application should be made pursuant to the provisions of Section 12 par. 1 (a) 480/2002 Coll., on Asylum, is considered to be manifestly unjustified and should be decided within 30 days.
Internationally recognised principles to identify economic migrants have not yet been developed to distinguish them from applicants persecuted in their country of origin and to speed up the asylum process.
In view of the above, it can be concluded that the Slovak Republic is a transit country in terms of international migration and the countries of destination of migration were and remain Western European countries.
After joining the EU, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic acceded to the Agreement determining the State responsible for examining asylum applications lodged in one of the Member States of the European Communities (Dublin Convention).
The Convention prevents multiple purpose-built applications for asylum from being made in several EU countries.
Applicants return to the country of first registration after a positive identification in EURODAC.
The Slovak Republic is part of the external border of the EU countries, so the application of the Dublin Convention may result in an increase in the number of applicants who will need to create the conditions for residence in the Slovak Republic until a decision is taken on whether or not to grant asylum.
4.2 Use of funds
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are obliged to provide financial and material security for asylum seekers in accordance with international agreements and national legislative arrangements based on them.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the length of the asylum procedure until the final decision granting asylum, as well as their state of health.
The increasing number of people entering the asylum process has a direct impact on the higher uptake of statutory benefits for applicants, such as food, pocket money, expenditure on basic material equipment, other material equipment and other social allowances.
The amount of some levies collected is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, meals were CZK 58 per person per day, pocket money CZK 12 per person per day and CZK 6 per child up to the age of 15.
The cost per asylum seeker per one day of residence was on average CZK 351 in 2001, CZK 383 in 2002 and CZK 345 in 2003.
In addition to pocket money, an allowance of up to a minimum subsistence allowance may be granted to asylum seekers accommodated in self-catering accommodation centres and to applicants accommodated privately outside asylum facilities.
Paragraph 84 of Act No 325/1999 on Asylum, as amended, grants municipalities the right to a contribution to cover the costs incurred in connection with the asylum facility in its territory.
The amount of the contribution was determined annually by government resolutions and in the audited period amounted to CZK 7 per person per day of stay.
At the same time, municipalities are entitled to a contribution to cover the non-investment costs of primary schools attended by asylum seekers.
In the audited period, the amount of the contribution was CZK 120 per pupil per month, provided that the person attended the school for at least 10 days in the given month.
In the Slovak Republic, meal allowances were 70 Sk per person per day, 12 Sk per person per day and 8 Sk per child up to 15 years of age.
The cost per asylum seeker per day of stay was on average 442 SKK in 2001, 447 SKK in 2002 and 445 SKK in 2003.
In accordance with Act No 480/2002 Coll., on Asylum, municipalities in whose territory an asylum facility is situated are granted a contribution towards the partial reimbursement of expenses incurred by the municipality in connection with the establishment and operation of the asylum facility.
So far, municipalities have made only partial use of the possibility to apply for a contribution, which is set at SKK 1,500 per bed per calendar year.
National legislation in both countries provides for a 90-day period from the start of the asylum procedure for issuing asylum decisions, while allowing for an extension of this period in justified cases.
The most common reason for extending the asylum procedure, which affects the level of state budget expenditure, is the lodging of appeals against the decision not to grant asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions was issued between 90 and 180 days (31.54%).
The second highest number was within 90 days of the date of application for asylum (17.61%).
In total, 73% of asylum procedures initiated in 2001-2003 were finally decided within one year of their initiation.
Within two years of the start of the asylum procedure, 92% of asylum applications had been finally decided.
In the Slovak Republic, according to MÚ data, up to 90% of applicants who have not been granted asylum make use of the statutory possibility to extend the time limit by lodging an appeal with the courts.
In some cases it was an extension of more than a year and at the time of the inspection the court proceedings had not been completed.
A certain benefit in the shortening of the asylum procedure is expected from the establishment of common workplaces of the ÚÚ and the Border and Foreign Police of the Police Force in reception centres in Adamov-Gbelochy, Opatovskej Novej Ves and Liptovské Vlachochy, which took place at the time of the inspection from 1.10.2004.
This envisages simplifying procedures and shortening the time limits for procedures between the two parts of the asylum process.
5. Asylum facilities
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic set up asylum facilities in which they gradually created appropriate conditions for the provision of services to persons subject to asylum procedures.
In asylum facilities, asylum seekers are provided with accommodation, food, health care, pocket money and basic material equipment and sanitary supplies during their stay.
At the same time, courses are organized as part of leisure activities and applicants are created conditions for cultural and sports activities.
5.1 Asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
SUZ manages and operates asylum facilities and is competent to manage the state property in the premises of the reception centre Vyšní Lhoty, the reception and accommodation centre Červený Újezd, the residential centres Bělá-Jezová, Zastávka u Brna, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov and in the buildings of the integration asylum centres Jaroměř and Zastávka u Brna.
At the beginning of 2002, a reception centre was established in the transit area of Prague-Ruzyně Airport.
SUZ also ensures the operation of asylum facilities in Stráž pod Ralskem, Seč, Bruntál, Zbýšov and Kašava, which are operated by a legal entity on the basis of § 80 para. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of the reception centres is 747 places and the total accommodation capacity of the accommodation centres is 1 977 places.
Reception centres are closed facilities which asylum seekers may not leave until the prescribed medical examinations and basic reception operations referred to in Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum have been carried out.
Violation of the obligation to stay in the reception centre is considered a misdemeanor.
The accommodation centres to which asylum seekers arrive from reception centres shall be used to accommodate asylum seekers until a final decision on their application for asylum has become final.
Provided that certain conditions are met, asylum seekers have the possibility to leave the accommodation centres, or alternatively. to be in private.
Applicants for asylum shall be entitled to accommodation, meals, other services and pocket money free of charge in the reception and accommodation centres in which they are registered for their stay, provided that they have endured the acts necessary to establish their financial and financial situation and that such circumstances are such that they cannot reasonably be required to reimburse even part of those services.
Integration asylum centres are used for the temporary accommodation of persons who have been granted asylum.
Clients are accommodated in the centre on the basis of an accommodation contract, which is usually concluded for 6 months with the possibility of extension until adequate housing can be provided for them, or they can arrange it themselves within the framework of the state integration program.
In the integration centre, clients cover all accommodation costs and eat individually.
Persons with recognised refugee status have the same rights and obligations as Czech citizens and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1 Cost of asylum facilities
In order to compare asylum facilities, it was chosen as the best indicator of the level of costs per physical day of stay.
It is based on the actual number of persons who were actually provided with the services provided by the asylum facility on a daily basis.
In Table 3 and in the graph, facilities operated by SUZs identified as own and facilities operated by legal entities on the basis of Section 80 of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, are contractual.
The cost of one day's stay in the SUZ's own asylum facility decreases as the capacity of those facilities increases. This is due to the fact that the fixed costs of running the objects are allocated to more asylum seekers.
The total cost of providing services for asylum seekers increases proportionally with the increasing number of asylum seekers.
In 2001 and 2003, applicants were accommodated in their own asylum facilities in a crisis capacity.
In part of 2003, extraordinary accommodation capacity in residential containers (320 beds in total) was even used to address the capacity crisis of asylum facilities caused by the mass arrival of asylum seekers of Chechen nationality from Poland.
This capacity was provided by renting 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
Expenditure per applicant per day of stay was lower in those years.
However, it is not possible to maintain a high level of filling of these devices in the long term.
The risks of an unexpected influx of refugees and the associated requirement for higher accommodation capacity should be taken into account.
At the same time, it is not possible to carry out some repairs, maintenance and investments with fully occupied accommodation capacity.
The form of contracted asylum facilities allows for the adoption of operational solutions to the capacity of asylum facilities where necessary.
5.2 Asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
Asylum facilities are reception centres and accommodation centres.
The MÚ has in its administration the reception centres Adamov-Gbely, Rohovce, Opatovská Nová Ves and the residence centre Brezová pod Bradlom.
The total capacity of the reception centres is 470 seats and the residence centre 100 seats.
The growing number of asylum seekers was solved by the MÚ by establishing a residential centre in Gabčíkov in the rented premises of the Slovak Technical University Bratislava with a flexible available capacity from 250 to 940 places.
According to the concluded contract, the lessor also provides services connected with the operation of the centre.
In this form, the MÚ solved the lack of its own staff.
The residential centre was also temporarily set up in 2002 and 2003 in rented premises in Jazierciach with a capacity of 160 seats.
Reception centres had an average occupancy rate of 57% to 62% in the audited period and an average occupancy rate of 33% to 50% in the residential centres.
The occupancy rate varied according to the season and was highest in the last months of the year, when a much larger number of applicants applied for asylum compared to other months of the year.
Further increase of accommodation capacity by about 450 places will be possible after the reconstruction of resorts in Opatovská Nová Ves and Vlachoch.
With the completion of the centre in Humennom in 2006, the number of places will increase by a further 550 persons.
5.2.1 Cost of asylum facilities
The cost of operating asylum facilities is shown in Table 4.
Their analysis shows that the operation of an asylum facility by another entity, which will provide premises and ensure the operation of the facility, including the related activities, is one of the ways to ensure, at reasonable cost, the tasks arising from the stay of asylum seekers in the Slovak Republic.
6th Management of funds and state property
6.1 Analysis of management
In the Czech Republic, the approved budgeted expenditures of SUZ were increased by thirteen budgetary measures by CZK 103,077,000 in 2001.
Of this, CZK 89 979 thousand (87.29%) were earmarked funds. Most of it was earmarked for dealing with the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (CZK 44,538 thousand) and ensuring health care provided to asylum seekers (CZK 38,870 thousand).
In 2002, expenditures of the SUZ were increased by CZK 88,362 thousand by twenty budgetary measures.
Of these, CZK 62,282 thousand (70.48%) were earmarked funds, of which the bulk (CZK 53,200 thousand) was earmarked for health care provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003, expenditures of the SUZ were increased by fourteen budgetary measures by a total of CZK 88,078,000.
Of this, 82,000 thousand CZK (93.99%) were earmarked funds released from the General Treasury Administration.
The amount of CZK 51 000 000 was earmarked for health care provided to asylum seekers, CZK 24 000 000 for dealing with the influx of Chechen refugees and CZK 7 000 000 for the humanitarian evacuation programme of the disabled inhabitants of the Republic of Iraq.
An overview of the utilisation of selected SUZ expenditure in the audited period is given in Table 5.
It is clear from the above overview that the highest part of the expenditure was spent on the provision of services.
The amount of expenditure incurred for the purchase of services ranged between 37,07% and 38.23% of total expenditure.
Excessive expenditure under this heading was the cost of housing and boarding applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, the cost of medical care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service providing security in individual asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work done and insurance premiums (23.99% - 24.97%) accounted for a significant share of SUZ's total expenditure.
Last but not least, material purchases accounted for a significant share of SUZ's total expenditure (approximately 14%), with food purchases accounting for the highest share (7.61% ? 9.83% of total expenditure).
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the MoA to safeguard migration policy and the asylum process was marked by more budgetary measures addressing legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
The draft and breakdown of the budget in the expenditure part was characterised, especially in 2001 and 2002, by an imbalance between the requirements of the MoA, which were based on an increase in the number of asylum seekers and the needs to finance their legal entitlements, and the resources provided mainly in the main category of current expenditures.
The administrator of the budget chapter addressed the disproportion in the course of the year by several budgetary measures, which increased the current expenditure limit by 41.8% in 2001 and by up to 71.7% in 2002.
An overview of the utilization of selected expenditures of the Ministry in the audited period is given in Table 6.
Expenditure on salaries, salaries and insurance premiums, ranging from 24.47% to 30.51%, and expenditure on materials and services, ranging from 21.04% to 38.82% of total expenditure, accounted for the bulk of current expenditure.
More than 10% was spent on security services and from 3.92% to 7.20% on food purchases.
Expenditure on accommodation and catering services accounted for another significant part, with a share ranging from 10.82% to 26.96%.
Capital expenditure accounted for a relatively low proportion, ranging from 1.03% to 6.25%.
6.2 Deficiencies identified
The results of the audit in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic pointed to some similar shortcomings that did not have a major impact on the management of state funds and property.
These shortcomings were mainly in the following areas: a) the use of state budget funds contrary to the purpose for which they were designated by the Act on the State Budget, when current expenditures were used to cover actions in the nature of technical appreciation of fixed tangible assets; b) the violation of the Act on Accounting in the area of inventories and non-compliance with the guiding chart of accounts.
In the Czech Republic, minor shortcomings were also found in the handling of state property, where it was left for use by another person without a proper contract; failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in Land Registry data violated the Land Registry Act; leaving waste for disposal to a person who was not authorized to handle waste violated the Waste Act.
Furthermore, in the Slovak Republic, weaknesses were found in the provision of disproportionately high advances for the purchase of electricity and natural gas, in public procurement and in the management of state property when its records were not sufficiently secured and the method of liquidating unnecessary assets was not demonstrated.
7th Internal control system
In the Czech Republic, the SUZ was as of 1.7. 320/2001 Coll., on Financial Control, determining the competences of individual employees responsible for carrying out preliminary, ongoing and follow-up checks.
At the same time, an internal audit system was put in place and an internal auditor of the SUZ was appointed.
Each year, the SUZ is issued with a plan of financial, social and operational technical inspections aimed at comprehensive verification of the management of funds and state property in individual asylum facilities managed by the SUZ.
42 management checks were carried out in 2002 and 54 in 2003.
In the Slovak Republic, the direct performance of control activities in departments and organisations of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic in terms of compliance with generally binding legislation and internal regulations is ensured by the Institute of Control of the Minister.
During the audited period, the performance of tasks in the field of asylum policy was not audited.
The MÚ's internal control system is focused primarily on carrying out preliminary and ongoing financial control in accordance with Act No.502/2001 Coll., on Financial Control and Audit.
The performance of financial control is also regulated by the internal regulations of the IO Director.
The factual focus of the audit activity as part of the management of individual departments was determined in the framework of the annual plan of the MoA.
Directors of departments have been designated as responsible for exercising control in this area.
According to the written documentation submitted, no deficiencies were found.
Since the entry into force of Decree No 28 of 23 of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic. 4th 2004, the IO is obliged to handle and investigate complaints under the Complaints Act.
The organisational security of this task will need to be finalised in the near future.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Joint report on parallel audits of expenditures on the construction of the Prague-Dresden motorway
Introductory word
Without the existence of the trans-European transport networks, it would be difficult to imagine a modern, dynamic and, above all, united Europe.
Quality transport networks are a prerequisite for maintaining and raising the standard of living of Europeans.
Creating the conditions for rapid, safe, reliable and inexpensive transport of people and freight is an important task for the state administration.
This is a very demanding task, both organisationally and technically and financially.
European efforts at sustainable mobility often find it difficult to compromise with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and human-friendly environment.
Construction of transport infrastructure, also thanks to the necessary measures in favour of the environment, is costly.
Considered procedures and decision-making by the state administration in the preparation and acquisition of transport constructions can bring significant savings in public financial resources that can be used in other ways for the benefit of citizens.
One of the roles of audit institutions is to actively seek out deficiencies that have led to lower than achievable economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditures on transport infrastructure constructions.
The audit institutions should not only draw the public administration's attention to the shortcomings identified, but recommend measures to improve the situation, for the benefit of citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short Summary
The two supreme audit institutions of the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as Germany and the Czech Republic) the Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as "BRH") and the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as "SAO") carried out parallel audits of expenditure on the construction of the Prague-Dresden motorway (the D8 motorway in the Czech Republic and the A17 motorway in Germany) in 2005 and 2006.
The highways are connected by a border bridge co-financed by both countries.
Thanks to the cooperation with the SAO, the BRH was able to carry out a thorough audit of the effectiveness of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
On the basis of close cooperation with the BRH, the SAO obtained for comparative purposes the necessary data on the level of German bridge and tunnel costs.
In 2000, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany signed a contract for the construction of a border bridge.
According to the construction process, the completion date was finally scheduled for the end of 2006.
The 
The contract with the contractor was thus signed later than anticipated.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in a shorter time and to ensure its completion in 2006.
However, as a result, RMD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
As part of the joint audit work, the prices of bridges on the D8 and A17 motorways were compared on the basis of a conversion per m2 of the bridge structure area.
The statistical analysis of prices made it possible to identify bridges with high costs per m2 of area.
Analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in a group of large bridges with a length of over 100 meters.
The price increase was also attributable to the delay in the contract procedure.
When analysing the tunnel construction costs, the auditors found that the tunnel prices on the D8 motorway were significantly higher than those of comparable tunnels in Germany.
The BRH and the SAO now have a database of bridge and tunnel prices on which they will be able to rely in future efficiency checks of funds used for transport infrastructure purposes.
For the construction of bridges, both audit institutions recommend: standardization of bridge constructions and the use of coupled steel-concrete and special structures only in cases where prestressed reinforced concrete bridges are not adequate.
The main features of the cooperation were its team spirit and informality.
During the parallel check, auditors shared their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report informs on the course and results of parallel audits of funds spent on the construction of the motorway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in the Czech Republic and A 17 in Germany).
The audits focused on economy, efficiency and effectiveness of incurred expenses.
Parallel audits were carried out by the BRH in Germany and the SAO in the Czech Republic.
Parallel controls took place in 2005 and 2006.
The SAO audited the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditures in the amount of approximately CZK 20 billion including VAT (approximately EUR 690 million) on the border section of the D8 motorway, which has the number 0807.
Of this amount, €64 million of European funds (ISPA) were planned to be used.
In addition to the parallel audit carried out together with the SAO, the BRH audited the preparation and construction of the A 17 motorway in 2003 and 2005.
The funds spent on the construction of all three sections of the A17 motorway amounted to some €670 million, of which €277 million will be co-financed by European funds (ERDF).
The motorway from Prague to Dresden is part of the Trans-European Transport Corridor IV. Dresden - central and southern part of Eastern Europe - Istanbul.
The D8 motorway runs from Prague through Ústí nad Labem to the state border.
The A 17 motorway runs from the state border of the Czech Republic/Germany to Dresden.
At the time of the inspection, the border sections of both motorways were under construction.
These sections were put into operation on 21 December 2006.
I'm going to get to the end of the road, to the end of the road, to the end of the road, to the
According to the plan, the section No. 0805 between Prague and Ústí nad Labem is to pass through the protected landscape area of České středohoří.
According to forecasts carried out in the Czech Republic in 2001, the traffic intensity of 22 940 vehicles per day should be in 2008 on the border section No 0807 of the D8 motorway.
According to German forecasts, the traffic intensity at the Czech border will total about 25 000 vehicles per day in 2010.
In 2000, Germany and the Czech Republic concluded a treaty between the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic to connect the German A 17 motorway and the Czech D 8 motorway on the common state border by building a border bridge.
Both states are involved in the construction of the bridge, therefore the control of the construction of this bridge was an important aspect of parallel inspections carried out by both audit institutions.
Cooperation between BRH and SAO
Since mid-2005, the two SAIs have discussed close cooperation in the control of the construction of the motorway connecting Prague and Dresden.
Both sides had serious reasons for such cooperation:
1st
Germany contributes financially to the construction of the border bridge.
Its planning and construction rests with the RMD.
Therefore, the BRH did not itself have the opportunity to carry out an inspection of this construction project.
2nd
The SAO did not have the comparative database needed to assess whether the funds were used economically as regards the overall level of costs for bridges and tunnels on D 8.
3rd
The SAO needed to make sure of the effectiveness of the expenditure, taking into account the main technical parameters of the motorway, especially the arrangement of bridges and tunnels, which should enable the same quality of driving on both sides of the border.
Following preparatory discussions, the Agreement on the Coordinated Inspection of the D 8/A 17 motorway was signed by the Presidents of both SAIs on 4 January 2006.
Joint working meetings of auditors of the BRH and the SAO took place throughout 2006 at intervals of approximately six to eight weeks.
The meetings dealt with current problems and tasks, in particular the preparation of a unified methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels, the exchange of findings from the inspection of the construction of the border bridge and the preparation of joint reports.
Continuous exchange of information was an important feature of the cooperation.
While the BRH carried out most of the work on comparing the technical parameters of bridges and tunnels and the procurement procedure, the SAO prepared for the most part a methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels.
The applicable legal standards for control in the civil service differ in the way control actions are concluded in both countries.
For these reasons, both SAIs drew their own audit conclusions on their findings during their audits.
This report reflects the results achieved in parallel checks.
The cooperation will end with the signing of the final communiqué in the first half of 2007.
Border bridge construction
In the 2000 agreement, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany agreed on a possible completion date for the construction of the border bridge in 2005.
Both sides then agreed to postpone this date to the end of 2006.
The RMD acted as an investor.
Germany accounts for 42.13% of the bridge's construction.
In the period up to 1999, the RMD proposed that the border bridge should have a prestressed reinforced concrete structure.
In 1999, in agreement with its partners in Germany, the RMD approved the coupled steel-concrete structure.
This decision was justified by the reduction of the number of double pillars from seven to five and the consequent ecological benefit of such a solution for the valley.
Moreover, the comparative calculations carried out by the RMD indicated that the coupled steel-concrete structure should be a less costly option.
But there was a mistake in the calculations.
It was stated that the new steel-concrete structure would be only 397 m long.
In fact, it's 5% longer.
In the course of awarding the contract for the border bridge, the RMD made serious mistakes.
It did not prepare contract documents adequately describing the evaluation criteria and the sub-criteria for comparing tenders.
This error led to the tender evaluation committee and the Director-General evaluating the tenders in a subjective and problematic manner.
The unsuccessful tenderer challenged the results of the contract procedure.
A subsequent investigation by the Office for the Protection of Competition resulted in the contract for the award of the construction contract being signed later than originally planned.
This meant that the 2004 summer construction season, after evaluation of the bids, was wasted and the construction time was shortened.
The construction company agreed to build the bridge in less time, but at the cost of a substantial increase in costs.
The procedure offered included a double assembly of the bridge superstructure, a change in the structure of the pillars and the establishment and equipment of the assembly areas.
Moreover, the construction company was not able to procure the originally designed type of steel within the required timeframe.
The new type of steel - at a cost of approximately EUR 4 million more, which had to be fully paid by the RMD - made it possible to shorten the time for anti-corrosion protection, which in turn made it possible to shorten the total construction time of the border bridge.
Compared to the net price of €18.3 million offered in the tender, the total cost of building the border bridge will increase considerably as a result of the accelerated procedure and other financing adjustments.
The reduced time allocated to the works resulted in an increase in the price of about €5.9 million.
At present, the net cost is around €25.9 million, not taking into account the automatic price increase (as of October 2006).
Price comparison of bridges and tunnels
The two SAIs analysed the prices of bridges on the D8 and A17 motorways in order to identify bridges whose price was too high and to compare the prices of bridges on the German and Czech sides.
The analysis was based on methods of mathematical statistics.
Furthermore, the tunnels on the D 8 were compared with similar tunnels on the motorways in Germany (A 71, A 38 and A 4).
There are no similar tunnels on the A17.
In preparing this part of the inspection, it was important to identify precisely the relevant prices.
