JOINT FINAL REPORT on the results of parallel controls of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Joint Final Report
May 2017
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Introductory word
The submitted joint report informs on the course and outcome of international cooperation in parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, focusing on the administration of excise duties in 2012-2015.
Cooperation between the supreme audit institutions of both countries was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic in the performance of parallel audits focused on excise tax administration, which was concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel controls was chosen on the basis of the fact that both EU Member States are based on common European legislation in order to find out how it is applied at the national level, how the system of excise tax administration is set up and how the systems in Slovakia and the Czech Republic differ.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out consisted in the exchange of experience, the identification of differences and the identification of good practices.
Last but not least, it was beneficial to note that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise administration is very limited without parallel controls.
Miloslav Kala
Karol Mitrik,
President
President
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel inspections of SPD administration in Slovakia and the Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legal regulation of excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia and their administration is in accordance with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences have been found between the regulation of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic.In the Czech Republic, verification of the economic stability of applicants for permits and mandatory marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils and some other oils contribute to the effective administration of excise duties.In the Slovak Republic, the distribution of stamps is simpler than in the Czech Republic and less burdensome for the tax administrator.
In the fight against excise tax evasion, the supervision of the movement of raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials, the implementation of the fuel distributor institute and the register of retailers of consumer packaging of alcohol have proven to be good practice in both countries.
Excise tax revenues in Slovakia and the Czech Republic are growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's objectives of reducing labour taxation, introducing eco-saving measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, among other things because there is no indexation of excise duty rates in both countries.
This has the effect of reducing the importance of excise duties on total tax revenues and, as a result of increasing purchasing power, of reducing the tax burden on excise duties in real terms.
The introduction of environmental measures has been financially supported by the State in the long term, but these measures have a negative impact on excise revenues, which will therefore need to be replaced in the future by other revenues or by a reduction in state expenditure.
Administrative expenditure spent on the administration of excise duties in both the Czech Republic and Slovakia has been growing in the long term, mainly due to wage growth, and its effectiveness is declining.
In the Slovak Republic, this efficiency is also negatively affected by expenditure on the computerisation of excise tax administration (IT expenditure) and expenditure on wages of employees performing permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses per alcohol.
The e-administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic did not significantly affect the reduction of the number of tax administrators.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend the SAO to reconsider the justification for the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses.
In the Czech Republic, the effectiveness of administrative expenditure was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures during the audited period that would have led to a reduction in the personnel demands of the excise tax administration.
The number of comparable administrative acts of tax administrators in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic was similar in the individual years of the audited period, while the number of comparable tax subjects in the Slovak Republic is about one third lower than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrators in the Slovak Republic perform administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical performance of tax supervision, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic emphasize remote supervision and risk analysis.
Administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is more administratively demanding than in the Czech Republic and more costly due to the ratio of the number of tax transactions to the number of entities.
Electronic administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In the Slovak Republic, the administration of excise tax returns is fully computerized; in the Czech Republic, documents proving taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are transmitted electronically.
Both methods of computerization support effective administration of excise taxes and therefore the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend their application not only in both countries.
The total expenditure for the implementation of EMCS could not be compared as FS SR provided data on expenditure only for the upgrade of the system in 2011-2015, but expenditure was still incurred before this period.
Expenditures spent in this period only on the upgrade of EMCS in Slovakia were approximately 20% higher than those spent in the Czech Republic both on the introduction of EMCS and on the upgrade of this system in more than ten years.
Excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia did not achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenditures.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in Slovakia the administration of excise duties is significantly more resource-intensive.
The introduction of the electronic system for monitoring the movement of products subject to excise duty (EMCS) made the administration of excise duties more efficient, but to a lesser extent in Slovakia, as significantly higher expenditures were spent on the implementation and modernisation of the system than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
The cooperation of the two audit institutions took place on the basis of the Cooperation Agreement in carrying out parallel inspections aimed at the administration of excise duties of 18. 8th 2015.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic agreed to carry out parallel audits, which will primarily focus on the issue of excise tax administration and the results of which will enable analysis, mutual comparison and evaluation of the established facts.
Common audit issues were agreed on which parallel controls were based.
Characteristics of the subject matter and objectives of the parallel control:
The aim of the parallel checks was to compare the performance of excise administrations, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators, and to identify weaknesses in the excise administration process.
In particular, the following main audit questions were to be answered:
Did the excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenses?
Has the introduction of the Excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) made the administration of excise duties more efficient and has the expenditure to implement it been spent effectively?
The parallel audits should have identified the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of the tax administration in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, especially in the area of legal regulation and in the setting of the organizational structure.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The General Directorate of Customs (DG) and the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic (FŘ SR) have joined the joint declaration on mutual cooperation between the Visegrad Four countries, the objectives of this declaration include, among other things, the fight against fraud, exploring the possibility of harmonising legislation and seeking harmonised interpretations on the rules of selected problems, exploring the possibility of joint activities to increase the effectiveness in detecting fraud and sharing experiences and best practices.
1 The EMCS is operated pursuant to Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on computerising the movement and monitoring of excisable products.
Identification of the audit performed by the SAO of the Czech Republic
Inspection number: 15/33
Subject of the audit: Excise Administration
Objective of the audit: The aim of the SAO audit was to examine the procedure of customs authorities in the administration of excise duties, especially in the monitoring of transport in the system of conditional exemption from excise duties and in securing the tax (customs debts); to examine whether the system of excise duties administration is set up in such a way as to ensure the efficiency of the collection of state budget revenues.
Inspected period: years 2012-2015 and, in case of relevant connections, previous and subsequent periods
Controlled entity: Directorate-General for Customs
Identification of the audit carried out by the SAO SR
Inspection number: KA-023/2016/1050
Subject of the audit: Excise Administration
Objective of the audit: The aim of the audit was to independently and objectively examine whether the FS SR and the Customs Offices (CA) were operating economically, effectively and efficiently in accordance with generally binding legal regulations.
Audited period: years 2012-2015
Audited entity: Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic
Legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
The legislation on the administration of excise duties is divided into EU legislation (see Annex 1) and national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008/118/EC concerning the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC defines the excise duty and lays down the basic rules for the administration of taxes and the treatment of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This Directive makes it possible to levy taxes on consumption on other products.
In particular, EU legislation regulates minimum conditions for: the level of tax rates for individual types of selected products, the production, storage, processing and holding of taxable products, the chargeability of tax, tax exemptions and refunds, the supervision of the transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and the maintenance of registers of economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows for control procedures and institutes at national level, provided that they do not distort competition.
Excise Tax Legislation in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the regulation of excise duties is concentrated in the Act on Excise Duties (Act No.353/2003 Coll.), which regulates the administration of the tax on mineral oils, the tax on alcohol, the tax on tobacco products, the tax on beer, the tax on wine and intermediate products and the tax on crude tobacco.
This Act defines the forms of treatment of products subject to excise duties, the tax payer, the authorisation procedure, the conditions for the transport of products, the tax declaration and the penalties for breach of legal regulations.
The Act and related decrees further regulate certain other conditions for the disposal of mineral oils (labelling of mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and the storage of crude tobacco for purposes other than the manufacture of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and some other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in parts 45 to 47 of Act No.261/2007 Coll., on the Stabilization of Public Budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are contained in special legislation. Fuel Act No. 311/2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation regulate the conditions for the sale, dispensing, distribution of fuel and keeping records of fuel put into free tax circulation.
61/1997 Coll., on alcohol, and its implementing regulations define the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol.
Act No.307/2013 Coll., on mandatory labelling of alcohol, and the relevant implementing regulations stipulate mandatory labelling of alcohol in consumer packaging, conditions for handling control tapes and conditions for handling alcohol (i.e. for the manufacture, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, acceptance, use, possession, import or export of ethyl alcohol).
Procedures in tax proceedings, which are not specified in special regulations, are regulated by Act No. 280/2009 Coll., the Tax Code.
Sanctions are imposed in accordance with the procedures of Act No. 500/2004 Coll., Code of Administrative Procedure.
The conditions for the issuance of a trade licence (concession) for the pursuit of a trade, namely the production and processing of fuels and lubricants and the distribution of fuels, and the production, treatment and sale of fermentation alcohol, alcoholic beverages and spirits, are governed by Act No.455/1991 Coll., on Trade Licensing (Licensing Act).
The Czech Republic has made use of the authority to establish control procedures and institutes to control the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and to supervise compliance with legal regulations in the handling of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid, as well as in the handling of selected products for which tax has already been paid.
These include monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and crude tobacco, labelling of certain other mineral oils, labelling of tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic made use of the right to apply excise duty to other products and introduced excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
On the basis of the resolution of the Government of the Czech Republic of 3 October 2012 No. 735, to implement the "zero tolerance plan for the black market in spirits," major legislative adjustments were made in the Czech Republic in 2012-2015, introducing a number of measures against tax fraud on excise duty on spirits.
During the same period, there were also fundamental changes in the legal regulation of the tax on mineral oils, the tax on tobacco products and the criminalisation of the preparation of tax evasion.
Protection of tax revenue by criminal law
Effective from 1. 7th In 2016, the criminalisation of the preparation of a crime - the reduction of tax, fee and similar compulsory payment - was introduced. The modification should enable police authorities to take more effective and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, e.g. the deployment of operative means of investigation.
General provisions for the administration of excise duties
The issuance of a permit for the disposal of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act is effective from 1 January 2013. 1st 2015 subject to: reliability; non-debt; economic stability; authorization to conduct a trade enabling the performance of an activity related to the permit; a situation where the petitioner is not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
In particular, the aim of the legislation was to address the issue of tax arrears by reducing entities authorised to dispose of products subject to excise duty.
The condition of economic stability newly allows the tax administrator to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both in the permitting procedure and after the permit is issued.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent operators who do not have sufficient financial resources to properly discharge their tax obligations from disposing of the selected products.
In order to assess the economic stability of the proposer, indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labour productivity) have been established on the basis of which a financial analysis is carried out.
In addition to these indicators, the administrative discretion of the tax administrator depends on the individual conditions of the procedure.
The Act stipulates the periodicity of the verification of the fulfilment of the condition of economic stability due to the up-to-dateness of the data - the verification takes place once a year in connection with the deadline for filing income tax returns.
The tax administrator also has the possibility to set other conditions necessary for the administration of the tax.
If the permit holder does not meet the conditions, the tax administrator is entitled to revoke the permit or cancel it with a delay.
Of the total number of 2,609 entities for which the Czech Customs Administration examined the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable with a high risk of arrears if the tax liability exceeds the amount of tax security (e.g. repeated recipient).
The permit was revoked for ten entities, the other applicants increased the security of the tax, capitalized their contribution to the company or documented current accounting data, according to which they already fulfilled all the conditions for issuing the permit.
In addition to the applicant, the conditions of reliability and debt-free status must also be met by a natural person who is a statutory body or its member, or by a natural person who, although not a statutory body of the applicant or its member, carries out this activity (a chain of legal persons in the capacity of a statutory body or its member, so-called connected entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30,000 associated entities had been screened.
Records kept pursuant to the Excise Tax Act (Sections 37 to 40 and Section 60 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.) contain information on:
the type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, received, delivered or dispatched, broken down by type of tax treatment (suspension arrangement, import, reintroduction, export, free circulation, own consumption, loss);
the SEED ID of the consignee or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of occurrence of the event and the entry in the register;
transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carrier, transport number);
the registration numbers of the related documents;
notification of the release for free fiscal circulation of ethyl alcohol in immediate packaging marked with a control band and details of its distribution.
A record of receipt after transport must be made without delay after its completion.
In the case of records kept electronically, the records must be kept or allow output in the format xls, xlsx, ods.
Ethyl alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a set of measures aimed at ensuring a detailed overview of the activities of the entities (see Annex 3, Diagram A) from the production of raw alcohol through the labelling with control tape to its distribution to the final seller or the authorised user of exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the production facility for the production of alcohol, which is not in operation, is also subject to supervision by the customs authorities.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of the processing of alcohol and the production of spirits and to identify persons handling alcohol in consumer packaging, to reduce the handling of alcohol to financially stable and reliable persons and to ensure permanent supervision of the production and labelling of spirits.
The most important measures are: Records of production, intake, stocks and issue of alcohol contain information on the quantity of alcohol according to the individual stages of production and processing of alcohol with the document numbers.
Restrictions on the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and the number of packages with broken control tape at the point of final sale or release to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other packaging with a capacity of max. one litre or three litres if the container is made of glass.
Prepackaged spirit drinks shall be considered as unlabelled and prohibited to be disposed of.
At the point of final sale to a natural person for his personal consumption can be located max. one consumer package with a broken control tape, or three if fitted with a one-way valve.
Mandatory registration of a person who introduces alcohol in products in consumer packaging with at least 15% by volume of alcohol into free tax circulation and is: an importer of alcohol, a producer of alcohol in the Czech Republic or an operator of a tax warehouse under the regime of conditional exemption from tax, provided that personal and technical conditions are met.
Personal conditions - reliability, integrity and non-disqualification - must be met by the applicant and a person in his capacity as a statutory body or responsible representative.
The applicant must provide a deposit of CZK 100,000 to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. about €3,700 to €185,000).
The technical conditions for registration are a suitable place for the marking of alcohol and the equipment of the place of marking or tax warehouse with video surveillance equipment with continuous operation and remote access by the tax administrator.
The registration markings of the control tapes are introduced for the marking of spirit drinks of a capacity of more than 0,06 litre.
In the case of the transport of control strips, the registration marking of the control strips must appear on the transport documents or on the customs declaration at export.
Check tape till 30. 11th 2013 contained a ten-digit registration code, which included a four-digit registration sample number, an application code for the allocation of control strips and a classification code according to the level of ethanol concentration by volume.
Control tape from 1. 12. 2013 newly contains two types of identifiers and the amount of alcohol in consumer packaging expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20 °C, rounded down to the nearest millilitres.
The register of control tapes for the marking of spirit drinks contains daily records of the various methods of handling control tapes according to the registration codes and also documents on the basis of which the registration was made.
In the event of destruction, loss or theft of specific control tapes, their holder is obliged to notify the tax administrator electronically of the registration code of the control tapes in question and their number on the following working day after the decisive event.
Introduction of new offences and adjustment of the level of penalties applicable to infringements in the handling of control tapes.
Penalties may be imposed up to the amount of excise duty or exceed it up to tenfold (e.g. in the event of destruction or loss of control tapes in the amount exceeding 0.1% of the total quantity of an individual order of control tapes, in the event of failure to return the control tape within the statutory time limit).
Restricting the handling of control tapes only to registered holders who may not pass them on to another person, with the exception of their provision to a foreign supplier for the purpose of labelling spirits in consumer packaging produced outside the Czech Republic.
The exported control tapes must be placed on consumer packaging and re-imported no later than nine months after receipt from the tax authorities.
Mandatory registration of the distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging, provided that similar personal conditions are met as for a person obliged to label alcohol and with the obligation to lodge a deposit of up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. about €185 000).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of alcohol in consumer packaging.
Eligible persons shall be obliged to sell ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or to final sellers or may sell it as a final seller.
They may acquire alcohol from other registered persons, the insolvency administrator, an administrative body, state organizational units or unregistered persons in the exercise of tax execution.
Notification of the introduction of alcohol or sale in consumer packaging into free tax circulation is obligatory for the holders and distributors of alcohol to send immediately the following day after the decisive event to the tax administrator via the information system maintained by the tax administrator (ORO web client) or following the content in xml format.
The notification shall include the number of control strips used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the percentage by volume of alcohol, the European Commodity Code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or final seller, as well as the name of the product and the batch of production.
In 2014 and 2015, tax entities sent approximately 10.5 million notifications.
Mandatory concession (specific form of trade licence) not only for the production and treatment of alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in consumer packaging by the entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or to another legal or entrepreneurial natural person for his own internal use.
Concession trades may be performed only after a decision has been issued by the Trade Licensing Office, subject to the fulfilment of professional competence and other conditions.
No prescribed professional competence is required for the sale of alcohol.
The benefit for the tax administrator is an overview of the sellers and their establishments and restrictions
trading on reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, approximately 94,000 licences were registered for the production, treatment of fermentation alcohol, potable alcohol, spirits and other alcoholic beverages and sales in 2014 and approximately 104,000 in 2015.
Checks on compliance with legal regulations in the area of handling products subject to excise duties in the Czech Republic are also carried out by: trade licensing offices, the State Agricultural and Food Inspection Authority, bodies of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic, bodies of the Czech Trade Inspection Authority.
Where it finds that there has been an infringement or an infringement of the prohibition, it shall immediately inform the excise authorities thereof.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has set up a comprehensive supervisory system (see Annex 3, Diagram B) to which mineral oils subject to excise duty are subject, but also selected mineral oils not subject to excise duty which have been misused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from the production of mineral oil through storage, transport, labelling and colouring of selected mineral oils, labelling of certain other mineral oils up to delivery to the final consumer or user and, in some cases, consumption of mineral oils.
Customs supervision includes the manufacture of markers for the marking and handling of mineral oils.
The marking and colouring of selected mineral oils shall be subject to mineral oils falling within Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (kerosene other), 2710 19 29 (other intermediate oils not elsewhere specified) and to heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49, unless their labelling is prohibited.
For example, benzol, toluene, xylol and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion are subject to the labelling of certain other mineral oils.
Marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils with a marker is possible only with the permission of the tax administrator.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils, which are a group of mineral oils under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion) whose kinematic viscosity at 40 °C is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and having at least one of the following characteristics: the flash point is less than 150 °C, at least 20 per cent of the volume is distilled during the distillation test, including losses up to 350 °C.
These mineral oils were misused as admixtures in finished fuels, in particular diesel, or were directly used or sold to power engines, as the physical characteristics are very similar.
Entities handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres must register with the tax administrator.
For the issue of registration must be fulfilled the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative, which applies throughout 2 Except for beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by burning.
No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 E.g. for the use of mineral oil as propellant (except for navigation on water, unless they are private pleasure craft) or as a component for the production of propellant, if the labelling impairs their use.
registration.
To 30. 11th In 2016, the register of persons handling special mineral oils contained 54 valid registrations, at the request of the registration holder, four registrations were cancelled.
The electronic register shall contain detailed information on the receipt, own consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil, including document numbers, notification numbers of acquisitions to the tax authorities, places of storage and consumption, purpose of consumption, place of storage and consumption or, on sale, place of delivery and registration number of the purchaser.
Notification of any acquisition of special mineral oil must be given to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours before receipt.
The identification of trading partners, the name and nomenclature of the specific mineral oil, the quantity, the purpose of consumption or information on sale or transfer shall be reported.
Notification of the estimated quantity of mineral oil purchased, sold or consumed in the year concerned shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the calendar year concerned.
Notifications of the intended use and labelling, the place of storage or consumption, the identification details of the person to whom the special mineral oil is resold or transferred shall be transmitted before any change.
Notifications shall be submitted electronically by means of smart forms or by means of a data box in PDFa format.
In 2015, 630 notifications were made by persons handling special mineral oils.
Seizure and forfeiture of special mineral oils or means of transport must be declared by the tax administrator in cases where it finds out the handling of special mineral oils without registration or where the registered person fails to fulfil his reporting obligation.
As in the case of failures to fulfil obligations in the transport of products subject to excise duties, these deficiencies cannot be remedied subsequently.
Registration as a fuel distributor is compulsory for persons who sell or are authorised to sell fuel.
Only persons meeting the following criteria may be registered fuel distributors:
Mandatory Trade Licensing Office concession (specific form of trade licence).
The opinion on the application for a concession and, where appropriate, on the appointment of a responsible representative shall be given by the customs office, which shall examine whether the applicant for a concession, the statutory body or members of the statutory body of the applicant-legal person and the appointed responsible representative fulfil the condition of reliability.
If these persons fulfil the condition of reliability, the customs office shall give a favourable opinion.
A reliable person is a person of good repute in terms of criminal property, customs and tax law.
Professional competence is a condition for the award of the concession.
Debtlessness of the same group of persons as in the case of reliability.
A debt-free person is a person who provides sufficient guarantees that he will properly and timely discharge his payment obligations towards the State, i.e. does not have arrears to the state budget and general health insurance.
A fuel distributor may not be prohibited by a court or an administrative authority from carrying out an activity which renders his activity impossible.
The fuel distributor shall not be in liquidation or bankruptcy.
Deposit of security deposit (or bank guarantee) in the amount of CZK 20 000 000 (i.e. approx. €740,000), which can be reduced to CZK 10,000,000 (i.e. about €370,000).
The distributor is obliged to submit the notification of fuel distribution to the customs office within 20 days after the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification shall contain details of the individual purchase and sale of fuel.
The data to be notified are data on business partners, document numbers, product selected, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
The claim for a refund of the tax on mineral oils consumed in primary agricultural production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
Reimbursement of excise duty on mineral oils may be claimed only in respect of an activity which is clearly linked to an activity carried out on the land.
In 2015, there were approximately 64,000 claims for tax refunds in the total amount of CZK 1,172,844,680 (i.e. €43,401,720).
Since 2017, the Government of the Czech Republic has also introduced a refund of fuel excise duty to livestock farmers.
Farmers or breeders who, for example, are engaged in cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats will now be able to exercise this right.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on the sale of tobacco products at the old rate of duty
In response to the long-term under-achievement of budgeted revenues from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic introduced, with effect from 1. 12. 2014 restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate in the event of a change in the tax rate.
Excise duty on manufactured tobacco shall be paid by the use of tobacco labels.
The use of a tobacco label means placing it on a unit packet (Section 116 of the Excise Duty Act).
The manufacture of a tobacco product in a condition intended for the final consumer shall be decisive for the application of the rate of excise duty and need not be removed from storage, delivered, dispatched or sold or sold to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterising the excise duty rate appears on the tobacco label together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, and the label indicates the number of items in the package or the quantity of smoking tobacco in kilograms.
The tobacco label has no identifier.
The length of the transitional period for the resale of ready-to-eat unit packets of cigarettes bearing a tobacco label with the previous (old) tax rate was fixed until the last day of the second calendar month following the entry into force of the new excise duty rate.
The development of the collection of tobacco labels in 2014 and the comparison with the development in previous years show that manufacturers of tobacco products significantly frontloaded each year with tobacco products with the "old" tax rate, effectively delaying the effectiveness of the "new" tax rate by about one year.
Tax on raw tobacco
Due to the misuse of raw tobacco for the manufacture of tobacco products without the authorisation of the tax authority and the non-payment of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and monitoring of the handling of raw tobacco were introduced as anti-tax fraud measures.
Effective from 1. 7th 2015, raw tobacco which has not been used or supplied for the manufacture of tobacco products, has been delivered to another Member State or a third country or for which the origin, purpose or person to whom the raw tobacco has been or is to be supplied has not been proved shall be subject to excise duty.
Restrictions on the disposal of raw tobacco
Measures such as the supervision of the transport and manufacture of tobacco products, the marking of unit packets with a control tape and restrictions on sales at designated locations have been supplemented by restrictions on the disposal of raw tobacco.
Manufacturing establishments for the processing of tobacco raw material and the manufacture of tobacco products shall not be subject to customs supervision.
Only a registered person may store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, but such tobacco may not be further processed or processed.
The registered person may only be a person meeting the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative, which applies throughout the registration period.
The conditions of registration are: a) authorization to conduct a trade enabling the performance of the activity of a person storing raw tobacco, b) reliability, c) debt-free, d) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco has not been banned from carrying out his activity, e) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, f) provision of a security deposit of CZK 20 000 000 (i.e. about €740,000).
The electronic register shall contain the date of receipt or delivery of the raw tobacco, the document number, the identification of the trading partner, the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
Notification of any acquisition of raw tobacco by a registered person storing raw tobacco must be given to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours before receipt or dispatch.
The details of the trading partner, the quantity of raw tobacco, the storage address, the purpose of use and the details of the carrier shall be reported.
Notification of the estimated quantity of raw tobacco received or dispatched in the year concerned shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the calendar year concerned.
Notifications shall be submitted electronically by data box in PDFa format.
The transport of raw tobacco shall be accompanied by a document with the prescribed particulars.
Excise tax legislation in Slovakia
The legal framework regulating the area of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is based on EU legislation and thus co-creates its unified tax system.
Individual types of excise duties are exhaustively determined by the legislation of the Slovak Republic, which is similar to the legislation of neighbouring countries.
Definition of legislation in the Slovak Republic
The legislative regulation of excise duties is ensured by four laws according to the individual subjects of the tax.
Harmonization was achieved by the adoption of the following laws on excise duties: Act No. 98/2004 Coll., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No. 106/2004 Coll., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No. 530/2011 Coll., on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No. 609/2007 Coll., on excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All laws on excise duties constitute provisions of substantive law and deal with the taxation of the subject of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No. 563/2009 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes (Tax Code), is a regulation of procedural law, regulates the administration of taxes, rights and obligations of tax entities and other persons.
This legal framework transposed the individual provisions of Council Directive 2008/118/EC of 16 December 2008 concerning the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC and transposed the provisions of other directives and legislation of the European Community.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Slovak Republic
Since 2011, the legislation on the administration of excise duties has undergone several fundamental changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In the EMCS system, the monitoring of the transport of selected excise products under suspension of excise duty has been changed from a paper accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system where these transports are monitored in real time.
As part of the electronic EMCS system, the suspension of tax subjects" access to the EMCS was introduced in 2015.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The Customs Office has the possibility to suspend access precisely in the event of a well-founded fear of an unpaid or undetermined tax from previous tax periods and its unenforceability.
This concerns the payment of the tax, since the movement of excise goods requires the lodging of security, which is released by the termination of the transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A fundamental change in the administration of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the option to use so-called red diesel was abolished.
Designated gas oil, also commonly called red diesel, was a mineral oil.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific statutory purposes, e.g. in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The aim of the abolition of red diesel was to reduce the public deficit, simplify the system of taxation of mineral oils and reduce the administrative burden on the business entities concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely a fuel retailer.
The purpose of this statutory amendment was to introduce an obligation to keep records for all petrol stations.
The clarification of the movement of taxed petrol and diesel is linked to the obligation to purchase petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
New institutes of tax subjects, namely fuel distributor and fuel consumer, were introduced in 2014.
This amendment has contributed to the elimination of tax evasion for petrol and diesel and has made the movement of these fuels clearer (see Annex 4, Figure A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, the legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils have been extended.
In Slovakia, however, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to be labelled with an indicator substance.
Excise duty on manufactured tobacco
As part of the fight against tax evasion and monitoring of tobacco raw material, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Materials Act was extended and a new tax entity - a trader in tobacco raw materials - was introduced.
Tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movements are not monitored within the EU.
Furthermore, an obligation to register technological facilities for the manufacture of tobacco products has been introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using stamps intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of tobacco products.
The control mark shall refer to cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Under the new system, the purchaser of stamps must apply to the customs office for the issue of stamps electronically, through the stamp collection information system.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax subject and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was established in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of stamps was also introduced.
The changes significantly contributed to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system of printing stamps strengthens the system of control of goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the stamp to easily verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
Unique 12-digit identification number (1.ç2. place is a checksum; 3rd place is whether the code belongs to a checkmark or a group of packages; 4th place is a series identifier; 5th place is 8th place. place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9. place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
The control mark intended for the labelling of cigarettes must also indicate the price of the cigarettes, the sign indicating the validity of the rate of excise duty, the number of cigarettes in the consumer pack and the length of the cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected alcohol, wine and beer, as the original three provisions of substantive law were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The Act was drafted mainly because of the need for a comprehensive solution to the issue of taxing alcoholic beverages, addressing their production, monitoring movements, securing the tax, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, streamline the performance of tax administration, and reduce the administrative burden for small and medium-sized entrepreneurs.
The new way of dealing with the issue of taxation of individual types of alcoholic beverages introduced the use of a uniform rate of excise duty on an alcoholic beverage and took into account the percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength.
For still wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength of the final product shall be taken into account.
The beer concentration shall also be expressed as a percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength of the finished product.
A category of small-scale producer of fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which is to exempt from excise duty a natural person who produces a sparkling fermented beverage for his own consumption and for the consumption of his household in quantities of not more than 1 000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using stamps intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Under the new system, the purchaser of stamps must apply to the customs office for the issue of stamps electronically, through the stamp collection information system.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax subject and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was established in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of stamps was also introduced.
The changes significantly contributed to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Diagram B) and the elimination of falsification of postage stamps.
The new system of printing stamps strengthens the system of control of goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the stamp to easily verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
Unique 12-digit identification number (1.ç2. place is a checksum; 3rd place is whether the code belongs to a checkmark or a group of packages; 4th place is a series identifier; 5th place is 8th place. place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9. place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise duties on alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one common Act No.353/2003 Coll.
The tax on solid fuels, the tax on natural gas and certain other gases and the tax on electricity are part of Act No. 261/2007 Coll.
In contrast, in the Slovak Republic, each excise duty is regulated by a special law, except for the Act on Excise Duty on Alcoholic Beverages, which contains a tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic is from 1. 1st 2015 the issuance of a permit to deal with products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act is subject, among other things, to the proof of applicants" economic stability, which the customs authorities verify annually by conducting a financial analysis.
In the Slovak Republic, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding on the waiver or reduction of the tax security.
FF SR performs tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate over the handling of stamps for the marking of alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in a printing works and their sale to individual customers.
The law stipulates that the production of stamps is ensured by the state-owned company Mincovna Kremnica.
The production of tobacco labels and control tapes in the Czech Republic is not supervised by the customs authorities.
Tobacco stickers and control tapes will be taken from the printer by the authorized territorial office of the Customs Office in Kutná Hora.
Tobacco labels are taken over by their customers at this territorial workplace, control tapes for alcohol marking are further distributed to individual locally competent tax authorities according to the place of marking.
Czech legislation does not define manufacturers of tobacco labels and control tapes.
In Slovakia there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products or its part, in the Czech Republic there is no such obligation.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco label carries excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when tobacco labels are collected from the authorized customs office.
In Slovakia, on the other hand, the stamp does not contain excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, a refund of excise duty on mineral oils was introduced in the audited period in the case of their use for primary agricultural crop production, the so-called green diesel.
Since 2017, this tax refund has been extended to livestock production.
In Slovakia, such support for farmers is not in place (it existed until 31.12.2008). 12. 2010 as so-called red diesel).
In order to strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a deposit of CZK 20 million (i.e. €740,000).
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors was reduced from 1 891 in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1,717 tax entities).
In Slovakia, a similar institute of fuel distributor is in place, but without the deposit needed to secure excise duty on mineral oils.
There were 303 registered distributors in Slovakia in 2014 and 407 registered distributors in 2015.
In Slovakia, there is an institute of fuel sellers and fuel consumers, which is licensed by the locally competent customs office.
There is no such institute in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils are subject to labelling; in Slovakia, after the abolition of so-called red diesel, the labelling of mineral oils is not applied.
In the Czech Republic, the control tape for the marking of alcohol contains an eight-digit individual code used to verify the origin of alcohol and a twelve-digit registration code indicating the spirit content of the spirit drink, according to which the control tapes are kept.
The destruction, loss and return of the control tape shall be entered in the register on the following working day.
The holder of the tape shall notify their use within the same period.
In the Slovak Republic, a control stamp intended for the marking of alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique 12-digit identification number, which, if used once a month, is communicated to the tax administrator and serves to verify the authenticity of the control stamp.
The records contain the number of collected, used and claimed control marks.
Both the Czech Republic and Slovakia introduced the institute of compulsory registration or registration of alcohol distributors.
In Slovakia, registration is subject to the fulfilment of conditions relating, inter alia, to a storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol of at least €100,000 or paid-up registered capital of at least €100,000; minimum number of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining registration is subject, among other things, to a deposit of CZK 5 000 000 (i.e. 185 000 €) for the benefit of the tax administrator for the entire period of validity of the registration.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In Slovakia, the permanent presence of the tax administrator is required for the production of alcohol not only in consumer packaging.
In the Czech Republic, the production of alcohol in consumer packaging requires a special form of registration of a person obliged to label alcohol with the condition of lodging a deposit for the benefit of the tax administrator in the amount of CZK 100,000 (i.e. €3,700) up to £5,000,000 (i.e. 185 000 €) depending on the amount of control tapes taken and the installation of a tracking device with continuous access by the tax administrator.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and Slovakia greatly exceeds the minimum EU requirements for the subject matter and administration of excise duties and responds to identified risks from other Member States as well as to risks identified in tax territories.
Legislative changes adopted during the audited period allow tax administrators to prevent possible tax evasion to a greater extent.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, as part of the fight against tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw materials (e.g. leaves), an excise duty on raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials was introduced in addition to EU legislation.
Although neither raw tobacco nor tobacco raw material is a harmonised tobacco product, both the Czech Republic and Slovakia monitor their movements.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic may recommend that this measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the examination of economic stability of applicants for permits under the Excise Tax Act has proved successful because it reduces the risk of tax arrears.
For this reason, both audit institutions recommend applying such audits also under the conditions of the Slovak Republic.
Distribution of stamps is more efficient in the Slovak Republic than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden the customs authorities with costs related to transport between the printing works and the purchaser of control tapes and tobacco labels.
The financial administration of the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the existence and location of technological facilities for the production of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, the collection of tax on tobacco products is more effective, because the ordering of the tobacco label itself is a tax return with subsequent payment of tax.
The financial administration in Slovakia has a better overview of fuel sales points thanks to the introduction of the "fuel seller" and "fuel consumer" institutes.
The introduction of mandatory labelling of mineral oils in the Czech Republic enables simpler control of misuse of mineral oils with a reduced tax rate or exempt from tax.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and Slovakia (2014) a new control tape or stamp containing an identification code was introduced.
The control tape in the Czech Republic also contains a registration code, while in Slovakia the new legislation has waived its inclusion.
It is not yet possible to evaluate the impacts due to the short effectiveness of the legislative changes.
The introduction of effective labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol with a control mark or tape is an effective measure in the fight against tax evasion.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic may recommend the introduction of this control measure in other Member States.
The position of the Slovak Republic on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterized by a pro-client approach that does not block the funds of tax entities.
On the other hand, the Czech Republic's approach is rather restrictive, because it introduces a deposit burdening tax subjects" cash flow, but it reduces the risk of tax arrears more.
Development of excise tax revenues
Excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the State in order to increase the revenue of the State budget and also to regulate the quantity of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered harmful to individuals and/or society (regulatory function of the tax).
According to the Commission Communication: EUROPE 2020 - A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3. 3rd 2010 under the Resource Efficient Europe flagship initiative, the European Commission intends to improve the framework for the use of market-based instruments, including through a revision of energy taxation with a focus on reducing energy and resource consumption.
In order to fulfil the EC's intention, Member States should endeavour to shift the tax burden from labour to energy and environmental taxation, among others, as part of a greater "greening" of tax systems.
Collection of excise tax revenues in the Czech Republic and Slovakia includes collection of excise tax on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP is monitored, among other things, by the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).
Both SAIs used the following selection criteria to enter the query on the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties in connection with macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP declined slightly according to OECD data.
To convert amounts in CZK to € at 31. On the 12th of the relevant year, the ECB rate of the European Central Bank was used.
The nominal exchange rate of CZK against the euro in 2013 weakened by 9.1% year-on-year compared to 2012 (from 25.140 to 27.425).
This was mainly due to the CNB Bank Board's monetary policy decision of 7 November 20136.
The resulting values of excise duty collection, excise duty rates and income per capita in euro decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant decrease in the share of excise duties in 2014 was caused by a one-off shortfall in excise revenues from tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting sales of tobacco products with the old tax rate.
The share of excise duties is also affected by growth in income tax collection, which increased significantly as a result of the improved overall economic situation in the Czech Republic.
Excise duty on mineral oils accounts for the largest share in the total collection of excise duties (approximately 55.7% in 2015), but this declined despite significant growth in the economy compared to 2012.
The collection of excise duty on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although registration of fuel distributors was introduced in 2013 as an anti-tax fraud measure.
The trend of eco-efficient vehicles and the promotion of biofuels have a negative impact on the tax revenue.
Natural gas, solid fuel and electricity taxes account for a negligible share, due to the low tax rate, which is close to the EU minimum rates, compared to neighbouring countries.
In the absence of an increase in rates, their share will decrease in the future in view of the ever decreasing energy intensity of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the repercussions of a large-scale case of tax fraud involving the introduction of untaxed alcohol, alcohol containing methanol or insufficiently denatured alcohol into circulation in the form of spirits.
In 2015, following the adoption of a number of measures against such behaviour and the recovery of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded the 2012 collection by €4 million.
The share of the tax on tobacco products increased as a result of increasing rates.
The basic rates of excise duties changed between 2012 and 2015 for the tax on tobacco products, where the rate was increased mainly due to compliance with Council Directive 2011/64/EU on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
As a result of the CNB's monetary intervention, the real rate of excise duties in euro, excluding the tax on tobacco products, fell significantly. It rose only slightly for tobacco products.
In relation to price growth, GDP or the standard of living, the indexation of the excise duty rate is not set, so the function of excise duties to regulate socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
As the Czech Republic's economic growth and living standards rise, real excise tax rates are declining.
7 Indexation - an automatic adjustment of an economic variable for inflation, based on a law or contract (in the case of state-paid income, this is called indexation).
Collection of excise duties in connection with macroeconomic indicators in the Slovak Republic
The current legislative regulation on excise duties in the Slovak Republic does not address the indexation of excise duty rates to consumer price developments, as they are fixed.

THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Of all excise duties introduced in Slovakia, the excise duty on mineral oils accounts for the largest share of the full-year tax revenues of the state budget, while its share did not fall below 52% in the whole audited period.
Excise duty on tobacco products accounts for the second largest share.
On average, this tax accounts for around 32% of the total excise collection.
Between 2012 and 2015, the collection of excise duty per capita of the Slovak Republic increased.
This development is due to the rise in excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The growth of excise duty collection per capita of the Slovak Republic is constant and corresponds to the development of excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the decrease in income in euro per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention regarding the exchange rate of the koruna against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which is approximately 2.7 and 2.8 times higher in the Czech Republic respectively, but per capita of the Czech Republic the collection for these selected products is only about 1/3 higher.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and the exchange rate of CZK against € for foreign consumers.
In the case of the mineral oil tax, the cause is also greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of the tax on tobacco products, growing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases have a significant impact.
Assessment Real excise duty rates in the Czech Republic were falling as a result of the CNB's interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in total tax revenues is not rising and there is no shift from taxation of labour to taxation of consumption of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the achieved levels of the excise duty ratio are consistently above the OECD average.
The total collection of excise duties is influenced mainly by a change in excise duty rates, the development of economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future shortfalls in the collection of excise duties due to environmental measures subsidised by the State in various forms will have to be compensated by other revenues or by a reduction in state expenditure.
By not introducing the indexation of excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, their regulatory functions are reduced and the EU's objectives of a Europe less dependent on environmentally unfriendly sources and reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco are insufficiently supported.
The higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic reflects higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by a lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure on excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the correlation between expenditure and revenue related to the administration of excise duties, i.e. expresses the amount of expenditure per 100 units of income (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the efficiency of administrative costs.
The effectiveness of the tax administrator in the administration of the tax is influenced by the competence and organizational arrangement of the tax administrator, the management of the organization, the legal environment and the level of computerization of individual activities.
The determination of the efficiency of the administrative costs of tax administration using the conversion factor method is based on the number of employees involved in the administration of excise duties in a linearly managed structure.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties is carried out in addition to other activities by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is an independent organisational unit of the state and an accounting unit.
In the Slovak Republic, the administration of the tax is ensured by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, while the customs administration is an internal organisational unit, the costs and revenues are included cumulatively for the whole organisational unit.
Therefore, with regard to the possibility of comparing the efficiency of excise tax administration, expenditures and revenues of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were included in the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in the Czech Republic
Administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative acts performed mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some partial inspections are carried out by other public authorities, but their importance is negligible.
Excise duty administration is mainly carried out by the following departments:
Directorate-General for Customs
Department 23 TAXATION
Department 231 - Tax Methodologies monitors and proposes legislative measures, ensures the interpretation of legal regulations, methodically manages and coordinates: performance of tax administration agendas and related regulations, in particular tax proceedings and related control and supervision activities, administration of transport of selected products;
Unit 232 - ELO and Search performs search and methodological control of the transport of selected products and ensures international cooperation between ELO and EMCS;
233 - Tax control department methodically manages and coordinates the implementation of the tax control agenda at customs offices;
Department 30 LEGAL
Department 301 - Legal performs methodological activities in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative procedure, tax inspection process, registration procedure, discovery procedure, payment of taxes, fines for late tax claims, penalty payments and interest;
Department 302 - Administrative activities carry out decision-making activities in cases where the legislation provides for the competence of the DG, e.g. deciding on the delegation of the territorial jurisdiction of the entity to another competent tax administrator, deciding on the attraction, i.e. taking over the case by the superior tax administrator, appealing against decisions of customs authorities and examining suggestions of inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Unit 303 - Revenue and Enforcement Administrations methodically manages, coordinates and performs the tasks of international cooperation in the recovery of tax arrears and the performance of insolvency tasks;
Department 60 ANALYSIS AND INFORMATION SUPPORT
Department 601 - Risk and criminal analysis ensures and performs risk analyses and participates in the management of executive risks and the planning of control activities and control actions;
Department 604 Financial analysis performs financial analysis in the customs administration, especially in the context of the authorisation procedure.
Customs offices carry out activities within the framework of the agenda in various places in the region and the agendas are dispersed in several places:
Unit 02 - Analysis and information support, which carries out risk analyses, risk profile management and the collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Department 1 LEGAL
Department 11 - Legal and administrative activities, which prepares documents, opinions and submission reports for the appeal body, issues permit decisions in connection with the administration of excise and environmental taxes, the law on compulsory labelling of alcohol and the law on alcohol, decides on the issue of securing payment of a tax not yet due or not yet determined;
Department 3 - TAX
tax department 31, which carries out the following agendas: tax supervision of tax subjects, e.g. checking compliance with the conditions laid down in the issued permits, supervising the functionality and correctness of the production equipment for the production of alcohol and determining the quantity and concentration of the alcohol produced, professional supervision of the denaturing of tobacco products, physical inspections in the area of excise tax administration; non-tax inspections in the area of inspections on the basis of laws with an indirect relationship to excise taxes, inspection of the compulsory marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils, inspection of the tax compliance with tax regulations, inspection of the tax liability for the taxation of selected products, inspection of the marking of tobacco products;
Department 39 - Tobacco stickers and control tapes - is an organisational unit of the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region and carries out activities in the field of ordering, manufacturing and distribution and disposal of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
For the disposal of returned/damaged tobacco labels, representatives of the customs office as well as representatives of the DGs are present to supervise the disposal process and to record the disposal.
For alcohol-labelling control strips, the Director of the Customs Office shall, by means of an internal management act, appoint a three-member panel to dispose of the discarded uncollected/returned control strips by shredding.
After the physical destruction of the control tapes, the chairman of the winding-up committee shall ensure that the details of the destroyed control tapes are recorded;
Department 5 - CONTROL,
Department 52 - Tax inspections carry out tax inspections;
Department 6 SURVEILLANCE
Unit 61 - Supervision of entities supervises operators at points of sale, e.g. control of sales of spirits and tobacco products;
Department 62 Mobile surveillance performs inspection of transport of selected products on the way.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic from 1. 1st 2012 has undergone a difficult transition process in accordance with the approved UNITAS programme.
The establishment of the FS SR was also reflected in the composition of employees of the newly established departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In the context of the exercise of excise duties, the activities related to the administration of excise duties within the FSB organisational structure were integrated into a larger number of different sections and related departments.
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic Customs and Tax Section FŘ SR Department of Excise Duties (all-Slovak competence):
Guide and coordinate activities in the field of excise administration; draw up expert opinions; submit proposals and comments on legislative amendments; issue decisions on the delegation of territorial jurisdiction to tax subjects; assign and cancel registration collection numbers;
the Fiscal Supervision Unit - guiding and coordinating activities in the field of fiscal supervision and fiscal supervision;
guiding and coordinating mutual administrative cooperation activities in the field of excise duties, including the exchange of information through SEED and ISA; ensuring the management and updating of SysNeD and EMCS application equipment;
the stamps department - directs the printing and handling of stamps; exercises fiscal supervision over the loading and disposal of printing sheets and stamps in the printing works.
Department of Vice-President of Financial Administration
Department of Excise and Customs Remedies (Slovakia-wide):
the Excise Remedies Unit shall review the decisions of the customs authorities on the basis of the ordinary and extraordinary remedies applied; the appeal procedure at the second stage of the decision-making process.
The Customs Section was created in the course of 2012; it directly integrated the various Customs Offices (9 Customs Offices), which have territorial competence determined by higher territorial units, with the exception of one Customs Office, which was set up, inter alia, to carry out tasks related to the external border of the Community.
Customs offices:
Excise tax department - the performance of methodological activities in relation to branches of customs offices and stations of customs offices; for selected entities, the tax administrator performs direct acts, i.e. decides on registration (tax warehouse, authorised recipient repeated, registered consignor), on the amount of tax security, determines and refunds tax, performs tax supervision and tax control; decides on the waiver of tax security; decides on the waiver of the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee in the tax warehouse on alcohol;
Legal department - decision-making activities in relation to tax infringements; activities related to ordinary and extraordinary remedies; tax execution proceedings;
the branch of the customs office decides on the registration (with the exception of the tax warehouse, the authorised consignee for readmission, the registered consignor), the amount of tax security; prescribes and refunds the tax; carries out tax supervision and tax control; decides on the security and forfeiture of the goods;
station of the customs office - exercising tax supervision over the holding and movement of excise goods; ensuring the performance of permanent tax supervision in a tax warehouse for alcohol; deciding on the security and forfeiture of goods.
Expenditures of the Slovak tax administration on excise administration are steadily increasing as, with the exception of wage growth, investments in effective tax administration and the computerisation of financial administration are increasing.
Although excise revenues increased, expenditure increased faster as a result of the IT adjustments related to the UNITAS project.
Wage expenditure in the Slovak Republic is significantly influenced by the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses per alcohol, which the Czech Republic does not apply.
Expenditure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic on excise tax administration between 2012 and 2015 increased more significantly in 2015, this growth was caused mainly by growth in wage expenditure and expenditure on technical support.
In the Czech Republic, revenues from excise duties rose at approximately the same rate.
Compared to the Slovak Republic, wage expenditure in the Czech Republic is positively influenced by broader competences of the customs administration, e.g. weighing of trucks, control of fulfilment of obligations in connection with tolls.
The efficiency of administrative costs in the Slovak Republic shows a slightly worsening trend year-on-year.
The number of employees did not change significantly, but expenses per employee increased.
Also in the Czech Republic, the number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditures per employee grew more slowly than in Slovakia.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, wage growth is a significant factor in the worsening efficiency of administrative expenditure, which can be assessed as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining a significant administrative burden in the administration of excise duties appears to be a negative factor, as confirmed by the non-decreasing number of employees in the excise administration.
In Slovakia, however, the administration of excise duties with lower revenues is significantly more demanding on staffing capacity.
Performance indicators of excise tax administration
Excise administration is a set of activities aimed at correctly determining, determining and securing the payment of tax.
The main processes in the administration of excise duties are tax assessment, authorisation and registration of activities, supervision of transport, control and tracing of tax subjects.
The number of administrative acts and managed entities are indicators of the tax administrator's performance.
The correlation between the monitored indicator and the number of tax administrators expresses the efficiency of the tax administrator's activities and defines the cost of a particular activity.
Licences and registration for activities are essential prerequisites for the handling of selected products for commercial purposes and their transport under suspension of tax.
The tax administrator is obliged to perform continuous administration for entities with a permit or registration, with a focus on supervising the fulfilment of legal regulations and conditions set by the tax administrator, for which adequate personnel resources must be allocated.
The indicator monitored was the number of permits or registrations in force at 31 December of each year.
The number of authorisations or registrations issued is not the same as the number of taxpayers.
Administrative acts are specific administrative acts in a case.
