The monitored administrative acts are the most significant acts of the tax administrator (tax confirmation, transport administration in the EMCS), or activities that are a sequence of acts culminating in a report or decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Licence and registration to operate in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
Selected products may be produced, processed, stored, received or dispatched on the basis of a tax administrator's permission to operate a tax warehouse.
Where the tax warehouse operator has several warehouses, the authorisation shall be issued separately for each warehouse, including the securing of the tax.
Tax security is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax administrator (i.e. physical presence of the official and securing the equipment with the conclusions of the tax administrator).
In the Czech Republic, permanent tax supervision is not applied.
The tax warehouse operator is also registered for tax pursuant to Section 125 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.
Permission to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for the transport of selected products conditionally exempt from tax from the place of import to a tax warehouse, to an authorised consignee in another Member State, to a place of export in another Member State or to a consignee in another Member State (replaces the status of registered consignor under Art. Article 4 (2) 10 of Council Directive 2008/118/EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include tax-free permits for the acquisition of electricity, natural gas and solid fuels, which are analogous to tax warehouse permits.
Growing distilleries produce alcohol at a reduced 50% tax rate (CZK 14,300/hl ethanol) - fruit spirits for growers. It is not a tax warehouse and the permit to operate is issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced rate of tax may be applied to 30 litres of pure alcohol per household of the grower for personal consumption during the production period (July-June).
The cultivation firing register kept by the operators of the distiller and made available to the tax authorities must contain information on the grower, the basic raw material, the distillate dispensed, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
The authorised consignee for the repeated acceptance of selected products and the authorised consignee for the single acceptance of selected products shall be entitled, on the basis of the authorisation of the tax administrator and the conditions laid down, to receive once or repeatedly selected products under the conditional system shipped from another Member State.
The authorised consignee is not a tax warehouse operator and may not store or dispatch selected products under suspension arrangements.
The user of selected tax-exempt products is a legal or natural person who receives and uses, or sells selected tax-exempt products to another user pursuant to Section 52a or Section 53 of Act No.353/2003 Coll.; users have the status of tax subjects without the obligation to register for tax.
Selected exempt products may be received and used only on the basis of a final authorisation and only from the supplier specified in the authorisation.
On the basis of an authorisation, exempt mineral oils may be sold to another holder of an authorisation for use or to a user authorised to use mineral oils without authorisation.
Exempt mineral oils may be sold without authorisation in cases provided for by law, e.g.:
waste oils in quantities of less than 10 000 litres per calendar year, if produced by the user himself or in the course of his activities,
selected exempt mineral oils in unit packs of not more than 20 litres intended for purposes other than engine propulsion or heat production and at the same time intended for sale to the final consumer.
Selected exempt products may be transported with proof of exemption.
After mandatory registration with the tax administrator, the distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging is entitled to sell or otherwise transfer alcohol put into free tax circulation.
A storekeeper of raw tobacco shall be authorised, on the basis of registration with the tax authorities and the conditions laid down, to store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products.
A person handling special mineral oils is entitled, on the basis of registration with the tax authority and the conditions laid down, to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils which are in bulk or placed in packages exceeding 220 litres.
On the basis of the issued concession and the registration of the tax administrator, the fuel distributor is entitled to sell fuel on the territory of the Czech Republic under specified conditions, with the exception of the sale of fuel from a petrol station.
The transport of fuel must be accompanied by a tax document, a sales document or a transport document, or a distribution plan and bottling tickets.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent to the tax authorities before the start of transport.
The service station operator is the owner of the fuel sold at the service station.
Petrol stations are places where, by permission of the Building Authority, the sale or dispensing of fuel is usually allowed to the fuel tank.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade records petrol stations and their operators broken down into: registered - ordinary sale or dispensing of fuel usually to the fuel tanks of vehicles; with a defined approach - operating usually in various company premises (e.g. quarries, sawmills, agricultural farms, transport organisations, construction yards), the sale is carried out for the other party only on the basis of specific contractual relations; non-public - fuel dispensing points only for the own consumption of operators.
A service station is not a construction or installation in the form of an operational tank located in service (e.g. on a chassis) if the fuel is dispensed for own use only.
Operational tanks are not subject to the tax administrator's permission and are not registered.
Natural and legal persons may purchase, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases put into free tax circulation for resale on the basis of the tax administrator's permission.
They must also be authorised to purchase or obtain liquefied petroleum gases for their own consumption exceeding 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative acts in the Czech Republic
A tax audit is a set of actions. The subject of the tax audit are tax obligations, claims of the tax subject or other circumstances relevant for the correct identification and determination of the tax relating to one tax procedure.
A tax audit may be carried out jointly for several tax proceedings of a single tax entity.
Repeated tax inspections may be carried out only under the conditions and justification laid down by law when the inspection is initiated.
The tax audit is carried out within the time limit for determining the tax, which is three years, and the time limit is extended by one year under the conditions laid down by law (e.g. filing additional tax proceedings, initiating criminal proceedings in connection with the tax in question) or suspended (court proceedings, international cooperation).
The period for determining the tax shall expire no later than ten years after the expiry of the period for making a proper tax claim.
The tax administrator is not obliged to carry out a tax inspection of each tax entity.
Initiation of the tax audit imposes deadlines for the possibility of filing an additional tax return or an additional accounting by the tax subject (Section 141 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.) and restarts the period for determining the tax (Section 148 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.).
Its result may lead to an ex officio assessment of the tax.
A local investigation is an individual time-limited act (one day) in which the tax administrator searches for evidence and conducts an inspection of premises, goods, documents, records, means of transport and transport packaging at tax entities and other persons involved in tax administration, on a place outside the tax administrator's premises (e.g. at a tax entity, at a point of sale, on the way to transport).
The tax administrator is entitled to borrow documents and items, to take samples or to secure them.
On the basis of the outcome of the local investigation, it is not possible to assess the tax separately, but the tax subject may be required to file an additional tax return (§ 145 para. 280/2009 Coll.).
The EMCS traffic data check is not a local survey.
Only a registered person obliged to label alcohol can place an order for control strips for alcohol marking to the tax administrator of the locally competent place of marking and it is carried out by means of intelligent forms that are automatically imported into the application of the register of alcohol markers.
The tax administrator processes the order, evaluates the adequacy of the quantity of control tapes ordered and orders the production.
It does not supervise the production of control tapes.
The production is provided by the State Securities Printer, a state enterprise.
The purchaser of the control tapes receives the control tapes from the tax authority of the locally competent place of marking.
The order of tobacco labels for the marking of cigarettes, cigarillos, cigars and smoking tobacco fulfils the function of a tax return.
The value of the tobacco label corresponds to the amount of tax liability, while the purchaser of the tobacco labels is obliged to pay their value within 60 days from the date of their collection from the tax administrator.
The customer is obliged to calculate the value corresponding to the tax liability of the ordered tobacco stickers.
This period shall only apply if the value of the tobacco labels is assured.
Tobacco stickers are ordered on a form specified by the Ministry of Finance in writing or via a data box with the possibility of using intelligent forms.
The production of tobacco labels is ensured by the State Securities Printer, a state enterprise.
The authorized tax administrator, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region (territorial office Kutná Hora), ensures the purchase and transport of tobacco stickers to the tax administrator, who distributes them and further examines their transport, storage and use at customers.
Tax claims include regular tax returns, additional and corrective tax returns, including orders for tobacco labels, filed by taxpayers.
Tax declarations under customs procedure on the basis of customs declarations and declarations of claims for refunds on: mineral oils used for the production of heat, other petrols used in the course of business activities other than for the production of heat or the propulsion of engines, mineral oils used for primary agricultural production are not included.
The fines imposed include administrative proceedings to deal with the infringements found, which are a series of consecutive administrative actions. The international exchange of information on tax entities (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 takes the form of: requests for administrative cooperation, replies to requests for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, event reports, inspection reports.
Transport carried out under the conditional exemption regime between the Czech Republic and EU Member States - the Czech Customs Office is the tax administrator of the receiving or dispatching tax warehouse or the authorised recipient.
Performance indicators in the Slovak Republic
Licence and registration to operate in the Slovak Republic
Administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is ensured mainly by customs offices and the Department of Excise Duties of the Customs and Tax Department of the Slovak Republic, whose procedure for administering excise duties is regulated by individual laws on excise duties and the Tax Code.
These laws stipulate not only the scope of authorization for CA and FC SR in the administration of excise duties, but also the rights and obligations of tax entities in connection with registration or payment of excise duty.
The largest year-on-year increase in tax subjects (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, which was caused by an increase in issued permits within tax warehouses, an increase in registrations of an authorised recipient for re-acceptance and the registration of a large number of user enterprises.
The legislation clarified the transport of certain mineral oils in bulk, as well as the notification obligation if they are transported in bulk or in packaging of more than 150 litres and 230 litres respectively, and also extended the list of mineral oils subject to inspection and transport procedure to include other goods such as anti-knock products, oxidation inhibitors, bituminous inhibitors, viscosity improvers, anti-corrosion products.
A mandatory indication concerning the indication of their kinematic viscosity has been introduced for lubricating oils.
An approximation of the registration process for selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the Slovak Republic is given in the following parts of the document.
Tax warehouse operator
Within the framework of the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering a tax warehouse operator within the scope of all subjects of excise duties, a person who wishes to operate a tax warehouse must also apply for registration and issuance of a permit to operate a tax warehouse.
The resulting decision in the registration process is a certificate of registration for the relevant excise tax, by which the tax warehouse operator acquires legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CA issues a permit for the operation of a tax warehouse, which entitles the tax warehouse operator to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under the conditional exemption scheme.
If the tax warehouse operator has tax warehouses in more places, the tax administrator will issue a separate permit for each tax warehouse to operate a tax warehouse.
The transport of the subject of excise duty under suspension of excise duty is monitored electronically through the EMCS system.
A unique reference code is generated for each shipment.
ARC code under which the transport can be monitored on-line and thus in real time.
If the tax warehouse operator is also a person authorised to distribute ethyl alcohol, he is obliged to notify the CA electronically of the trade name of the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging he puts into free tax circulation, no later than the date of its release.
Registered sender
A registered consignor is a special type of tax entity which cannot also be registered as a tax warehouse operator, even if it dispatches the subject of excise duty under a duty suspension arrangement after its release for free circulation.
Within the framework of the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering a registered consignor in the context of all subjects of excise duties, a person who wishes to dispatch an item of excise duty under the conditional exemption regime after its release under the "free circulation" procedure must also apply to the CA for registration and issuance of a permit to dispatch the item of excise duty under this procedure.
The CA issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty and at the same time also issues an authorisation to dispatch the subject of excise duty under the duty suspension regime after its release for the "free circulation" customs procedure.
Growing distiller
The basic act for the operation of the distillery is obtaining a permit for the production of alcohol in the distillery from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic.
However, a licence from the Ministry alone does not entitle the holder of a licence to operate a distillery.
In order to operate a distillery, a person must submit an application to the CA for registration and issue of a certificate of registration of a distillery operator.
The CA issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, which also entitles the operator of the distillery to produce alcohol in the distillery.
The purpose of the distillery is to provide services to growers.
Growing distilleries cannot be tax warehouses.
The legislator allows a reduced tax rate of 50% of the basic tax rate, i.e. 540 €/hl a.
The reduced rate of tax shall be applied to ethyl alcohol produced in a growing distiller in quantities of not more than 43 litres a year per grower and per household per production period in the tax territory.
The production period runs from 1. 7 of the current year to 30. 6 the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year, and therefore it is possible to apply a reduced tax rate to the alcohol produced several times within one calendar year, because the alcohol is produced in two production periods.
This is the production of ethyl alcohol outside the duty suspension scheme, which means in practice that the ethyl alcohol produced is in free tax circulation.
The grower pays not only excise duty and value added tax for the alcohol produced, but also the price for the services rendered.
The growing distiller shall issue a removal certificate to the grower, which shall serve not only as proof of the origin and method of acquisition of the ethyl alcohol but also as proof of payment of the excise duty.
The transport of alcohol produced in this way is not subject to monitoring by the tax administrator.
Importer of consumer packaging
National legislation allows persons who intend to import consumer packaging of alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third country and put it into free tax circulation in the tax territory to apply to the CA for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
The importer of consumer packaging shall not register for the relevant excise duty, but the CA shall issue him with a confirmation of inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
That certificate authorises the importer to import consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol or consumer packaging of cigarettes from the territory of a third country.
At the same time, before issuing stamps, he must lodge a tax guarantee equal to the tax attributable to the quantity of ethyl alcohol or cigarettes which he wishes to put into free fiscal circulation.
The importer of consumer packaging must release for free tax circulation only consumer packaging marked with a stamp.
To that end, they must submit to the customs office of export the number and identification number of the stamps exported to the territory of a non-member country.
On importation, the importer shall have the number of stamps reimported from the territory of a non-member country certified by the customs office of importation.
When importing consumer packaging, the importer proceeds in accordance with the customs legislation, where the amount of excise duty is also part of the customs debt.
Where consumer packaging is released for free fiscal circulation, the tax guarantee lodged shall be returned to the importer or may be used to pay the customs debt.
The importer of consumer packaging is not a tax warehouse.
If the importer of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol is also a person authorized to distribute ethyl alcohol, he is obliged to notify the CA electronically of the trade name of the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging he puts into free tax circulation, no later than the day of its release.
Vendor of consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute for consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a permit to sell must apply to the CA for a permit and fulfil the legal conditions (trade licence; good repute in relation to intentional economic crimes; his permit to sell has not been withdrawn for ten years; he is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As this concerns consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation is sufficient to prove the method of obtaining the consumer packaging of alcohol.
The licence holder is obliged to keep for each establishment a calendar month a record of the number of items of consumer packaging of alcohol, the number of items of consumer packaging of alcohol issued, the stock of alcohol in consumer packaging of alcohol as of the last day of the month and a record of shortages or surpluses in the number of consumer packaging of alcohol received and issued.
The licence holder is obliged to purchase alcohol in consumer packaging or otherwise obtain it in the course of business activities only from the person authorised to distribute.
Distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislature introduced a new tax institute as a distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a distribution licence must apply to the CA for a distribution licence.
The applicant must fulfil the legal conditions (trade licence for a trade; storage area exceeds 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of spirits of at least €100,000 or paid-up registered capital of at least €100,000; minimum number of 10 employees; no arrears with the customs office; no arrears on compulsory levies; good repute in relation to intentional economic crimes; no licence to sell has been withdrawn for ten years; no liquidation or bankruptcy).
As this concerns consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation is sufficient to prove the method of obtaining the consumer packaging of alcohol.
The holder of the distribution authorisation is obliged to keep, for each establishment, a calendar month record of the number of received items of consumer packaging of alcohol, the number of issued items of consumer packaging of alcohol, the stock of alcohol in consumer packaging of alcohol as of the last day of the month and a record of shortages or surpluses in the number of received and issued consumer packaging of alcohol.
The holder of a distribution authorisation is obliged to purchase alcohol in consumer packaging only from another person authorised to distribute.
The person authorised to distribute shall notify the data for each calendar month electronically by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Fuel Seller
In order to monitor fuels in free tax circulation as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity was introduced, namely a fuel vendor.
There is no specific regulation governing petrol stations in Slovakia.
Therefore, petrol stations are incorporated into the national legislation of the Slovak Republic as fuel retailers.
A person wishing, in the course of a business activity in the tax territory, to sell petrol, diesel or LPG for final consumption in free tax circulation is required, before the start of the sale, to apply to the CA for a licence to sell and to produce a document proving that the storage facility is verified and equipped with suitable certified measuring equipment enabling the quantity of mineral oil to be measured at reception and dispensing, and the tank must comply with technical standards.
Where the fuel vendor is a tax warehouse operator, an authorised consignee or a registered consignor, the CA shall also issue an authorisation for the sale of fuel to automatically registered persons.
In addition to other legal obligations, the fuel seller is obliged to keep records of purchased and sold petrol, diesel or LPG per calendar month and is also obliged to notify the CA of the new fuel supplier (distributor).
A fuel vendor is required by law to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from a fuel distributor or a registered person.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
However, when delivering fuel through a tanker, the distributor prints a so-called bottle from a measuring device installed in the tanker when refuelling the dealer.
That document shall contain, in addition to the quantities, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the DMV.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor assigned by the tax administrator, is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel.
When exercising tax supervision over mineral oils, the tax administrator in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods.
First of all, this is an attempt to avoid roadside checks during transport, which is why hauliers use secondary roads, circumventing the toll collection system in order to make it more difficult to monitor actual transport operations.
Transports of mineral oils are also carried out in converted double-bottomed tanks.
It is often the case that illegal transport is accompanied by a vehicle which reports possible mobile patrols to hauliers in order to change their route and avoid roadside checks.
Fuels are also mixed with light fuel oils or waste oils.
Fuel Distributor
In order to monitor fuel in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity was introduced, namely the fuel distributor.
A person intending to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in free tax circulation in the tax territory in the course of a business activity shall, before the start of the distribution, apply to the customs office for a distribution permit and submit a document proving that the storage facility is verified and equipped with appropriate certified measuring equipment, as well as a list of suppliers and purchasers.
In addition to other legal obligations, the fuel distributor is obliged to keep separate records of purchased and sold petrol, diesel or LPG per calendar month for each establishment.
The fuel distributor is required by law to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
A fuel distributor may sell in the tax territory only to a fuel distributor, a registered person or a consumer of fuel.
However, when fuel is delivered through a tanker, the distributor prints a so-called bottle from a measuring device installed in the tanker when refuelling the fuel dealer or consumer of the fuel.
That document shall contain, in addition to the quantities, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the DMV.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
An invoice, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor or registered person assigned by the tax administrator, is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel.
Fuel consumer
The fuel consumer has a special position in national legislation.
A person who purchases, for his own consumption, petrol, diesel or LPG in the tax territory and stores that mineral oil in a storage facility with a capacity of 15 000 litres or more shall notify the customs office at the latest before the first placing in the storage facility.
The customs office shall register the fuel consumers.
He is obliged to indicate, in addition to the legal facts, the address of the location of the storage facility.
In practice, these are large transport companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
The storage facility must be verified and equipped with a measuring device enabling the quantity of propellants (marker, measuring rod) to be measured at reception and dispensing.
The tank shall comply with technical standards.
The fuel consumer must purchase the fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for transport.
However, when delivering fuel through a tanker, the distributor prints a so-called bottle from a measuring device installed in the tanker when refuelling the consumer.
That document shall contain, in addition to the quantities, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the DMV.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor assigned by the tax administrator, is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel.
When exercising tax supervision over mineral oils, the tax administrator in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods.
Small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who produces beer in the course of his business and meets the legal conditions.
Provided that the statutory conditions are met, a small independent brewery may apply a reduced tax rate, i.e. € 2,652 per hl/per cent by volume of actual alcoholic strength.
Annual beer production is limited to a quantity of up to 200 000 hl of beer.
As the production of beer outside the duty suspension scheme is concerned, there is no need for an accompanying document for the transport as it is in free tax circulation.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, they are small family businesses which also operate restaurants or saloons in which they offer their own beer for sale.
Administrative acts in the Slovak Republic
This sub-chapter presents the performance of tax supervision of excise tax administration in selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the Slovak Republic.
The largest year-on-year increase in administrative tasks (by 5.3%) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, which was due to the implementation of more EMCS traffic.
On the contrary, the biggest year-on-year decline was recorded in 2014, namely by up to 4.3%, which was caused by fewer completed tax inspections and fewer tax returns filed.
This decrease related to legislative changes.
Tax controls
By carrying out a tax audit, the CA ascertains or examines facts decisive for the correct determination of the tax.
When performing a tax audit, CA employees present themselves with a tax audit mandate, which includes, among other things, the purpose and subject of the audit and the scope of the audited tax periods.
In practice, this means that the audited tax period may be one month or more tax periods.
The scope of audited tax periods is determined by the CA.
The tax inspection begins when the record of the commencement of the tax inspection is drawn up.
Acceptance of the documents shall be confirmed by the CA.
The CA is obliged to return the loaned documents within 30 days of the completion of the tax inspection.
The CA employee draws up a report from the tax audit.
If a tax audit reveals a difference in the sum that the audited tax subject should have paid, declared or claimed a refund, the CA shall also send the audited tax subject an invitation to comment on the findings set out in the minutes.
The tax inspection shall end on the date of delivery of the report.
The period for carrying out a tax audit shall not exceed one year from the date of its commencement.
The tax inspection of registered persons and selected registered persons shall be carried out as necessary, but at least once until the date of termination of the right to determine the tax, which shall be 5 years.
The FF SR issued an internal management act modifying the above-mentioned deadlines due to the unified procedure of the tax administrator on the territory of the SR.
Local investigation
Local investigation is the activity of the tax administrator in which it searches for evidence, examines and establishes facts that are needed for the purposes of tax administration.
An employee of the CA draws up a report on the local investigation and gives a copy to the tax subject.
When carrying out a local investigation, a CA employee has the right to unrestricted access to land, operational buildings, rooms and places, including means of transport, transport packaging and accounting documents.
The quantity of alcohol produced shall be accounted for by means of an on-the-spot survey.
The established facts are the basis for the tax audit.
Similarly, when carrying out an on-the-spot investigation, the CA is entitled to take samples and to secure the case.
The FF SR issued an internal management act regulating the performance of tax supervision and local investigation for individual subjects of excise duties in order to unify the procedures of the tax administrator.
Permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses per alcohol
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1. 5. In 2004, there was also a change in the administration of excise duties.
The need for more efficient spending of state budget funds in the administration of excise duty on alcohol, the improvement of the business environment in this area and the introduction of legislative instruments for more effective suppression of the shadow economy in this area resulted in the adoption of new laws in 2004 in connection with the administration of excise duties.
One of the measures introduced by the new legislative change was not only the transfer of the tax administrator in the area of excise tax administration from tax authorities to customs offices, but also the introduction of the need for the tax administrator to be present in the tax warehouse for alcohol.
In the territory of the Slovak Republic, national legislation defines exhaustively that it is possible to receive, dispense, produce or process alcohol in a tax warehouse only in the presence of a CA employee.
This shall not apply to a tax warehouse which receives, stores or dispatches ethyl alcohol only in consumer packaging.
At the same time, the CA is obliged to provide employees in the tax warehouse so that the receipt, dispensing, production or processing of alcohol is not restricted.
The tax warehouse operator is obliged to ensure the working environment conditions for CA employees.
On the basis of a contract concluded with the FC SR for the premises provided, the CA pays the tax warehouse operator the rental costs.
In a tax warehouse for the production, processing or storage of ethyl alcohol, the production facility for the storage of ethyl alcohol must be adapted in such a way that the quantities of ethyl alcohol produced, processed ethyl alcohol, stored ethyl alcohol, including stocks of ethyl alcohol and the alcohol contained therein, can be ascertained at any time.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Where ethyl alcohol is not received, dispensed, produced or processed in a tax warehouse, the customs office may waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee and shall be required to secure that area by sealing the customs office.
In practice, however, this option is not used very often as tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs employee to their advantage.
Some tax warehouse operators make use of the legal possibility within the meaning of Act No 467/2002 Coll., on the production and marketing of ethyl alcohol, and use the production facilities for the production of ethyl alcohol in the distillery for growing burning and also for the purposes of the distillery for distillates, which must be a tax warehouse.
Around 250 customs officers carry out permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses per alcohol.
Issuing vouchers for the collection of alcohol stamps
The basic act for the collection of stamps is to send an application to the customs office for the allocation of a registration collection number and to issue a voucher for the collection of stamps for alcohol.
An alcoholic beverage which is ethyl alcohol means goods of the combined nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength by volume exceeding 1,2 per cent vol.
The trade mark is intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol shall be considered to be sealed immediate packaging filled with ethyl alcohol intended for direct human consumption.
Consumer packages falling within Combined Nomenclature codes 2207 and 2208 may be put into free circulation for tax purposes in the tax territory only if they bear a stamp.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee and the importer of consumer packaging, who will put it into free tax circulation, may mark the consumer packaging of alcohol with a stamp.
The stamp contains, inter alia, an identification number consisting of a 14-digit numerical digit. The identification number contains the registration subscription number (1.ç6. instead of a numeric digit), the volume of alcohol (7.- 11. instead of a numerical digit) and the concentration by volume of alcohol in consumer packaging (12.- 14. instead of a numeric digit).
Original design of the stamp on alcohol:
The registration collection number shall be assigned by the CA to each purchaser of the stamp separately.
Only a control mark the identification number of which corresponds to the volume of the consumer package, the volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer package and the customer's control mark may be used to indicate the immediate packaging of ethyl alcohol.
At the end of 2014, the national legislation introduced a new information system for postage stamps.
The aim of the new stamp information system was to simplify and computerize the system of ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using stamps intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee, the importer of consumer packaging and the consignee (buyer) of alcohol may label the consumer packaging of alcohol with a stamp.
A stamp purchaser wishing to collect stamps under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of stamps electronically.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of postage stamps is obliged to request their issue, to report data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of postage stamps.
The number of stamps ordered may not be less than 500 or more.
The tax administrator also communicates with purchasers of postage stamps through the electronic system of postage stamps, especially when announcing the number of postage stamps that the purchaser of postage stamps may withdraw, or when determining the date of receipt of postage stamps by the purchaser of postage stamps in the printing house.
Before receiving the stamps, the purchaser of the stamps is obliged to deposit into the tax administrator's account funds corresponding to the price of the stamps which he may withdraw and the amount of which shall be notified to him by the customs office.
The price of the stamp takes into account the amount of refunds to the printer. However, it does not take into account the amount of excise duty.
The state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice is authorised to print the stamps.
FF SR performs tax supervision over the handling of stamps and their liquidation in the printing works.
The FS SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when handling the stamps.
FF SR ensures the sale of postage stamps to the purchaser of postage stamps in the printing house.
The stamps may only be collected in a printing works from an employee of the Financial Directorate.
Issuance of vouchers for the collection of postage stamps for tobacco products
The purchaser of the stamp must apply to the CA for the allocation of a registration collection number and the issue of a voucher for the collection of the stamp.
Consumer packages of cigarettes may be put into free circulation for tax purposes only if they bear a control mark.
Only an undertaking which manufactures cigarettes may affix a control mark to the consumer packet of cigarettes.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee or the importer of tobacco products who wishes to put tobacco products into free tax circulation in the tax territory may be a purchaser of the stamps.
Only a stamp the particulars of which correspond to the relevant price of cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the pack, the length of cigarettes, the sign of validity of the rate of duty and the registration number may be used to indicate the consumer pack of cigarettes.
Consumer packages of cigarettes may be sold for final consumption only at the price indicated on the stamp.
At the end of 2014, the national legislation introduced a new information system for postage stamps.
The aim of the new stamp information system was to simplify and computerise the system of ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using stamps intended for the marking of consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A stamp purchaser wishing to collect stamps under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of stamps electronically.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of postage stamps is obliged to request their issue, to report data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of postage stamps.
The state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice is authorised to print the stamps.
FF SR performs tax supervision over the handling of stamps and their liquidation in the printing works.
The FS SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when handling the stamps.
FF SR ensures the sale of postage stamps to the purchaser of postage stamps in the printing house.
The stamps may only be collected in a printing works from an employee of the Financial Directorate.
A control mark may be affixed to the consumer packaging of tobacco by the tax warehouse operator or the importer of tobacco products.
A control mark may be affixed to the consumer packaging of cigars or cigarillos by the tax warehouse operator, the importer of tobacco products or the authorised consignee.
Only a control mark the particulars of which correspond to the indication of the validity of the rate of excise duty shall be used to indicate the immediate packaging of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos.
A control mark may be affixed to the consumer pack of cigarettes only in the undertaking which manufactured them.
The number of stamps ordered may not be less than 500 or more.
Within three working days at the latest, the CA shall notify the purchaser of the stamps electronically of the number of stamps it may withdraw, the price of the stamps and the account number of the FC SR.
The CA may reduce the number of stamps ordered if there are circumstances on the basis of which it is reasonable to assume that there may be a breach of tax legislation.
The FS SR will determine the date of receipt of the stamps by the purchaser of the stamps, but no later than within 10 days.
The date of receipt of the postage stamps will be notified to the purchaser of postage stamps via the electronic system of postage stamps.
The stamps shall be issued by the Financial Directorate exclusively in a printing works, but only after receipt of funds corresponding to their price into the appropriate account indicated in the electronic notification from the customs office.
The purchaser of postage stamps is obliged to keep a register of postage stamps in the electronic system of postage stamps separately broken down for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
In accordance with Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012, the ELO and SPD Systems Department of the Excise Tax Department of the FF SR is responsible for ensuring the exchange of information on the basis of a request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the competent financial administration authorities.
These are in particular requests for examination of entities within the framework of excise administration, requests for information concerning excise administration and also requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications shall take place in electronic form within the EMCS.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States includes the following actions: requests for administrative cooperation (request for verification, request for information on excise administration, request for confirmation of registration in SEED); reply to a request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; inspection report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Authorisation and registration
In the Slovak Republic, permanent tax supervision is applied to tax warehouses for alcohol; in the Czech Republic, this supervision is replaced by continuous supervision by the tax administrator via a tracking device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are tax warehouses, in Slovakia they are only registered by the tax administrator.
In Slovakia, there is an institute of registered consignor, which is included among tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In Slovakia, with a reduced rate of excise duty on alcohol in the case of growing burning, it is possible to burn 43 l a.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the reduced rate of alcohol tax can be applied only to 30 l a.
Growing distilleries in Slovakia must have a permit not only from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic, but also from the tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, cultivation distilleries are allowed only by the Ministry of Agriculture.
In Slovakia, the import of consumer packaging of alcohol is carried out in addition to the tax warehouse operator also by the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol.
The importer's authorisation shall be subject to registration of the applicant with the excise authorities.
In the Czech Republic, the import of consumer packaging of alcohol does not require any special permission from the tax administrator.
In Slovakia, the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol is subject to the issuance of a tax administrator's authorisation for the seller.
The seller of consumer packaging of alcohol has a statutory obligation to keep records, inter alia, of purchase and sale.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administrator does not issue any permit for final sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol, it is sufficient to issue a concession for the sale of alcohol by the Trade Licensing Office; the final seller does not keep any special records.
In Slovakia, the fuel vendor must have permission from the tax authority to sell them.
National legislation in Slovakia does not regulate petrol stations by any special regulation, all activities relating to petrol stations are regulated only in the Act on excise duty on mineral oils.
In the Czech Republic, the petrol station is regulated by a special fuel law, but the tax administrator does not issue any permit for the sale of fuel.
Petrol stations are registered and their list is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In Slovakia, it is not technically possible to obtain a list of service stations from the financial management system.
In Slovakia, there has been a significant increase in the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities since 2012.
This increase was due to a legislative change during that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits decreased significantly in 2013 due to the introduction of a deposit for fuel distributors.
Administrative acts
In the Slovak Republic, the substantive legislation stipulates the obligation to carry out tax inspections of selected tax entities.
This issue is further specified in an internal management act issued by the FF SR due to the application of a uniform procedure of tax administrators in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
In the Czech Republic, the substantive legislation does not provide for the obligation to carry out tax inspections; the procedural legislation provides only for the possibility of carrying out inspections no later than the deadline for tax assessment.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax inspections and local investigations carried out in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is the fact that the internal governing act of the FSR determines in which cases and within what time limits the tax administrator must carry out a tax inspection, while in the Czech Republic the correctness of the declared amount of excise duty or its refund is verified mainly by local investigation.
The number of comparable administrative operations in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 due to the increase in the number of transports in the EMCS system and also due to the increase in the number of tax returns submitted.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of administrative operations followed a slightly increasing trend between 2012 and 2015, which was influenced by the increasing number of traffic in the EMCS system and at the same time by the decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the number of comparable permits and the registration of taxpayers have resulted in different legislative arrangements.
The number of comparable administrative acts of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in individual years of the audited period.
In Slovakia, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is approximately two-thirds of the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for approximately the same number of administrative acts.
From the above it can be stated that the SR is focused more on carrying out administrative tasks by tax administrators, e.g. performing physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, more emphasis is placed on remote monitoring, e.g. monitoring devices, immediate sending of data via a web interface and risk analysis.
Electronicisation of administrative tasks
Electronicization of administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax returns can be filed via a data box.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has introduced so-called interactive tax return forms, which, however, can no longer be processed automatically.
The data must then be transferred to the taxpayer's personal tax account.
The benefit is the limitation of the error rate of the submitted tax returns (DAP), which saves the tax administrator's actions related to the procedure for corrections erroneously filed by the DAP.
The DGC is working on a new application for electronic processing of DAP.
Smart forms can also be used to: submit tax or registration applications and notifications of changes in data, claim refunds, comply with reporting obligations for the handling of special mineral oils, the handling of crude tobacco and the fulfilment of biofuel obligations.
The handling of control tapes is recorded by tax subjects in the ORO WebClient information system, which is available for registered subjects for registration by the tax administrator of the specified data.
The transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under the conditional exemption scheme must be carried out in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document, which is implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality into the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
The transport of selected products in free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic may always be carried out with a document proving their taxation, a document proving exemption from excise duty, a decision of the customs office on the placing of selected products under the customs procedure, a simplified accompanying document or another decision on the assessment of excise duty.
The required content of the data is determined by legislation.
In order to facilitate the fulfilment of these obligations, the Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for issuing alternative documents (Sections 5 and 6 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.).
This allows the paper form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents, which are sent to the data warehouse via the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, where each such document is assigned a unique twelve-digit identification code (JIK).
The JIK serves for customs control purposes en route and prevents repeated transport on the same document.
At the largest operator of a fuel tax warehouse in the Czech Republic, which puts roughly half of the fuel volume into free tax circulation, CS CR has on-line access to the electronic registration system, into which the entity automatically stores the issued tax documents.
CS CR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. an electronic system for registering and monitoring shipments of selected products carried out in free tax circulation.
This system should use 70% of the existing EMCS functional specification.
The advantage will be a user-friendly environment for both declarants and customs officers.
It will also be connected to the Global Guarantee Scheme, the Tax Entity Register or the Risk Analysis System.
The system should allow for an overview of transport in free circulation between Member States, which so far operates on the basis of documentary evidence without registration and the sharing of reference numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current procedure of registration of transports of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen mainly in the abuse of the simplified accompanying document, repeated use of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronics of administrative tasks in the Slovak Republic
When administering excise taxes, the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic uses electronic communication in monitoring the movement of goods in the EMCS system under the regime of conditional exemption from tax, stamps, filing tax returns and also in the registration and registration of tax entities.
In 2014, one-way electronic communication between tax entities and the tax administrator was also introduced, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016.
Within the framework of electronic communication, after entering the access data, the tax subject has access to a personal internet zone, the so-called electronic personal box, which is intended for communication with the financial administration.
Within this zone, the tax subject has access to an electronic mailroom through which he lodges applications, notifications, tax returns and other documents relating to the administration of excise duties.
However, electronic communication through the personal internet zone does not concern all tax subjects.
National legislation defines tax entities that are obliged to communicate with the tax administrator electronically.
These are primarily value added tax payers, tax advisors representing the tax entity and attorneys representing the tax entity.
During the audit, the SAO also examined the scope of computerization of excise tax administration.
These were only fully electronic transactions, namely tax returns and electronic communication within the ELO.
Leaving aside the transports carried out in the EMCS system, there has been an increase in the computerisation of selected comparable administrative tasks, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
In the Slovak Republic, fully computerized processing of tax returns is already in place, from its filing to the registration of tax liability.
In the Czech Republic, electronic processing of tax returns is not set up.
In the Czech Republic, tax entities can enter mandatory documents for individual transports in free tax circulation on the website.
In the future, the reporting of transport in free tax circulation is prepared in the form and on the basis of the EMCS system.
Evaluation
The system of reporting transports in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax supervision, thereby eliminating the transport of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid in violation of legislation.
This can be recommended as good practice.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Due to good practice in Slovakia in the area of computerization of tax returns, the SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic recommend completing the computerization of tax return processing in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes in organizational structure and personnel security in the field of excise duties
The organizational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic has undergone fundamental changes.
Organisational arrangements of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
Customs Administration of the Czech Republic from 1. 1st 2013 consists of the General Directorate of Customs and Customs Offices, which are administrative offices and organizational units of the state.
The DGC is the accounting unit for the entire customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been carrying out comprehensive excise tax administration since 2004 as one of the many competences it provides.
CS CR also performs:
(a) control of:
in the field of road transport (weighing of goods vehicles, payment of road charges, fulfilment of conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and international passenger transport),
• management of waste and packaging materials,
the safety of imported food;
in the field of consumer protection and the protection of intellectual property rights,
employment of foreigners,
b) customs administration - it is a complex application of customs regulations, commercial policy measures and formalities for the import and export of goods,
c) collection and enforcement of pecuniary benefits imposed by other public authorities within the framework of divided administration,
d) activities of the police authority (authorized customs authorities) in proceedings on crimes committed in violation of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is the tax administrator.
Although the scope of competences (simultaneity of control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there are cost savings of scale as the public administration does not have to spend expenditures on the position of the control group for each subject of the control separately.
At the same time, the administrative burden of the inspected persons is reduced by re-inspection.
10 The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic also performs from 1. 12. 2016 competence to verify the fulfilment of obligations in the registration of sales (§ 2 para. 112/2016 Coll., on the registration of sales) and from 1. 1st 2017 supervision of compliance with the law and the conditions for the operation of gambling, including the imposition of penalties (Section 116 of Act No.186/2016 Coll., on Gambling).
Within the project Modernization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed with effect from 1. 1st 2013 a three-tier structure to a two-tier structure, with the abolition of the middle management link (customs directorates).
The DGC spent approximately 51 million CZK (i.e. about €2,031,000).
CS CR from 1. 1st 2013 consists of DGC and regional customs offices, which are administrative offices and organizational units of the state.
Customs offices and their competences are determined by law, the administration of excise duties is carried out by all customs offices through departments and territorial departments.
Territorial offices are internal organisational units of customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is entitled to establish and abolish territorial workplaces and determine their material competence by decree.
Legislation does not provide for any competences for the territorial workplace; the territorial workplaces exercise the competences of the customs office on its behalf.
Organisational structure by 31. 12. 2012
Organizational structure from 1. 1st 2013
Administration of excise duties by 31. 12. 2012 was performed by DGs, eight DGs and 58 CA units (including branches), i.e. 67 departments and departments in total.
To 1. 1st In 2016, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the DGC and 51 departments at the CA and their territorial departments, as well as eight departments of the Legal Department of the DGC and the CA departments providing mobile supervision, i.e. Approximately 60 seats.
The costs of the CS CR most significantly affect wage expenditure.
As a result of the reorganization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there were no savings in personnel resources.
The performance of the main processes is ensured by customs officers in the service of the Act on the Service of Members of the Security Forces.
The possibility of reducing the number of these members is very limited in the Czech Republic, because according to the provisions of Section 42 para. 361/2003 Coll., on the Service of Members of the Security Forces, they may be dismissed from the service only in cases exhaustively defined.
Reduction of service posts as a result of organizational changes in the security corps is not a reason for dismissal and the employer is obliged to ensure the allocation of adequate service posts within the corps, or to provide service posts with another security corps (e.g. the Police of the Czech Republic, the Prison Service of the Czech Republic), otherwise they will be reassigned to the reserve for temporarily unattached, in which members of the security corps are entitled to 80% of the average service income by law.

Organizational arrangement of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic
As part of the Programme Declaration for 2012-2016, the Government of the Slovak Republic has identified as one of its priorities the completion of the reform of the tax administration through the UNITAS programme, which will provide additional budgetary resources by unifying the collection of taxes, customs duties and levies and suppressing tax evasion.
In this context, the tax reform was implemented at the central level, which resulted in the merger of the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic into the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the creation of the financial administration.
FS SR was established on 1. 1st 333/2011 Coll., on State Administration Bodies in the Field of Taxes, Fees and Customs, as amended, as a budgetary organization that has its seat in Banská Bystrica and is connected to the state budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
FŘ SR, CA and Criminal Office of Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No. 199/2004 Coll., the Customs Act and on Amendments and Amendments to Certain Acts, as amended, are customs authorities if they perform tasks under customs regulations.
In accordance with Act No.333/2011 Coll., on State Administration Bodies in the Field of Taxes, Fees and Customs, as amended, together with the tax authorities they form the financial administration.
The new organizational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration, the Competence Centre of Financial Operations, tax authorities, the Tax Office for Selected Tax Entities, branches of tax authorities, contact points of tax authorities, customs offices, branches of customs offices (CA Tax Branch, CA Combined Branch, CA Customs Branch) and customs office stations.
The main mission of FS SR is the effective collection and administration of taxes and customs, i.e. also excise duties, to fulfil the revenue part of the state budget and to protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the FC SR is the President of the Financial Administration, appointed and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The President of the Financial Administration is responsible to him for the activities of the whole financial administration and therefore also for the activities of the FC SR, which he manages and represents in full.
Organizational structure of FF SR from 1. 1st 2012 in abbreviated form
Within all customs offices in Slovakia, activities and processes in the field of excise administration are ensured by the excise department (9 departments) and the legal department (9 departments) in addition to branches of customs offices (38 branches) and stations of customs offices (18 stations).
