Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Within the organizational structure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic, in 2015, apart from the FSSR, the administration of excise duties was dealt with by 74 organizational units with a total number of 1 300 employees; these units manage almost 48 000 tax entities.
Within the organizational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties in 2015 was handled by approximately 60 organizational units with a total number of 1,011 employees, which manage approximately 114,000 tax entities.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of individual activities of excise tax administration is divided between several personnel independent departments.
Their mutual coordination and cooperation is solved through middle and top management.
In the Slovak Republic, the performance of individual activities (registration, tax return, tax inspection) in the field of excise tax administration is divided between the excise tax department and the branch of the customs office, within which the same employees of the tax administrator often deal with this agenda.
Evaluation
In the Slovak Republic, there is approximately one-third of the number of tax subjects per total number of employees in the area of excise tax administration compared to the situation in the Czech Republic; the effect of a higher number of employees on the efficiency of excise tax administration is not obvious.
EMCS
According to the preamble to Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on computerising the movement and monitoring of products subject to excise duty, the aim of the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of selected products was to make it possible to obtain information on the movement in real time and to carry out the prescribed checks, to facilitate the movement of goods within the Community under suspension of excise duty.
When setting up the system, Member States should have allowed economic operators, in particular SMEs active in the sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of the EP and Council Decision allows the inclusion in the EMCS of a national specification, a national database forming part of the system and such hardware or software as a Member State considers necessary to ensure full use of the system in its administration.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
Development and functionalities of EMCS
In the Czech Republic, the EMCS system was preceded by the Selected Products Registration System (EVV), which operated from May 2004 to the end of March 2010.
EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1. 4th 2010 and is continuously supplemented by European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
In the Czech Republic, the so-called customs module and declarant module were introduced.
The customs module contains a number of national functionalities.
In addition to the Community system, in the Czech Republic the EMCS system monitors transports under the conditional exemption scheme initiated and terminated in the Czech Republic.
After approval of the notification of receipt of a consignment intended for an authorised consignee for a single acceptance, the system ensures the automatic sending of the information to the tax entity register followed by the invalidation of the authorisation.
The system fully ensures the administration of received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELO, including the sending of replies with an attachment in any format and the provision of translations.
It is also possible to receive a manual export termination report in the ECS (only the transmission of an automatically generated report is implemented in the EU).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to currently required criteria.
EMCS will not allow the approval of an e-AD or receipt notification without a response from the competent customs authority to the risk profile (the risk profile cannot be ignored).
The declarant module is available for tax subjects free of charge, it takes the form of a web application, to which the user logs in with a username and password (coordinates), which are assigned to him after registration with the CS ČR.
Each operation in relation to the EMCS customs module shall bear a valid electronic signature in the EMCS declarant module.
The declaratory module allows tax subjects to directly record data on commenced and completed movements under the duty suspension regime, so that tax subjects do not have to spend money on the acquisition of the system.
The national functionalities of the declarant module make it possible to retrieve and store data offline (saving time for frequently used data), to fill in data on the recipient on the basis of a SEED ID check and to require mandatory completion of data that are optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows you to block in real time the securing of excise tax in the corresponding amount of taxable supply for each consignment sent from the Czech Republic until the end of the transport.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by EMCS.
Without sufficient security, it is not possible to send the e-AD proposal for approval to the CA of dispatch from the EMCS declarant module.
Each guarantee has a unique number and contains the ARC of the transport (including the amount of blocked collateral) for which it was used.
The tax entity can manage its guarantees directly in the EMCS declarant module, where it can see the current amount of the blocked and unblocked excise duty guarantee.
Expenditure on the implementation and use of EMCS
The development of EMCS was implemented on the basis of eight contracts with performance from 2006 to 2017 in the total amount of CZK 46,791,924.60 (i.e. 1 761 412,56 €) without VAT.
In accordance with the concluded contracts, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (i.e. 1 640 401,10 €) without VAT.
In the audited period, expenditures amounting to CZK 14,545,454 excluding VAT (i.e. €547.438.99).
The amount spent on the EMCS upgrade during the audited period and converted to one transport input into the EMCS is on average CZK 16.49 (i.e. Excluding national transport, these expenses per transport between the Czech Republic and the EU Member States amount to CZK 24.40 (i.e. €0.92).
The EMCS technical support was implemented on the basis of four contracts from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, the total amount of technical support in the amount of CZK 7,499,675 (i.e. €281,389.77) including value added tax.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 on one transport loaded into the EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6.18 (i.e. €0.23).
The development and technical support invoices related to the national solution and developed the EVV application already operated by the DG before the EMCS system itself.
Invoices were paid under programme financing from national resources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of the supply of services and other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in Slovakia
EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor the movement of excise goods between Member States under suspension of excise duty.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document - SAD, which was used before the entry into force of this system, thereby ensuring better control and management of transport.
In Slovakia, it has been introduced since 1. 4th 2010 and is continuously supplemented by requirements arising from EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport.
ARC code under which it is possible to monitor the transport on-line, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionalities of EMCS
The EMCS ensures the receipt and dispatch of excise goods only by those tax entities authorised to use the EMCS system, thereby significantly reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The biggest evolution of functionalities occurred in 2011 when EMCS was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the implementation and use of EMCS
The implementation of the EMCS system was implemented as another module of the SysNeD application equipment and therefore it is not possible to determine the exact cost of its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The aim of the EMCS was to replace the paper-based transport administration system.
The benefit of the EMCS system is a comprehensive overview of transport between Member States within the EU from the announcement of the start of transport to its termination - a significant reduction in administrative costs for tax administrations and tax entities for the processing, transmission and archiving of documents.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, national functionality enabling traffic monitoring in a conditional system between two points in the Czech Republic and Slovakia has been introduced into the EMCS system.
In addition, the automatic functionality of on-line monitoring and guaranteeing of excise duty is applied in the Czech Republic.
There is also a national functionality that monitors the risk of the tax subject or transport, followed by a mandatory response from the tax administrator.
Slovakia and the Czech Republic register a comparable number of transports within the EU in the EMCS system.
However, the expenditure spent in Slovakia on upgrading this system was €744,310.01 higher than in the Czech Republic between 2012 and 2015.
The SAO SR obtained data on the upgrade of the EMCS system from the FS SR only for the period since 2011, although this system was introduced and operated earlier.
Nevertheless, the expenditure spent on the upgrade of the EMCS system in Slovakia was 188,134.44 € higher than the expenditure on the introduction and upgrade of the EMCS system in the ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
Over the audited period, the volume of expenditures related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in the Slovak Republic per transport exceeds 2.3 times the expenditures of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
Cooperation between the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic met the objectives.
Both audit institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the excise tax administration system in the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
It was found that, despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences between the two tax systems which affect the efficiency of excise administration.
During parallel audits, examples of good practice were identified that could contribute to reducing tax fraud, and their importance will increase as tax rates rise.
Procedures to reduce the costs of administering excise duties have also been identified.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons unless mutually coordinated due diligence checks are carried out at the tax administration.
In this, the role of SAIs is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of a parallel audit of the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The 1977 Lima Declaration stresses that supreme audit institutions (SAIs) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The Declaration calls for tax revenues to be controlled as far as possible.
Organisation The European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers taxes to be one of the most important parts of public revenue.
The 6th EUROSAI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 dealt with the audit of public revenues carried out by SAI.
The development of a specific strategy for auditing public revenue is an important step towards optimising the control activities of SAI.
This applies in particular to taxation, which is the largest source of public revenue and the most prone to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may to some extent be unable to carry out control activities without the cooperation of the SAI of another state.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes substantial losses in the revenues of many countries.
In order to combat this crime, the competent authorities need to cooperate with each other.
SAIs that carry out inspections in this area must be willing to establish closer cooperation with each other.
It was at the 6th EUROSAI Congress in Bonn that the idea of carrying out an audit of the administration of value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") and VIES was conceived in cooperation between the Supreme Audit Office and the Bundesrechnungshof (Federal Court of Auditors).
Careful preparation followed, when both parties first had to get acquainted with the legal environment and procedures for VAT administration in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Based on the analysis of this information, a selection of control topics was made and included in the control programme.
Achieving efficient and efficient VAT administration is a long-term problem and individual countries (particularly the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve the system, simplify and make the collection of this tax more transparent.
We are convinced that the results of our audit can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrations, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the international information exchange system.
Report on the results of parallel inspections of the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 - 2005 - 1215
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Administration of value added tax after the Czech Republic's accession to the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the auditing operation in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in administering value added tax after the integration of the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "EU") connected with the free movement of goods and services and to examine the use of the VIES system, especially when controlling the application of the right to exemption from value added tax for intra-Community supplies.
(D) The aim of the audit was to examine the system of control of intra-Community value added tax, with a special focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the above-mentioned regulations.
This should result in a report on the weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
Value added tax information exchange system The audit operations were carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the SAO") and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as "BRH") in mutual cooperation on the basis of a contract concluded between the two audit institutions on 8 June 2006.
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected business transactions carried out between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "Czech Republic") and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as the "German Republic"), the use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation between tax administrations and the comparison of VAT administration systems of both countries.
The joint final report on the results of the audits was prepared in accordance with the European Directive No.31 for the implementation of INTOSAI auditing standards.
The audited period covered the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 31. 12. 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
A parallel audit in the area of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAIs.
In addition to the main point - the exchange of information on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004 - the audit covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and recapitulative statements, which are closely linked to the main point.
In addition, the audit included the legal situation in the field of international passenger transport by bus and a comparison of certain statistical data.
A comparison of the VAT administration systems of the two countries revealed differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion for registration is (among others) exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, payers are assigned only one tax identification number, which they also use in intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, taxpayers are assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, which is used only for business transactions on the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different registration methods create problems, conditions should be levelled across the EU (cf. 4.1).
2) International bus transport of passengers.
In the Czech Republic, international bus passenger transport is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of VAT (cf. 4.2.
3) VAT returns.
While in the Czech Republic payers file VAT returns only for individual tax periods (month or quarter), in Germany payers are obliged to file so-called provisional VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year they must file an annual VAT return.
Unlike in the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to file provisional tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to file VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see No. 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic payers file summary reports at tax offices, in Germany payers file summary reports at CLO.
Financial authorities in the Czech Republic therefore have data from summary reports immediately after their submission.
The information from the recapitulative statements is available to the German tax authorities only after it has been processed at the CLO.
The fight against VAT fraud requires that updated information on intra-Community transactions be made available as soon as possible.
The monthly reporting of recapitulative statements would shorten the time lag between the transaction date and the update of the VIES data.
This would in turn allow timely verification of taxation in the Member State of the purchaser (cf. 4.4).
However, this would require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for submitting a recapitulative statement.
(5) International exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech CLO monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for incoming requests for information.
The German CLO does not keep track of the elapsed time.
Consequently, the German tax authorities dealt with a significantly lower percentage of applications received within the prescribed period.
Due to these problems, the BRH recommended to the German CLO the implementation of a permanent warning (cf. 4.6).
(6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States is developing its own risk management system (RMS), which has its own strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and the BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5. ).
As part of the cooperation, both SAIs examined selected cases of intra-Community transactions between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together, thirty-one cases of commercial transactions in which there were doubts about their implementation or suspicions of VAT evasion were examined using the Customs Duty legislation.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used the information obtained in the form of international cooperation and assessed the VAT liability of the payers.
In these cases, the payers either improperly exercised the right to exemption of the supply from VAT or did not declare the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used due to different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to respond to a request for information.
Cases were found where payers erroneously reported business transactions in recapitulative statements.
As a result, the VIES data were incorrect and the tax administrations had to examine these cases (cf. 6th ).

4th Administration of value added tax in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Payers who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
According to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 337/1992 Coll."), a taxpayer, a tax payer and a legal successor of a natural or legal person who is defined as a tax subject by law.
As of 31. 12. In 2004, a total of 421 865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
To 1. 12. In 2005, the number of tax entities registered for VAT increased to 457,590.
A taxable person who has a registered office, place of business or an establishment in the Czech Republic whose turnover exceeds CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) in the preceding 12 consecutive calendar months becomes a payer from the first day of the third month following the month in which he exceeded the registration limit (§ 94 para. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; hereinafter referred to as "Act No.
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration within 15 days after the end of the month in which he/she exceeded the registration limit.
The current legal regulation does not allow registration of a taxable person so-called retroactively in cases where the reason for registration is exceeding the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with the right to deduct may become a tax payer even if it does not exceed a turnover of CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) if it fulfils any of the other conditions specified in Act No.235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not fulfil any of the conditions laid down by law may apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The delivery of the application for registration to the locally competent tax administrator initiates the registration procedure under Act No. 337/1992 Coll.
The voluntary VAT payer shall also state on the VAT registration application the date on which he/she applies for registration as a VAT payer.
Tax administrator data communicated by the tax entity, i.e. the completed registration form with all attachments will be verified.
If it has doubts about the information provided, it shall ask the tax subject to explain, supplement or substantiate the information.
After verifying that the tax subject meets the conditions for registration, the tax administrator issues a decision in the form of a certificate that the tax subject is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as "TIN").
The tax administrator shall indicate on the certificate the effective date of VAT registration and the periodicity of the VAT tax period.
The tax period is the calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the preceding calendar year did not reach CZK 10 000 000 (EUR 335 750).
If the payer's turnover for the preceding calendar year reached CZK 10 000 000 (EUR 335 750), the tax period is the calendar month.
A payer whose turnover in the preceding calendar year reached CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax period and shall notify the tax administrator of this change.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the VAT number in the registration certificate is always of a constitutive nature and the tax subject is obliged to indicate it in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special law so provides (e.g. Act No.235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The TIN contains the code "CZ" and the master part, which is a generic identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is the birth number, or. another general identifier, if provided for by a special law, and in the case of a legal entity, an identification number (provision § 33 para. 337/1992 Coll.).
If the tax entity has not fulfilled its registration obligation even on the request of the tax administrator, the locally competent tax administrator shall register it without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issuance of an Ex Officio Registration Certificate, which is served on the tax subject.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that has been authorised to conduct business activities is assigned a TIN at the moment of its first registration for any tax.
The tax subject uses the same VAT number even if he is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the wording of Act No.235/2004 Coll., which is effective from 1 January 2004. 1st 2005, in the event of failure to comply with the VAT registration obligation, the tax administrator may charge the taxable person a refund of up to 10% of the total revenue or income for taxable transactions that the taxable person has carried out improperly without tax, for the period from the date on which he should have been a registered payer by law to the date on which he became a registered payer by virtue of the tax administrator's decision (Section 98 para. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payment of the amount determined in this way is considered as a tax payment (§ 98 para. 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. is not a sanction.
Cancellation of VAT registration if the statutory conditions are met is possible for two reasons:
(1)
Cancellation of registration at the request of the payer, primarily due to the amount of turnover that does not reach the registration limit (§ 106 para. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer is entitled to apply for deregistration no sooner than 1 year after the effective date stated on the registration certificate.
2) Cancellation of registration ex officio (§ 106 para. 235/2004 Coll.), if: a) the payer has failed to perform for 12 consecutive months without announcing the reason to the tax administrator, b) the payer fails to fulfil his obligations under Act No.235/2004 Coll., c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Payers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who carries out a transaction with a place of performance in the Czech Republic and is a person obliged to declare and pay tax on this transaction pursuant to Section 108 of Act No.235/2004 Coll. (the so-called "non-established payer") becomes a payer on the day of such transaction.
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration to the Financial Office for Prague 1 no later than the date of performance.
It is required to indicate in the registration application all the TINs allocated to it in other Member States or in a third country.
If the "non-established" payer submits an application for registration later than the date of the first taxable supply in the Czech Republic, the Financial Office for Prague 1 will register it retroactively, because according to Act No.235/2004 Coll., the tax subject became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable supply in the Czech Republic.
When registering retroactively, the Financial Office for Prague 1 requires tax entities to provide proof that the transaction has been performed (invoices or invoices). explanatory letters).
If a "non-established" tax subject applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable supply is made, then the Financial Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts that the supply will take place.
At the Financial Office for Prague 1, as of 31. 12. In 2004, 473 unsettled payers were registered, including 124 payers from Germany, and as of 31. 12. In 2005, 951 unsettled payers were registered, 233 of them from Germany.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 106 para. 235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of the "non-established" payer as of 31 January of the following calendar year if the payer did not incur any obligation to declare and pay the tax during the current calendar year.
The SAO audit revealed that if the "non-established" payer submits a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 January, i.e. In accordance with the legal regulation by the deadline for filing the tax return, it is often not available to the tax office on 31 January.
In cases where the facts relevant for the possibility of deregistration to the tax authority are known later than 31 January, it is no longer possible to cancel VAT registration in the Czech Republic in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in Germany
Due to the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (§ 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter referred to as "AO"), anyone who carries out business activities is obliged to inform the municipal/municipal authority or the competent tax authority.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after the start of the business.
This information is processed by the municipal/municipal office for the tax office.
If the tax office identifies a business that has started but has not registered, the competent tax office may register that payer ex officio - even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both resident and non-resident for tax purposes in Germany are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria laid down in Paragraph 2 of the German Law on VAT ("the UStG").
That obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover which they generate.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
There are special tax offices for entrepreneurs permanently residing abroad.
For example, for those established in the Czech Republic, the competent tax authority is Chemnitz-Süd.
As of 30 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Financial Office; as of 1 March 2006, a total of 1,050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered.
The BRH found that these special tax authorities often refused to register so-called semi-dependent independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
As work permits for employees from the ten new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers have tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
Those undertakings do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs laid down in Paragraph 2 of the UStG because they are normally dependent on a single employer, which determines their working time and the manner in which they carry out their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must complete a questionnaire from the relevant tax authority in which he must provide information about the company and the activities it carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form which is binding on all tax authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the tax authorities or by departments with a general focus, which are responsible for the assessment of taxpayers.
This form is used to assess the risk of individual taxpayers before the tax office issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions is governed by certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the relevant tax office, the following three (or four) provide information about the relevant department at the tax office, the next five (or four) are to distinguish payers, the last being always a check digit.
If the entrepreneur intends to participate in intra-Community trade, he needs a VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive an exempt intra-Community supply.
The CLO assigns a VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and if he has a VAT number.
The CLO assigns VAT ID to entrepreneurs automatically when the payers indicate an intra-Community supply in their VAT return.
VAT ID structure is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
Entrepreneur's registration may be revoked: (1) at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business activities), after all administrative work has been carried out (assessment for all business years) and (2) if the tax administration realises that he is no longer engaged in business activities.
The validity of a VAT identification number is normally linked to the validity of the VAT number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are obliged to inform the CLO of the cancellation of the tax number so that the CLO can terminate the validity of the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT Act (§ 19 (1) UStG), tax residents in Germany are not required to pay VAT if (1) the turnover plus the corresponding VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and (2) it is unlikely to exceed EUR 50 000 in the following year.
So-called small business owners (the "Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice other business owners for VAT and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not liable for VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and must submit an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur may declare that the provisions of Section 19 para. 1 UStG to apply.
This declaration is binding on him for the next five years.
The trader can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
For non-resident taxpayers, it is possible to appoint tax representatives (Paragraph 22a UStG).
It is a prerequisite that they carry out exclusively exempt commercial transactions and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
The function of the tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign entrepreneur, who does not have to register for VAT.
Invoices must include information on representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion for registration is (among others) exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
If the tax entity in the Czech Republic does not exceed the stipulated limit, it has the option to apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration procedure is standardised in Germany, but differences may arise as a result of different organisational models in the federal states.
In the Czech Republic, the tax identification number is assigned to the payer at the moment of its first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he uses the same VAT number for intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, the tax number assigned to the payer when registering for VAT is used only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and BRH found out, the German two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, such as the Czech Republic, which assigns a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intra-Community transactions.
On the other hand, the two-stage system allows retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax authority about their business.
This retroactive registration allows the correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax year, in particular the accurate estimation of VAT liability.
As different registration methods create problems, the conditions should be levelled across the EU.
The German Parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (TIN).
The Federal Taxation Office will allocate the TIN at birth to a natural person.
This TIN will be valid for the entire life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the relevant tax office will ask for an economic VAT number, which will be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the allocation of VAT ID.
Work on the implementation of an IT device to manage the TIN has not yet been completed.
International bus passenger transport
Legislation in the Czech Republic
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., with effect from 1. 5. 2004 Passenger transport between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct tax.
That transport is exempt from VAT even if it is carried out by traders who are registered for tax purposes in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
The return transport is considered to be a separate transport.
If non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out any other economic activity besides international bus passenger transport, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International passenger transport in the Czech Republic has been exempted from VAT on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V, ch. Article 5 (1) 1 (a) (b) where it is stated:
For the purposes of Art. Article 28 (1) Article 3 (a) Pursuant to Article 5 (1) (b) of Directive 77/388/EEC, the Czech Republic may continue to exempt from value added tax the international transport of passengers referred to in point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Art. Article 28 (1) 4 of the Directive or for as long as the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier.
Description of legal regulation in Germany
According to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006, implemented in § 3b para. 1 of the German VAT Act is the place of supply of passenger transport (i.e. transport services) route (i.e. place) where the shipment takes place.
Therefore, the German tax system does not distinguish between domestic and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only that part of the route which takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable supply of transport within Germany.
Nor does the German tax system distinguish between resident and non-resident taxpayers.
If a non-resident taxable person transports passengers through Germany, the part of the route which takes place in Germany also constitutes a taxable supply of transport.
A non-resident taxpayer must declare his intention to provide passenger transport services to the competent tax authority before carrying out his services in Germany.
The IRS registers this non-resident taxable person (cf. 4.1.2) and issue a special certificate for any bus or coach specified in the taxpayer's notification.
The taxpayer is required to declare his taxable supplies of transport in the German VAT return.
As of 1 March 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office registered 741 Czech payers who were engaged in passenger transport.
Where the transport of passengers is supplied to a resident taxable person liable for VAT, the non-resident taxable person does not have to pay the VAT himself to the tax authority.
Instead, the entity liable to pay VAT to the tax authority and the invoiced net amount to the non-resident taxable person is the tax resident receiving the services; this process is known as reverse charge and is in accordance with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
In addition to the declaration by the non-resident taxpayer and his VAT return, the German tax authorities have a number of means of assessing the accuracy of the declared taxable supplies of passenger transport.
Customs office mobile inspection teams audit the certificates of buses with a foreign transport permit (licence) which are used to transport passengers through Germany.
After each audit, the mobile control teams send an inspection report to the competent tax authority.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile inspection group is entitled to demand payment of VAT from the bus driver before continuing onward transport.
A non-resident taxable person may deduct the VAT thus paid from the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may declare its intention to carry out an audit, which must take place in the office of the tax office, or it may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if the tax non-resident refuses to pay the amount of VAT assessed in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308/EEC.
If there is to be a review of the VAT return or the fulfilment of the obligations of a non-resident taxable person, the BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too labour-intensive in comparison with the small amounts of VAT to be paid for taxable supplies of passenger transport.
In particular, the audit of the accounts of a non-resident taxpayer entails disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration must audit foreign accounting, which means not only knowledge of a foreign language, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to require more time than a resident tax audit, but this audit is limited to those passenger transport services that take place in Germany.
On the other hand, a non-resident taxpayer is not only required to accept the right of inspection enjoyed by his national tax authorities, but also the right to have an audit carried out by other Member States in which he transports passengers.
Moreover, in any Member State in which only one supply of passenger transport takes place, the taxpayer is required to comply with all the tax obligations applicable to him in those Member States, in all the languages and on all the tax forms of those Member States.
Effective taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore entails disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in the two countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, the transport of passengers between individual EU Member States, i.e. between Member States and third countries, is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct tax on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory constitutes a taxable transaction.
If this transport is provided for the first time in Germany by a non-established payer, he is obliged to give advance notice of the provision of transport to the competent tax authority.
The tax office registers this payer and the payer is obliged to declare in Germany the taxable supplies of part of the transport in the tax return.
The implementation of the law in Germany is very time-consuming.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered with the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office are active in passenger transport.
Compared to the efforts, the tax revenue, when realised, is rather low.
Member States which collect VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT are burdened with time-consuming obligations without a financially sensitive outcome.
In order to avoid disproportionate VAT costs, the supply of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in only one Member State.
This could be the State where the transport starts or where the provider is based.
Such taxation would require an adaptation of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
VAT tax returns
Filing and processing of VAT returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to file a VAT tax return on a form prescribed by the Ministry of Finance within 25 days after the end of the tax period, even if he has not incurred a tax liability, unless the law provides otherwise.
The actual tax liability is due within the deadline for filing a VAT tax return, with the exception of the tax charged in connection with the importation of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No.235/2004 Coll., for which the due date of the tax is determined by customs regulations.
If a refundable overpayment arises as a result of the assessment of the excess deduction, the payer shall be reimbursed without request within 30 days of the assessment of the excess deduction.
The time limit is not applied in cases where the tax administrator initiates tax proceedings concerning the payer's tax obligation.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 73 para. 235/2004 Coll., the right to deduct may be exercised in the regular VAT return at the latest for the last tax period of the calendar year in which the right to deduct could be exercised.
After this period, the right to deduct may be exercised up to 3 years after the end of the tax period in which the right to deduct could be exercised at the earliest.
However, this is only possible by submitting an additional VAT return.
Amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. effective from 1 January 2004. 1st 2005 allows the filing of an additional VAT return only for the period when the right to deduct could be exercised for the first time.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT tax return if (a) by means of a summary of corrections he/she increases the tax liability, (b) he/she makes a correction in which the last known tax obligation does not change, but only the data previously claimed by the tax subject, (c) he/she corrects the rate and amount of the tax pursuant to Section 49 of Act No.235/2004 Coll.
The payer may submit an additional VAT return if the totality of the corrections reduces the tax liability.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The submission of a VAT return in electronic form may be made either via the Internet or on a technical data carrier.
Internet submissions may be made as submissions with a data message bearing an advanced electronic signature or as submissions with a data message bearing no advanced electronic signature.
In the case of filing with a data message not bearing an advanced electronic signature, filing in written form is also required, i.e. delivery of a computer report to the tax administrator (e-form).
The VAT return contains separate lines concerning the values of intra-Community supplies/acquisitions of goods.
Acquisition values of services are reported on separate VAT return lines.
Some lines are used for the purpose of the initial automated control within the ADIS system.
The values of supplies of goods to other Member States to persons registered for tax purposes in other Member States shall be compared with the data contained in the recapitulative statements submitted by the Czech payers.
The values of acquisitions of goods from other Member States from persons registered for tax purposes in other Member States shall be compared with the values obtained through VIES from the recapitulative statements of payers from other EU Member States.
The tax office is carrying out a credibility test of VAT returns under the ADIS system.
This test is carried out automatically, as VAT returns cannot be assessed without a test.
The credibility test includes the calculation of credibility criteria and the evaluation of risky types of VAT returns.
According to the provisions of Section 37 para. 337/1992 Coll., the Financial Office may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on a person who fails to comply within a specified period with an obligation of a non-monetary nature arising from this or a special tax act, or imposed by a decision pursuant to this Act.
Automated tax information system used by the FCA for technical support of tax administration.
The SAO audit revealed that the tax authorities mostly did not use the possibility to impose a fine on payers for failing to file a VAT tax return.
Filing and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between provisional monthly or quarterly VAT returns and annual VAT returns.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit provisional VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small business owners who are not subject to VAT must submit an annual tax return.
In general, taxpayers are required to submit quarterly VAT returns by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which VAT is incurred (§18 para. 2 UStG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6 136 in the preceding calendar year or in the case of a newly established business, the trader concerned is required to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day of the following month.
The taxpayer may also decide to file a monthly VAT return if there has been a tax refund in the past year that exceeded EUR 6,136 (§18 para. 2a UStG).
VAT returns need not be submitted if the amount of annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT liability must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax year in which the VAT accrued.
The refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FCA.
Deadlines (under the law) for processing tax returns and refunding excess VAT do not exist.
In order to reimburse the tax in good time, provision may be made for the amount to be reimbursed.
The basic principle is to process VAT returns and refund the tax quickly.
The German VAT Act provides for the possibility to extend this period (§ 18 para. 6 UStG).
Such an extension shall be requested separately.
It makes it possible to submit a VAT return and pay the relevant VAT liability one month later, provided that a special advance is paid in the case of a monthly return.
This advance payment will be settled against December's VAT liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the entrepreneur must submit a corrective VAT return.
There is no supplementary VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be filed by 31 May of the following calendar year, is registered with the tax office, the entrepreneur cannot correct an erroneous provisional VAT return, but only the annual VAT return.
Correction of the annual VAT return in favour of or against the payer is possible within the following 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payers are required to submit provisional VAT returns electronically.
Tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule in order to avoid undue hardship.
Filing the annual VAT return is possible in paper form or via the Internet, either with or without certification.
If it is done without certification, payers must file the return once more on paper with personal signatures.
If the payer fails to file a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In the event of late filing, a penalty payment (maximum 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000) may be imposed on the payer.
During a previous audit, the BRH found that tax authorities often do not impose this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities imposed a fine, the amount was assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
The standard fine therefore fails to meet its objective of reducing the average delay, in particular when submitting an annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values of intra-Community supplies/acquisitions of goods.
Acquisition values of services are reported on separate VAT return lines.
Tax-free transactions must be reported on a separate line of tax return/VAT.
In the case of VAT returns which are submitted on paper, a copy must be made either by means of a scanner or by staff specifically authorised to do so.
Data from VAT returns submitted electronically are immediately available to the tax office employee.
Once all the data has been entered into the system, the RMS staff will go through it and make a selection of cases that meet certain criteria.
The selected VAT returns must be checked by a tax office official on the basis of an inspection report prepared by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax authorities must make a rough estimate of the amount of VAT to be paid by the taxpayer, the estimated tax must be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, tax payers file VAT returns within 25 days after the end of the tax period.
Depending on the amount of the payer's turnover, the tax year is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month.
In Germany, payers file provisional VAT returns, depending on their tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days of the end of the calendar quarter or within a month.
By 31 May of the following year, payers are required to file an annual tax return.
The obligation to submit an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in (monthly provisional) tax returns by filing a single annual VAT return;
Where the payer corrects declared intra-Community transactions, the correction cannot be related to the period covered by the recapitulative statement;
The Länder do not normally compare VIES data on intra-Community acquisitions of German taxpayers before processing the annual VAT return.
In accordance with the registration (see. 4.1.3) German taxpayers are required to file an annual VAT return regardless of the amount of their turnover.
This obligation enables the German tax authority to examine the maximum turnover limit for small entrepreneurs.
In addition, the responsible tax office is able to compare the annual VAT returns with the direct tax returns and the closing accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax administrators are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only from the submitted income tax returns.
Unlike in the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to file VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of the obligation to file tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
In accordance with the provisions of Section 102 of Act No.235/2004 Coll., a payer who has delivered goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State shall submit a summary report (hereinafter referred to as "SH").
The information on the value of the delivered goods is always given in Czech currency broken down by individual tax entities, stating their VAT ID under which they are registered in their country.
Data on services rendered shall not be included in the TA.
SH shall be filed by payers with monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days of its termination with the locally competent tax authority.
The correction of erroneous data shall be carried out in the subsequent SH within 15 days of the date of detection of the errors.
The erroneous data entered in the SH are always replaced by the data entered in the subsequent SH.
As well as tax returns, payers can file SH in electronic form.
In the event that the payer fails to file the SH or the subsequent SH and should have filed it under Act No.235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator will ask him to file it and at the same time instruct him on the consequences in the event of failure to file the SH or the subsequent SH, i.e. that the tax administrator is entitled under Section 37 of Act No.337/1992 Coll. to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for non-fulfilment of obligations of a non-monetary nature.
The SAO audit revealed that the tax authorities mostly did not use the possibility to impose a fine on payers for failing to fulfil their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of SH submissions, taxpayers are not sufficiently incentivised to fulfil their obligations because the non-filing of SH does not affect VAT liability.
The tax administrator is obliged under § 102 para. 235/2004 Coll., to examine the data in the SH, or in the subsequent SH, to remove any ambiguities and to use the data for determining the tax liability.
In case of discrepancy between the data in the SH and the data in the respective (payer with a monthly tax period) or relevant (payer with a quarterly tax period) VAT returns, the tax administrator should verify the correctness of the declared tax obligation stated in the VAT return.
The erroneous data in the SH are removed by the tax subject by filing the subsequent SH himself or may be requested to do so.
The tax administrator shall correct the data on supplies of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system if:
the payer fails to prove the data specified in the SH (or subsequent SH) and corrects them by filing a subsequent SH,
The tax administrator has proved that the information provided by the payer in the SH or subsequent SH is not true.
By inserting a correction without filing a subsequent SH by the payer, the tax administrator does not replace the submission of the tax subject, only adjusts the data in the VIES database so that they are up-to-date, complete and accurate.
The SH data shall be sent to the Member States concerned.
They can only be sent and received by a national financial administration body, designated for cooperation with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is the CLO (in the Czech Republic this function is performed by the Ministry of Finance, the Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (CLO).
O_MCTL is an automated message that the CLO receives from other Member States.
Contains all erroneous VAT IDs listed in sent SH lines.
If an incorrect VAT ID is used in one of the transferred normal lines of the SH or subsequent SH, an entry is made in the table of incorrect VAT IDs.
The table contains the so-called "Notification of doubts regarding VAT ID."
The tax administrator checks the data and records the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is obliged to declare VAT and state the values of the acquisition on separate lines of the VAT tax return.
Selected cases of discrepancies in the value of the acquired goods declared by the Czech payer in his VAT tax return and in the value of the delivered goods as stated by payers from other Member States in their SH are sent from the CLO to the tax office for verification.
Tax authorities are obliged to investigate irregularities.
There may be three situations:
a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the respective VAT return lines is lower than the value of the supply declared by EU payers.
In this case, the tax administrator shall verify the accuracy of the data.
b) The amount of difference is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (foreign supplier corrects its SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself submits an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax administrator whether to verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT tax return despite this fact.
c) The value of acquisitions of goods from other Member States stated by the Czech tax payer in the respective VAT return lines is higher than the value of the delivered goods declared by EU payers.
Here, too, it is at the discretion of the administrator to verify the accuracy of the data.
After verifying the difference and clarifying the causes of its occurrence, the tax administrator enters the result of the verification into the ADIS.
The results of the screening are transmitted back to the CLO.
Figure 1 shows the number of cases sent from the CLO to the tax authorities for examination for each quarter of 2005. source: MF).
Figure 1 above shows that the number of cases transmitted from the CLO to the tax authorities decreased for each quarter of 2005.
A significant drop in numbers occurred in 4. 2005 quarter. The CLO has increased the minimum threshold, inter alia with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between data from VAT returns and data from the EU may not always be caused by an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error due to the fact that some types of transactions may be introduced into the SH in different ways in different EU Member States.
The most common reasons for discrepancies in the values of the reported transactions found at the audited tax authorities are set out in Table 1.
Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in Germany
Entrepreneurs who make intra-Community supplies from Germany to other EU Member States or participate in triangular transactions are obliged to file quarterly SHs listing intra-Community supplies by recipient (§ 18a para. 1 UStG).
The CA must be lodged by the 10th day of the month following the calendar quarter concerned.
If an extension of this period is granted in the case of provisional VAT returns, this also applies to the SH.
SH must be supplied by the CLO.
They must be submitted electronically from 1 January 2007.
Exemptions may be granted by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers become aware that the SH contains incorrect information, they are obliged to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not file a SH, the CLO initiates proceedings to enforce the submission of that report.
This procedure includes: - a first reminder - a second reminder with the threat of a fine/penalty payment - and - a periodic penalty payment.
Although the German Tax Code allows fines of up to EUR 25 000 (Section 329 AO), the CLO imposes fines in three steps, amounting to EUR 125, 250 and 500.
In addition, Section 26a para. Article 1 (5) of the UStG provides that payers act unlawfully if, intentionally or negligently, they do not properly file the SH, submit it incompletely, fail to file it on time or fail to correct or correct it late.
This offence may be punished by a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Data on intra-Community supplies cannot be entered into VIES by the IRS as the processing of SH is the exclusive task of the CLO.
SH data are stored only in the CLO system.
Therefore, data from the SH are visually available to the IRS only after their processing on the CLO.
The processing times for SH are laid down in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Data from the SH must be stored within three months following the corresponding calendar quarter.
If incorrect VAT IDs are entered in the SH of German payers, the CLO from another Member State will receive the O_MCTL codes.
The CLO contacts a particular entrepreneur and asks him for correct data.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case is referred to the relevant tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct data.
During the audit, the BRH found that most entrepreneurs corrected the VAT ID at the request of the CLO.
However, the challenge, threat and assessment of three additional fines takes up too much time in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the relevant tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The IRS refused to exempt declared intra-Community supplies in 73% of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the tax office asked him to file a corrected SH with the CLO, as the tax authorities cannot correct the VIES data themselves.
The BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor the CLO checked the submission of the corrected SH, so the payers often did not comply with the request.
In view of the fact that the CLO does not have access to the VAT return data, the comparison of the supply data declared in the VAT return and in the SH will not take place before the submission of these data to the CLOs of the other Member States.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied in the preparation of the VAT control.
Data obtained from other Member States shall be processed on the CLO.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and then submitted to the Member States concerned.
These data are used for acquisition control purposes by the tax authorities.
Once they have been entered into the system, the CLO checks them against data from previous calendar quarters.
Where they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information is generated and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is created later and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the assessment procedure shall subsequently cross-check this data with data on intra-community acquisitions.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who are not fully entitled to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have delivered goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State submit the SS within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter to the locally competent tax authority.
The tax authorities process the SH and transmit the data to the CLO.
The values of supplies of goods to another Member State, stated by the payer in the TA, are compared at the tax offices with the values of supplies of goods to another Member State, stated by these payers in the VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the assessment procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made intra-community supplies are obliged to file the SP on a quarterly basis by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
SH payers file on CLO, from 1. 1st 2007 in electronic form.
The information from the SH is available to the tax authorities only after its processing at the CLO.
Payers from the Czech Republic and Germany state in the SH only the delivery of goods, the provision of services is not mentioned in the SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are not able to correct the erroneous lines filed by the SH on their own.
As a result of this limited access to the data of the German VIES system, the erroneous VAT ID was not corrected even though the payer provided the SA with the correct VAT ID.
The German tax authorities do not compare the data on intra-Community supplies which appear in the VAT return of the German payer and his SH.
Differences between the data of these two reports are usually not detected before the German CLO provides VIES data to other Member States.
Given the findings of the BRH, it is clear that a comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in VIES.
In the Czech Republic, data on the supply of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their VAT tax returns.
The comparison shall be made by the CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are handed over to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in the tax returns of payers.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions.
Such general control is processed only for payers who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax authorities control the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions of other payers only if the RMS produces an inspection warning or if the payer is designated for inspection anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities of the need to explain the reasons for any difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of the RMS.
The fight against carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intra-Community acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specifically VIES, provides the tax authorities with information that may be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if the payers file SH monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs because most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to file monthly VAT returns and the SH does not require any additional information compared to the tax return.
In order to avoid bureaucratic costs, the filing of a SH may be combined with the filing of a VAT return.
However, the obligation to administer SH on a monthly basis would cause more time discrepancies between reporting intra-community delivery and intra-community acquisition and could increase the data flow between CLOs.
In 2006, the German federal government considered a general provision for monthly SHs.
Its implementation failed due to doubts of the federal states.
They were concerned that the monthly submission of VIES data to the CLOs of other Member States could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the obligation of monthly SH reporting and monthly data transmission were to be effective, a monthly update of VIES would require a European standard of monthly SH.
Statistical data on the delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany
In terms of foreign trade, Germany is the most important trading partner for the Czech Republic.
The total volumes of intra-Community transactions in goods carried out between the Czech Republic and Germany are shown in Table 2.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous VAT or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for individual quarters of the audited period.
These figures are contained in the following tables.
The figures show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was filed, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL was received.
Level 3 International Information Exchange
Implementation of international information exchange in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information enables tax administrations to obtain information from other Member States concerning intra-Community commercial transactions and the payers who have carried out such transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 distinguishes between two basic categories of information exchange, namely the exchange of information on request and the exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information on request is carried out in the form of so-called requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "REI") using standardised SCAC forms.
Tax administrators from the Czech Republic send their ŽOI or replies to the delivered ŽOI through the financial directorates at the CLO, which ensures the translation of the information provided on the standardized SCAC forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
The CLO also ensures the reception of LIs from other Member States and replies to sent LIs, their translation into Czech and distribution to locally competent tax administrators for processing.
In Art. 8 Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 provides for a maximum period of three months from receipt of the application for the processing of the RES.
The SAO audited all RUs handed over between the Czech Republic and Germany during the audited period.
Of the total number of 94 ZOIs received in the Czech Republic from Germany, 70 cases (i.e. 74.5%) dealt with within the three-month deadline, a further 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) were processed after this deadline and the remaining 1 case had not been sent to Germany by the time of the SAO audit.
More detailed information on the deadlines within which the responses received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic can be found in Graph 2.
Of the total number of 335 CIs sent from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) response received within the three-month deadline, a further 179 (i.e. 53.4%) of requests were answered after this deadline and 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) the response from Germany had not been received by the time of the SAO audit (in the remaining 1 case it was not possible to determine from the submitted data when the response from Germany had been received).
More detailed information on the deadlines within which the responses to the RTD sent to Germany were delivered to the Czech Republic can be found in Graph 3.
The percentage expression of the values of intra-community transactions reported in the ZOI transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany can be found in Graph 4.
As can be seen from the graph above, the value of commercial transactions examined through the RUs was most often in the range above EUR 60 000.
The international exchange of information without prior request takes place either in the form of automatic or structured automatic exchange of information or in the form of spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax authorities from other Member States are often provided, without prior request, with information that may be relevant to them when administering VAT.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected on the CLO.
The information shall be transmitted electronically between Member States.
According to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, "automatic exchange" means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and at predetermined regular intervals.
"Structured automatic exchange" means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax administrator from the Report on the Delivery of a New Means of Transport form pursuant to Section 19 of Act No.235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the issued tax document.
When processing the above-mentioned form, the tax administrator fills in the necessary data in a specially created template and returns them to the contact person at the Financial Directorate, where these data are collected and within the specified deadline, i.e. no later than two months after the end of the quarter in which this information was available, it shall be transmitted to the CLO for subsequent processing and transmission to other Member States.
Furthermore, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on VAT-exempt mail order sales in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU transactions that appear to be unjustified and information on potential "missing traders."
This information is sent to other Member States by spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of international information exchange in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the locally competent tax authority.
Financial authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form directly by email to the German CLO, which transmits the SCAC forms to foreign CLOs.
The tax authorities have been instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information checked by the BRH were sent in order to ensure the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in another Member State or to prove the exemption of intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it shall check the value of the supply of goods or services referred to in the request for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
Unless there is a reasonable reason for such a request, the German CLO shall reject any application containing an amount lower than that limit.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E) ] if these texts are not in German or English.
To respond to a request for information, the CLO sends a request to the relevant tax authority, indicating a three-month period.
There are no further deadlines for processing applications at specific organisational levels of the tax administration.
Although the German CLO has the technical conditions to monitor the elapsed time limits, it lacks sufficient staffing capacity to alert the tax authorities to the response to unanswered requests for information.
The tax authorities obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audits: a special VAT audit, covering any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which can cover only one transaction that has been carried out recently.
This short and flexible type of audit requires no notification to the taxpayer and has proven its usefulness in investigating individual taxable business transactions.
In the framework of automatic exchange without prior request, the FED provides other Member States with information on VAT IDs allocated to payers resident in other Member States, on the refund of input tax to payers resident in other Member States.
In addition, Germany has undertaken to provide other Member States with the following information through structured automatic exchange:
a.
