Supply of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without the use of their VAT ID, b. sending or catalogue sale in other Member States which is not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intra-Community acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d. intra-Community supply of goods which the German payer did not declare in the SH because he treated the supplies as domestic transactions, e. potential "missing trader" who carried out intra-Community transactions independently of the validity of their VAT IDs, f. entrepreneurs who supplied their VAT IDs to potential recipients, f.
Comparison and evaluation
Sending of the ZOI or spontaneous information is initiated both in the Czech Republic and Germany by the locally competent tax authorities, which send the completed SCAC form to the CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the bilingual SCAC form (Czech - English) and translates the sent information into English or German, the German tax authorities follow the instruction that they should write the ZOI or spontaneous information only in German on the monolingual form.
The German CLO does not provide translation of German texts.
Examination of the RUs transmitted in the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 31. 12. 2005 between the Czech Republic and Germany, the SAO found that the Czech tax administration dealt with 74.5% of the applications received within the three-month deadline, while the applications sent to Germany were dealt with by the German tax administration within the deadline in only 40.6% of cases.
Although the German CLO draws the attention of the tax authorities to the three-month period, it does not monitor the elapsed time limits.
Missing alerts result in a large number of delayed responses to the RES.
Due to these problems, the BRH recommended regular warnings to the CLO.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, the German CLO is now alerting the tax authorities to the answers to the unfinished responses to the FOI.
Risk management in the field of VAT
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, VAT risk management is handled by several departments at various organizational levels of the tax administration.
Within the Ministry of Finance, the following departments deal with the issue of risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
The Department of Methodology and VAT Performance, including a report on VAT Risk Management, which, among other things, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates trends in these risks at the domestic and Community level.
It coordinates nationwide the functioning of the role of the Trustworthiness of VAT returns and the use of VIES data in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intra-Community transactions.
On the basis of data from the trade balance, the Czech Republic evaluates risky commodities, conceptually processes VAT risk management and cooperates in this area with relevant EU institutions and other Member States.
The Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT, which, among other things, ensures the exchange of information in the field of VAT, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, ensures public information and ensures other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous VAT or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for individual quarters of the audited period.
These figures are contained in the following tables.
The figures show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was filed, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL was received.
The Department of Tax Control and Search Methodologies, which, among other things, performs risk analysis within the framework of methodological management of tax inspections and, in accordance with the risk analysis, sets priorities for targeting tax inspections in the plans of financial directorates, prepares risk analyses within the framework of reducing tax evasion, including the collection of knowledge gained during tax administration and from other sources, and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
Search departments are set up in the financial directorates to carry out, among other things, searches for tax entities and areas that are at risk of tax fraud (e.g. online shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), searches for unregistered tax entities for risks of tax evasion (e.g. in the field of internet services, employment mediation, radio and press services, etc.), analysis of chain fraud links and transmission of information to territorial tax authorities.
Specialised control units are set up in selected 12 tax offices.
They have a regional remit and carry out tax inspections outside the territorial remit of the tax authorities on the basis of a mandate.
The need to set up specialised tax inspection units has arisen from the increasing discovery of new and improved forms of tax evasion, which occur mainly in chain-linked entities.
These departments focus on the control of tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with specific activities and multinational companies and tax entities of a large scope of activity in terms of turnover.
The following mechanisms for limiting VAT risks have been integrated into the ADIS system: the role of the credibility of VAT returns, used to evaluate the riskiness of submitted tax returns, the role of the selection of tax subjects for inspection, allowing the selection of payers for inspection on the basis of selected criteria, the role of the VIES, through which tax administrators have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES enables, among other things: to verify the validity of VAT IDs of payers from other Member States, to obtain from other Member States the values of goods supplied to the Czech payer, declared in the SH by all its suppliers from other Member States, to generate a report of payers who have not filed a SH, to carry out a formal check of the data that the payers from the Czech Republic have entered in the SH before sending these data to other Member States, to generate a report of payers for whom the data on supplies of goods to other Member States entered in the VAT returns do not coincide with the data of other Member States from the payers in the SH.
As part of their activities to limit the risks of tax evasion, tax administrators have access to registers of state administration bodies, such as the Commercial Register, the Land Register, the Register of Motor Vehicles, the Register of Trades, etc.
More detailed information can be found in the chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federal (federal) structure of the FRG, the federal tax administration (in particular the CLO) and the tax administrations of the 16 Länder are involved in the development and operation of the RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither the CLO nor the federal tax administrations share a fully consistent database.
At the level of the Customs Duty, the ST I 2 (hereinafter referred to as "KUSS") collects the findings of a check on tax fraud in a special database called the AACC.
KUSS, in cooperation with the tax authorities, has introduced a new database called ZAUBER designed to transfer the names of tax evaders" companies to "missing traders."
KUSS coordinates related domestic and cross-border tax fraud cases.
KUSS experience is reflected in RMS development in working groups.
In addition, the specialists of several other CLO and MF services are entrusted with the duties and powers associated with the RMS.
At the level of the CLO, there is a formal control of the composition of VAT IDs of other Member States in the SH filed by German payers.
This formal check is carried out prior to the provision of SH data to other Member States in order to improve the clarity and use of the VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
Validation of the VAT IDs listed in the SH is carried out on the basis of the O_MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the procedure for correcting invalid VAT IDs, cf. also 4.4.2).
In addition, the RMS on the CLO is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and generates several types of control reports based on several characteristics usually found in so-called carousel trades in order to identify potential "missing traders."
The tax authorities of the Länder are instructed to prepare these inspection reports and, in some cases, to report on the results of their findings to the CLO.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all available characteristics if the existence of a case of tax fraud (rather than an exclusive focus on the company's turnover) is to be assumed with a sufficient degree of probability.
The BRH therefore proposed to the MF that different characteristics be taken into account in the preparation of the reports.
The RMS should also cover other factors, such as the taxpayer's payment behaviour (morality), field (economic activities) or shareholder structure.
The second level of the RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the Länder and focuses on the processing of VAT returns.
For example, the RMS generates a list of those payers who have declared intra-Community supplies in their tax returns.
This list is sent to the CLO to monitor the full SH submission.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intra-Community acquisitions, as reported in the payer's annual VAT return, with VIES data.
The tax administrations of the Länder try to avoid comparing quarterly data because such a comparison would reveal too many discrepancies which are attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
the different execution time of the intra-Community transaction in the opinion of the supplier, on the one hand, and the recipient, on the other;
Different accounting for sales discounts and sales events (incentives) and their different presentation in the tax return.
In addition to comparing data from VAT returns and VIES, many Länder have introduced elements of the RMS which are based on VAT return data and certain other facts (such as the structure of the company name, the age of the shareholders, the number of employees and the payment behaviour/morality of the taxpayer).
Bavaria has implemented a rules-based RMS which allows a team of tax fraud specialists (hereinafter risk managers) to programme their own rules for singling out potential tax fraudsters.
This RMS is applied at the moment when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT return.
The competent tax authority therefore receives the recommendation made by the RMS before determining VAT.
As this RMS is unable to reflect up-to-date findings in its activities, risk managers need to adapt the relevant rules on the basis of feedback from the tax authorities.
The administrative district of Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with tax file data in which a check revealed tax evasion.
On the basis of this data, the RMS is able to identify the characteristics of tax evasion.
The RMS draws up a monthly list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The relevant tax authorities use this list as a basis for decisions on the audit of proposed taxpayers.
Following an audit, auditors must report their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The district of North Rhine-Westphalia uses an adaptive artificial neural network which is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
On the basis of a large number of data assessed VAT returns and some other facts, this neural-fuzzy system or data-mining system calculates the probability that a particular taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then draws up a monthly list of potential fraudsters.
The local tax authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers for inspection and report the findings of the inspection to the data processing centre.
The implementation of one of these three RMS is still ongoing in the other Länder.
Given that none of the three RMS is based on an identical approach, a combination of all systems seems useful for tackling tax fraud.
It remains to be seen whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although specific RMS criteria in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and BRH found that each Member State has developed its own RMS.
Like the different approaches in the three Länder of Germany, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
The tax authorities of the EU Member States are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud - especially carousel fraud - is not proving to be a national problem, but rather a European one.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State but in several States.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
The VAT loss caused by fraud in the EU may not affect the Member State of origin of the fraud.
Any Member State involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
There should therefore be a European exchange and debate on the RMS.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
Within the framework of cooperation on the implementation of parallel auditing actions, the SAO and the BRH scrutinized the quality and use of information on selected business transactions, which were the subject of international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
Furthermore, both audit institutions jointly scrutinized the implementation of several business transactions where there were doubts about their implementation, i.e. discrepancies in the way payers from both countries reported these business transactions in their VAT or SS tax returns.
At the request of the BRH, the SAO scrutinized a total of 8 cases concerning business transactions carried out between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
In addition, in 43 cases, the SAO scrutinized, on the basis of a warning from the BRH, the values of intra-Community transactions with Germany reported by Czech payers in their tax returns and SH.
At the request of the SAO, BRH scrutinized a total of 23 cases concerning commercial transactions carried out between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 through official communication with the CLO.
The examination of selected cases revealed, inter alia, that the different registration methods in the EU Member States lead to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1st
According to the data in VIES, the Czech payer should have purchased in III. quarter 2004 from the German payer of goods worth EUR 60 500.
Since the Czech payer only declared the acquisition of goods with a value equivalent to EUR 29 869, the Czech tax authorities sent a request to Germany to verify the value of the goods supplied.
In reply to the RES received from Germany, the German side stated that in II. quarter 2004, the German payer delivered goods worth EUR 27,381 to the Czech payer, in III. EUR 31 997 in the quarter and EUR 10 276 in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The reply also showed that the VAT ID of the German payer was valid only from 28. 9th 2004, but the German CLO in 2006, following an additional application from a German payer for a certificate of validity of VAT ID, retroactively issued a certificate of validity of VAT ID from 1. 5. 2004.
The German payer repaired the SH.
On the basis of this information, the Czech payer acquired the goods.
In an inquiry to the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer, on the basis of an investigation by the tax administrator, filed additional VAT returns for individual tax periods in 2004, in which he increased the value of goods acquired from other Member States and at the same time claimed a VAT deduction when acquiring goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional VAT returns, the Czech tax authorities could not clearly determine whether the values of supplies from the abovementioned German supplier were also included.
On the basis of the SAO's request, the BRH found that the German supplier was registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, because he did not ask for a VAT ID when registering, he was only given an identification number for transactions within Germany.
Although it is usually not possible to assign a VAT ID retroactively to the payer in Germany, in this case the German tax officer assigned a VAT ID retroactively to the above-mentioned German payer on 1 May 2004.
The German CLO allocates VAT ID retroactively if the German trader has not caused a delay in allocation; for example, if the delay was caused by the CLO after the payer's application for VAT ID.
In this case, the CLO allocates the VAT ID retroactively because the trader does not need his own valid VAT ID for intra-Community supplies according to § 6 of the German VAT Act.
On the other hand, the German beneficiary does not need a valid VAT ID of his supplier in order to declare an intra-Community acquisition.
Due to these different procedures between Member States, the German Customs Duty assigned VAT ID retroactively in this particular case.
2nd
As part of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator requested an examination of the German VAT registration.
VIES indicated a registration date of 5. 3rd 2005, with the date 1 on the certificate of registration of the German payer issued by the locally competent German tax authority. 10 a.m. 2004.
In a reply received from Germany, the German authorities stated that the German tax entity had been registered since 1. 10 a.m. 2004, but the VAT ID was provided to him in Germany for organizational reasons up to 16. 2nd 2005.
When asked by the local tax administrator, the SAO found out that the Czech tax administrator had performed a VAT audit on the Czech payer for the tax period III. 2004 to II quarters. 2005 quarter.
By this audit, the tax office found that the Czech payer included services worth CZK 9,897 (EUR 314) provided to the German payer before his VAT registration (i.e. before 1. 10 a.m. 2004).
For the tax year III. In the quarter of 2004, the tax office assessed the tax subject with VAT in the amount of CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
On the basis of the SAO's request, the BRH found that the German payer was assigned a VAT ID of up to 16. 2nd 2005 when he informed the IRS about his business, which he started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office registered it for VAT retrospectively on 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the payer declared an intra-Community acquisition from the Czech Republic worth EUR 160 (approximately CZK 5,000).
3rd The Czech payer reported VAT for September 2004 and SH for III. quarter 2004 delivery of goods worth CZK 114 615 (EUR 3 642) to the German payer.
When verifying the registration of a German payer in the VIES system, the Czech tax administrator found out that his registration was valid from 11. 11th 2004, i.e. only after the delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer filed an additional VAT DAP, in which he declared the taxable amount of CZK 114 615 (EUR 3 642) in respect of domestic transactions and CZK 21 777 (EUR 692) in respect of VAT which he paid.
The SAO enquired with the locally competent tax office in the Czech Republic that the Czech payer subsequently filed an application for a retrial of the additional VAT tax return and submitted as evidence a certificate from the German tax administration stating that the German payer had been taxed since 1 January 2008. 1st The 2000s.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the registration of the German payer in the framework of the international exchange of information.
The response received from Germany showed that the German payer was assigned a VAT ID of up to 11. 11th 2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the application for a retrial.
The BRH found that in the given case there was no intra-Community acquisition of goods, because the German payer did not obtain a VAT ID until 11.11.2004.
However, the German beneficiary declared the acquisition as an intra-Community acquisition and declared the VAT on that acquisition by claiming a refund of input tax of the same amount.
However, because there would be no changes in the value of the VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the tax administrator in Germany did not correct the data in his VAT return.
The BRH also found that the name of the German payer in the ZOI was changed during the processing of the response in Germany, as a result of which two German tax entities were confused.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4th
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax authorities verified the acquisition of goods by the Czech payer in I. quarter 2005 with a value of EUR 22 686 from the German payer.
When asked by the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found out that the administrator had carried out a local investigation of the Czech payer, during which it verified that the delivery of the goods had taken place and that the Czech payer had accounted for and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not declare the acquisition of the goods in the VAT tax return because the German supplier did not provide his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number designated for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer was not registered for VAT for intra-Community transactions until 21. 4th 2005, i.e. only after the delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax administrator asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the German payer's registration certificate so that it could take steps to assess the tax if necessary.
The Czech Financial Office assessed the transaction as an acquisition of goods from a non-payer from Germany and therefore did not tax the Czech payer on the transaction.
The BRH found that, under the German legislation, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to have a VAT ID in order for an intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
The supplier only has to have the VAT ID of the customer from another Member State and be able to prove the transport of the goods to another Member State.
According to the German VAT Act, it was therefore an intra-Community transaction and VAT should be assessed in the Czech Republic.
In any event, it is important that the Czech tax authorities took note of this transaction because the supply of a machine of the stated value was not the basic business of the German supplier.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to respond to LAIs concerning intra-Community transactions with a value of less than EUR 15 000: 5.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer had in III. quarter 2004 to acquire goods worth EUR 12 561 from the German payer.
The Czech tax administrator carried out a tax inspection of the tax subject for this tax period.
In the context of international administrative cooperation, he requested the German tax authorities to verify the supply of those goods by means of a SCAC form.
The Czech payer disputed the acquisition of the goods, claiming that he had never done business with the German company and that the acquisition of those goods had not been entered in his accounts.
The German tax authorities rejected the request to provide evidence of contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents on the grounds that the turnover did not exceed EUR 15 000 and no further explanatory justifications were provided.
Since the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence for the assessment of the tax on the acquired goods, it terminated the tax inspection without a finding and the tax liability remained at its original level.
On the basis of the SAO's request, the BRH found that the German payer acted as a so-called "fiscal representative" (Section 22 a - e UStG).
The German payer declared those supplies in his annual VAT return and in the SH.
He was granted the right to exemption from delivery.
On the basis of a warning from the BRH, the German Financial Office will send to the Czech Republic the documents necessary for assessing the tax on acquired goods in the Czech Republic.
As stated in Chapter 4.6.1, responses to RTDs sent from Germany to the Czech Republic exceeded the three-month deadline more frequently than responses from the Czech Republic to Germany: 6.
The SAO found out that the Czech tax administration sent 5. 10 a.m. 2005 to Germany a request for information concerning the verification of the value of the delivered goods for 4. 2004 quarter.
The German payer declared in the SH for this period the supply of goods to the Czech payer in the value of EUR 86 307 but the Czech payer stated in the same period in the VAT return the acquisition of goods only in the value corresponding to EUR 35 314.
In response to the ZOI, delivered to the Czech Republic 9. 5. 2006, i.e. after the expiry of the processing period laid down in Art. 8 By Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German authorities stated that the application could not be processed because the German firm's operations had ceased at the end of 2005.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration did not meet the deadline for processing the ZOI, the Czech tax administration did not have the necessary documents for tax proceedings in the Czech Republic.
7th In 2005, the Czech tax authority requested, by means of a SCAC form, an examination of the supplies of cars worth EUR 1 265 554 to the German taxpayer made in III. and the fourth quarter of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.

11th
The Czech payer had in I. According to data from the VIES system, the purchase of goods worth EUR 35 716 from the German payer in the quarter of 2005, but the Czech payer did not declare this acquisition.
Since the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not carry out any activities at the company's registered office, the Czech tax administrator requested to verify, as part of the international exchange of information, how the German payer communicated with the Czech payer.
The response to the ZOI delivered from Germany showed that, according to the findings of the German tax administration, the Czech tax subject was unknown at the address communicated and that the goods had been taken over by the agreed carrier.

12.
In the context of an international exchange of information, the German tax authorities requested, by means of a SCAC form, verification of the supplies of goods and services made in III. 2005 quarter.
According to this ZOI, the Czech payer was to deliver goods with a total value of EUR 396 126 to the German payer during this period and to provide services with a value of EUR 11,885.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation of the Czech payer in order to verify this supply.
In response to the ZOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech payer had supplied the German payer with a production line including assembly.
The Czech payer delivered individual parts of the production line before the Czech Republic joined the EU and after 1. 5. In 2004, the line was assembled on the basis of an order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because he claimed to have defects.
In III. In the quarter 2005, the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11,885 for services.
The German payer accepted the invoices issued but did not recognise them and did not pay them.
The SAO also asked the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that all invoices are properly registered in the accounts of the Czech payer.
In the VAT returns for III. Only amounts which have been documented by the Czech payer and which relate to invoicing after 1. 5. 2004.
The BRH found that, on the basis of a reply from the Czech tax administration, the locally competent tax authority in Germany concluded that the transaction in question involved the supply of goods from a Czech payer to a German payer, including services for assembly.
In this particular case, the place of so-called work performance is where the production line was assembled.
Under the German VAT law, the German recipient of the supplied service is liable for VAT.
At the same time, the recipient may claim a VAT deduction on the same amount.
As there would be no changes in the value of the VAT payable by the German payer, corrections to the VAT return were neglected by the German tax authority.
13. According to VIES data, Czech payer A was to acquire a machine worth EUR 58 000 from German payer C in February 2005.
The Czech tax authority sent a request to Germany to examine this supply.
In reply to the ZOI, the German side stated that this machine had already been delivered by the German payer C to the Czech payer B in 2004, who was to return the machine to the German payer C in October 2004.
According to the information of the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but was transported to the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, the response to the request for information showed that the German payer C sold the machine to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organizational unit of German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Since the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intra-Community supply of goods.
The SAO enquired with the tax administrator responsible locally for payer B that, according to VIES data, German payer C delivered in III. quarter 2004 to the Czech payer B goods (another machine) worth 88 027 EUR.
Payer B denied this acquisition of goods, so the locally competent tax administrator from the Czech Republic sent the BOI to Germany.
According to the response to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
Further inquiries with payer B revealed that the machine worth EUR 88 027 was not in payer B's accounts and that it could be of the same type as the machine delivered by the organizational unit of German payer C to Czech payer A in February 2005.
The SAO also found out that the Czech tax administrator competent locally for payer A carried out a local investigation of this payer.
The tax administrator was in possession of an invoice from German payer C dated 7. 2nd 2005, which listed payer A as the customer of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found that payer A does not have this invoice included in the accounts.
Payer A had a leasing contract with another Czech company, the subject of which was a machine of the same type.
The handover of the machine from the leasing company took place on 9. 2nd 2005, the transport of the machine was provided by a leasing company.
The information contained in the response to the request for information was not used by the Czech Financial Office to determine the tax liability of payer A.
The BRH found that the German payer C did not deliver the machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was therefore not an intra-Community supply of goods, but a taxable supply in Germany.
For those reasons, the German tax authorities did not grant German taxpayer C the VAT exemption and corrected the information in his tax return.
German payer D delivered the machine to Czech payer B.
Under the German legislation, that supply was not taxable in Germany but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, the BRH found that the German payer C stated in his SH for I. quarter 2005 delivery of a machine worth EUR 58 000 to Czech payer A.
That supply was not examined during the tax audit carried out by the German tax authorities.

According to the information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax administrator does not currently have any information that the German tax administration has addressed the issue related to the Czech payer.
According to the available information, it was not a delivery of goods, yet the stated value is still included in the VIES system as an intra-Community delivery of goods to a Czech payer from Germany.

17th
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the German payer was to deliver goods worth EUR 11,600 to the Czech payer.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator asked for confirmation whether the Czech payer actually existed because the alleged partner of the German payer had established more fictitious companies in Germany.
During the examination of the commercial transaction, the Czech payer confirmed the acquisition of the goods to the tax office.
However, according to the Czech payer, the goods were not transported from Germany to the Czech Republic and were further sold during 2005 in Germany.
The Czech payer submitted documents for the sale of goods for January 2005.
The Czech payer was not registered as a VAT payer in Germany and did not declare or pay the tax when selling the goods in question in the Czech Republic or Germany.
All of these facts indicated tax evasion in Germany and were communicated by the Czech tax authorities to the German tax authorities in response to the FOI.
When asked by the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer had filed an additional VAT return for the fourth quarter of 2004, which included the value of the acquisition of goods from the German payer and at the same time claimed a tax deduction for the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
VAT on the sale of goods in Germany was not included in the Czech VAT return.
After a local investigation, the Czech tax administrator assessed the additional VAT return unchanged.
Under the Czech legislation, that case did not concern the acquisition of goods from other Member States because the goods had not been dispatched or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax authority therefore drew an incorrect conclusion from the on-the-spot investigation.
The BRH found that the German tax authorities immediately corrected the German tax payer's tax return and demanded from him VAT in the amount of EUR 1 600 after receiving a reply to the ZOI stating that the goods had not left Germany.
In addition, the competent tax office sent a warning to the tax office of the actual recipient of the goods to ensure that the resale of those goods was correctly taxed.

18.
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech payer had acquired a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German payer in February 2005.
The application was accompanied by a copy of the VAT registration certificate of the Czech payer.
A copy of the passport of the person who was to carry out the transport of that car was also attached.
An investigation by the Czech tax authority found that it was a stolen passport, the person named in it did not import any vehicle into the Czech Republic and denied all contacts with the German tax authority.
The VAT registration certificate, a copy of which was sent by the German side, was never issued by the Czech tax administrator.
This information was included by the Czech tax authority in the response to the ZOI together with the statement that it could not confirm the acquisition of the goods - the car in question.
When asked by the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found out that the Czech payer was not registered at the address listed in the Commercial Register and the company's manager was uncontactable.
After carrying out the charging procedure for the February 2005 tax period, the Czech tax administrator assessed the Czech taxpayer with a tax liability of CZK 0.
Further investigation by the Czech tax authorities revealed that the car in question had been sold to another Czech entity, which had purchased it through an advertisement on the internet.
The BRH found that the locally competent German tax authority, on the basis of the Czech response to the ZOI, would not grant the German payer the right to VAT exemption for this supply.
19. During the inspection, the German tax office was unable to clarify the difference of 3000 euro between the value of the goods acquired declared in the payer's tax return and the value provided from another Member State.
It was stated that the Czech payer was to deliver during the fourth quarter of 2004 to I. quarter 2005 to the German payer of goods worth EUR 89 424.
Since the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the VIES data, the German tax authorities requested verification of the supplies and their payment in the context of the international exchange of information.
In reply to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the sole managing director of the Czech company was removed from the Commercial Register on 8. 7th 2005 and the new manager was not registered.
It appears that the German consignee of the goods was related to a partner in the Czech company.
The Czech payer filed VAT and SH tax returns, which were signed by an unauthorized person - the company partner - after the executive was deleted from the Commercial Register.
The Czech payer's accountant confirmed to the tax administrator that the company's partner had deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
Cash documents were not issued.
When asked by the local tax authority, the SAO in the Czech Republic found that the tax authority had recognised the Czech taxpayer's entitlement to VAT exemption on supplies of goods to another Member State in the amount of CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42,145) for the fourth quarter of 2004 and for I. quarter 2005 in the amount of CZK 1 416 180 (EUR 47 548).
The BRH found that the tax authority in Germany did not correct the German purchaser's VAT return because a German judge had confirmed the German payer's insolvency in the meantime.
Since an earlier inspection revealed no evidence of tax fraud, it will not be possible to recover the tax charged.
20. According to VIES data, the German payer acquired goods worth EUR 4 251 196 from the Czech Republic in 2005 after acquiring goods worth EUR 43 274 in the previous year.
In neither the 2004 tax return nor the 2005 tax return did the German payer declare an intra-Community acquisition.
Moreover, it did not declare adequate supplies.
Because of these differences, the German tax office sent the RES concerning 4. quarter 2005 and 1. 2006 quarter.
The Czech supplier reported intra-Community delivery of goods to the German payer for these two quarters with a total value of CZK 167,246,083 (EUR 5,615,299).
On 6. 9th 2006 was delivered to the ŽOI, in which the German side asked to examine whether the intra-community supplies declared by the Czech payer had been carried out.
In response to this request, the Czech tax administration stated that the German party's request could not be met because the Czech payer had no managing director.
According to the materials provided by the SAO by the relevant tax administrator, on 30. 3rd In 2006, a protocol was drawn up with the manager of the Czech payer on the start of the VAT inspection for the fourth quarter of 2004 and January to December 2005.
At the same time, the payer was asked by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the above-mentioned periods, but he did not submit any documents.
According to the Commercial Register, the sole director of the Czech payer ceased to hold office as of 16. 5. 2006, no new manager has been appointed.
As of April 2006, the Czech payer stopped submitting VAT returns.
As part of the audit, the SAO, in cooperation with the BRH, scrutinized several cases of intra-Community supplies made between the Czech Republic and Germany, which had not been the subject of prior exchange of information between the tax administrations of both countries.
Information on the cases examined was exchanged between the two SAIs through the CLOs of both countries.
21st A Czech company (eCR) which is not resident in Germany has informed the competent tax authority (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out a taxable transaction in Germany.
Because of this information, the company had been registered since June 2005, but had not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) accepted an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of a number of wind farms and the delivery of those wind farms in the name, at the risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to a lack of own capacities, the Czech company handed over part of the order to the German payer (eD), which is based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relations and the mode of transport of wind farms:
According to the German legal situation, the place of those transactions must be determined as follows:
The Danish entrepreneur (eDK) sent the wind farms for assembly under his own name, at his own risk and on his own account to Austria.
Since the assembly of that supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind farms is taxable in Austria.
Since the carrier was instructed by the Danish contractor (eDK) and the transport was carried out under his name, at his risk and on his own account, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport started in Germany.
Although the wind farms were dispatched to another Member State and the consignee is a registered payer from another Member State, the supply of a German subcontractor (eD) could not be exempted because another Member State of destination is different from another Member State of residence of the Czech company.
That supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted input tax in its tax returns.
The place of delivery to the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of transport.
The transport of some wind farms started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
The delivery of wind farms that are produced in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
The supply of other wind farms that are produced in Germany took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) made both intra-community delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intra-community delivery from Germany to Austria.
The BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not declare any intra-Community acquisitions or submit SH to the German CLO in its VAT return in Germany.
So it is possible that the Czech society reported all intra-community deliveries uniformly as intra-community deliveries from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that (eCR) showed no intra-community delivery to Austria, but intra-community delivery to Denmark.
An examination of the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), even though this case shows no evidence of tax fraud or evasion.
Furthermore, the SAO and BRH examined the transactions in order to point out the differences between the reporting in the tax return and the VIES data, which were caused by the different VAT legislation in 2004.
The audited cases also demonstrate that changes in the legal regulation need time for the application of new legislation into practice by payers and tax authorities:
22. In SH for II. until the fourth quarter of 2004, the Czech payer declared intra-Community delivery to the German payer in the total value of CZK 792,977,452 (EUR 25,197,885).
During the same period, another Czech payer declared intra-Community delivery to another German payer in the SH with a total value of CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576,970).
According to the information provided by the SAO from the BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers listed the above-mentioned deliveries in the SH in accordance with the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., in force in 2004.
Further examination of the above transactions revealed that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the legal regulation of the supply or purchase of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic, payers reported the supply of electricity in accordance with the valid wording of Act No.235/2004 Coll. as an intra-Community supply of goods, from the point of view of the German legal regulation in force in 2004, it was not an intra-Community acquisition, but a taxable supply with a place of performance on the territory of Germany.
The difference in legal regulations was eliminated in the Czech Republic by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll., which amends certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1 January 2004. 1st 2005.
23rd When examining selected intra-community transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was also found that the Czech payer reported in the SH for 1 to 4. quarter 2005 intra-community delivery to the German payer in the total value of 240,411,163 CZK (8,071,823) and another Czech payer declared intra-community delivery to the German payer in the same period in the total value of 263,470,776 CZK (8,846,050 EUR).
According to the information provided by the SAO from the BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No.235/2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2004. 1st 2005, in the case of the supply of electricity, the place of performance is the place where the customer has his registered office, place of business or where he has an establishment for which the goods are supplied.
Therefore, the Czech payers should not have mentioned the supply of electricity to the SH in 2005.
By the fact that both of the above-mentioned payers reported intra-community supply of electricity in the SH, the data in VIES were distorted by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917,873).
Conclusion
The cooperation met the objectives of the BRH and the SAO.
Both SAIs gained a deeper knowledge of VAT administration systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed the differences between the two systems and showed that the VAT administration legislation differs.
Suspected cases of intra-community transactions have been identified during parallel controls.
Some of them make sense to check out afterwards.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs made recommendations concerning VAT administration.
The follow-up of these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
The new experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation of both audit institutions are the basis for the successful implementation of the following VAT administration audits.
Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the Outcome of International Cooperation in Excise Duty Administration Inspections between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
The submitted joint report informs on the course and outcome of international cooperation in parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, focused on the administration of excise duties in the period after the accession of both countries to the European Union.
The cooperation was implemented on the basis of a control cooperation contract concluded in February 2006.
The topic of parallel controls was chosen with regard to a fundamental change in the system of collecting excise duties, which occurred in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union as of 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the internal market of the European Union requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow goods free of tax to circulate until the date of their delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows the movement of goods under fiscal supervision under a duty suspension arrangement.
The system places great demands on tax administrations and foresees close interaction between the competent administrations of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in excise duty administration checks for the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Inspection number: (Czech Republic) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject of the audit: (Czech Republic) Excise Tax Administration (CR) Procedure of customs authorities in the administration of excise taxes
On 8 February 2006, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO-CR) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO SR) concluded a "Contract on Cooperation in Audit Activities."
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel audits "Administration of Excise Taxes," included in the 2005 Audit Plan of the SAO-Czech Republic under No. 05/34, and "Control of the procedure of customs authorities in the administration of excise taxes," included in the 2006 Audit Plan of the SAO of the Slovak Republic under No. 48/11.
Parallel controls were coordinated controls.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information that the contracting parties could not obtain during the inspection of the administration of excise duties on their national territory and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the inspections within the meaning of the European implementing directives for the implementation of INTOSAI audit standards - Directive No 31.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the audit was carried out by groups of auditors from the State Budget Department and from the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, Southern Bohemia, Western Bohemia, Northwestern Bohemia, Northeastern Bohemia, Southern Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia in the period from 7 February to 2 June 2006.
The audit involved 27 inspectors.
The audited bodies were the General Directorate of Customs (hereinafter referred to as "DGC") and 11 tax authorities.
Within the DG, 12 selected customs offices were audited out of a total of 54.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 in the period from 13 February to 2 June 2006.
The audit involved 8 auditors.
The aim of parallel controls was to examine the procedure of customs authorities in the administration of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation was focused on the procedure of tax administrators in the supervision of the transport of goods subject to excise duties, in particular on the registration of commenced and completed transports under the regime of conditional exemption from tax, and on the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between excise administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
2nd Administration of excise duties
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was carried out by the tax authorities until 31 December 2003.
Since 1 January 2004, this agenda has been taken up by the customs authorities, which have hitherto levied excise duty only on importation.
In the Czech Republic, mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty.
The revenue of the state budget from excise duties in the Czech Republic totalled CZK 82.8 billion in 2004. CZK and state budget revenues from taxes and fees in the amount of CZK 424.7 billion Excise duties accounted for 19.5% of CZK.
In 2005, the revenue of the state budget from excise duties amounted to EUR 103.6 billion. CZK and the share of state budget revenues from taxes and fees in the amount of CZK 460,4 billion CZK was 22.5 %.
In 2004, the revenue from excise duty on mineral oils to the State budget amounted to 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it amounted to 90.9 %.
Difference from 100% of EUR 13 billion CZK in 2004 and 6.9 billion CZK CZK in 2005 was the income of the State Fund for Transport Infrastructure.
The administration of all excise duties in Slovakia has been carried out by the customs authorities since 1 May 2004, with the exception of excise duties on mineral oil, which they have been administering since 1 May 2004. 1 January 2002.
Until then, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the tax authorities.
Mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products are subject to excise duty in Slovakia.
In 2004, the revenue of the state budget from excise duties in Slovakia totalled CZK 43.4 billion. Sk and total tax revenues in the amount of CZK 209.5 billion Sk accounted for 20.7% of excise duties.
In 2005, the revenue of the state budget from excise duties was EUR 50 billion. Sk and total tax revenues in the amount of CZK 222.6 billion Sk accounted for 22.5% of excise duties.
Chart No. 1 - Comparison of revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic with revenues from excise taxes
The legislation in both countries is based on European Union legislation in this area, in particular: - Council Directive 92/12/EEC on the general arrangements for products subject to excise duty and on the holding, movement and monitoring of such products (hereinafter referred to as "Directive 92/12/EEC"); - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 2073/2004"); - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the movement of products subject to excise duty under suspension of excise duty (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 3649 of the Community (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 2719/92").
The basic legal regulation regulating the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No.353/2003 Coll., on Excise Duties, as amended, (hereinafter referred to as Act No.353/2003 Coll.) effective from 1 January 2004.
When administering excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the customs authorities are bound, among other things, by the following generally binding legal regulations: - Act No. 98/2004 Coll. on the excise duty on mineral oil in the form of non-sweeping regulations (hereinafter referred to as Act No. 98/2004 Coll.), - Act No. 104/2004 Coll. on the excise duty on wine in the form of non-sweeping regulations (hereinafter referred to as Act No. 104/2004 Coll.), - Act No. 105/2004 Coll. of the Act No. 106 of the Act No.
2.1 Movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty between Member States of the European Union
The conditions governing the movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty are laid down in Title III of Directive 92/12/EEC. 15 to 20.
Under those provisions, the transport of those goods may be carried out only by an authorised warehousekeeper, who means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to manufacture, process, hold, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
A consignee in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or an operator without the status of authorised warehousekeeper but who may not store or redispatch such products under suspension arrangements.
An authorised warehousekeeper in the Czech Republic and Slovakia means a tax warehouse operator, an economic entity is an authorised consignee for repeated or one-off receipt of products subject to excise duty.
Under Directive 92/12/EEC, the movement of products subject to excise duty under suspension of excise duty is possible only with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be drawn up by the consignor in four copies before the start of the transport, unless the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch require a further copy.
2.2 Procedure for commencing and terminating the transport of goods under the conditional exemption regime between the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for commencing transport is governed by the provisions of Section 25 para. 353/2003 Coll., which states, among other things:
The tax warehouse operator must inform the customs office which is competent locally for the tax warehouse from which the transport is to start before transport of the selected products begins;
the transport of the selected products may commence only with the agreement of that customs office.
The customs office shall issue approval for the transport of selected products without delay after the condition of securing the tax is met...
The consignor in the Czech Republic may start the transport of all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the locally competent customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the commencement of transport only if a tax guarantee equal to the tax attributable to the transported products is provided.
The consignor is obliged to draw up an accompanying document in five copies before the start of the transport.
The customs office shall indicate on the accompanying document its agreement to the start of transport.
Copy No 1 shall be retained by the consignor, copies Nos 2, 3 and 4 shall be surrendered by the consignor to the carrier and copy No 5 shall be retained by the customs office authorising the transport.
Under Slovak law, the consignee retains copy No 2 of the accompanying document in Slovakia. Copies Nos 3 and 4 shall certify receipt of the products and shall be presented to the competent customs office.
Copy No 3, endorsed by the customs office, shall be sent to the consignor no later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which the products were received.
Copy No 4 shall be kept by the customs office of the consignee.
Transport is completed upon receipt of the products by the consignee.
The release of the tax security shall be decided by the customs office in the Czech Republic which authorised the start of the transport within 5 working days of the submission of copy 3 of the accompanying document, which shall be confirmed by the consignee and the Slovak customs office.
Chart No. 2 - Circulation of the accompanying document in transport started in the Czech Republic and finished in Slovakia
Transport from Slovakia
Until 31 December 2005, the procedure for transporting ethyl alcohol and tobacco products from Slovakia to another Member State of the European Union was regulated as follows:
According to the provisions of § 26 para. 105/2004 Coll.
"When transporting a lie from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorised recipient, or to a tax agent in the same member, you will send it to the consignor (supplier) obliged to send a copy of the first dielu of the original document electronically or by fax to the Cold Office of Poprad on the day of the start of the transport; this copy is required to be sent to the customs office in writing within the fifth working day of the beginning of the transport.
According to the provisions of § 22 para. 106/2004 Coll.
"When transporting tobacco products from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorized consignee, or to a tax agent in the same member state, send them to the consignor (supplier) on the day of the start of the transport to send a copy of the first dielu of the original document electronically or by fax to the Cold Office of Poprad; this copy is required to be sent to the customs office in writing within five days.
When transporting other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) between 1 May 2004 and 31 December 2005 (hereinafter referred to as the "supervised period"), the tax subject was not obliged to notify the Poprad Customs Office or the competent customs office of the commencement of transport under the conditional exemption scheme.
The tax administrator learned about the transport of these products only during the local investigation or during the tax inspection from the accompanying documents and from the accounting documents of the tax entity.
The consignor in Slovakia is obliged to draw up an accompanying document in four copies before starting the transport.
Copy No 1 shall be retained by the consignor (for the transport of alcohol and tobacco products, a copy of Copy No 1 shall be sent electronically or by fax to the Poprad Customs Office and the competent customs office).
Copies Nos 2, 3 and 4 shall accompany the goods being transported.
Under Czech law, the consignee in the Czech Republic keeps copy No 2 of the accompanying document issued by the consignor in Slovakia and confirms receipt of the products on copies Nos 3 and 4.
Confirmed copies no. 3 and 4 shall be sent no later than the first working day after completion of the transport to the locally competent customs office in the Czech Republic.
The customs office shall keep copy No 4 and return copy No 3, verifying its accuracy and validity, to the consignee.
The consignee shall send the certified copy No.3 no later than the next working day after its receipt to the consignor in the Slovak Republic.
Transport in Slovakia is considered to have ended on the date of receipt of the products by the consignee.
The sender shall prove the termination of the transport by submitting copy no. 3 of the accompanying document confirmed by the recipient and the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
Chart 3 - Circulation of the accompanying document during transport (ethyl alcohol and tobacco products) started in Slovakia and finished in the Czech Republic
In 2006, amendments to all Excise Tax Acts were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under the conditional exemption regime is obliged to send a copy of copy 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of the locally competent consignor before the start of transport.
The document proving that the transport of ethyl alcohol and tobacco products has ceased shall be copy No 3 of the accompanying document, endorsed by the consignee and his competent tax authority.
Copy No 3, endorsed by the consignee, shall constitute proof that the transport of mineral oils, wine and beer has ceased.
A certificate from the tax authority of another Member State of receipt of those goods by the consignee shall be required where that authority is required, under the legislation of the Member State concerned, to endorse copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Records of commenced and completed transports kept by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
A single electronic system is not in place to monitor the movement of goods under suspension of duty between the Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on computerising the movement and monitoring of excisable products requires Member States and the European Commission to implement, as from 1 July 2009, an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) to enable excise authorities in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the movement of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently used only in paper form, and will contribute to simplifying the movement of goods under suspension arrangements and to ensuring more effective control of the movement of untaxed products within all Member States.
The national transport databases of each Member State will be part of this system.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transports started and finished on the territory of the Czech Republic in the module Register of Selected Products (hereinafter referred to as "EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have on-line access to the system.
In the case of transports carried out only on the territory of the Czech Republic, tax administrators may obtain information on the commencement or termination of transport immediately after registration of the accompanying document by the customs office in the EVV.
The customs office shall release the security of the tax on the transported products provided by the consignor at the time of registration of the end of the transport by the customs office to the consignee competent locally.
Customs offices in Slovakia use a database based on SysNed application software, which ensures the automation of their activities in the administration of excise duties and communication with European Union systems.
By registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorised recipient in the SysNed application software, this information is automatically transferred to the System for Exchange of Excise Data database (hereinafter referred to as "SEED").
3rd Preparation and conduct of cooperation
The first coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO-Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO SR, at which a specific procedure for cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties was discussed, took place in January 2006.
Both parties became acquainted with the legislation on excise duties and the organisation of excise duty administration in both States.
Special attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia in permitting or initiating and terminating the transport of products subject to excise duty under the regime of suspension of excise duty and the exchange of information between excise administrations of both countries.
At the meeting, it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak parties would: - process overall data on the quantity of products subject to excise duty transported from the Czech Republic to Slovakia and vice versa, the transport of which started in the audited period, - compare data on the transport of mineral oils - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and alcohol - Combined Nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 under the duty suspension regime initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in Slovakia and vice versa in November 2004 and September 2005.
During the inspections, the periods examined were extended to include October and November 2005 and the transport of tobacco products under suspension of duty was also checked during those months.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total quantity of products subject to excise duty that were transported under the conditional exemption regime between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the audited period.
4th Comparison of registers of transport of goods under suspension of tax
The SAO-CR handed over to the Slovak side a database of transports completed in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5,876 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 5,738 items concerned mineral oils, 134 items of alcohol and 4 items of tobacco products.
The SAO SR handed over to the Czech side a database of transports completed in the Slovak Republic, which contained a total of 3,319 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 696 items concerned mineral oil, 2,066 items of alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The SAO-CR compared data on transports listed in the register of commenced transports in the Czech Republic with data on completed transports registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are shown in Table 3.
The data on transports in November 2004 and September 2005 were compared by the SAO-Czech Republic with the database of the Slovak Customs Administration, which was handed over by the SAO SR at the beginning of the audit.
The database did not contain data allowing a reliable reconciliation of individual services and therefore only 63% of the services started were allocated.
Individual transports were assigned according to multiple data, e.g. consignor, consignee, date of transport, quantity of products transported.
Data on transports started in the Czech Republic and finished in the Slovak Republic in October and November 2005 were compared by the SAO-Czech Republic with the database of the Slovak Customs Administration, which contained all data according to accompanying documents, on the basis of which 93% of the transports started were clearly assigned.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the quantity of mineral oils were given in litres or in tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
The quantity of alcohol was in most cases expressed in litres, but it was possible to convert it into litres of absolute alcohol on the basis of the percentage of alcohol indicated in the database.
The quantities of tobacco products were given in pieces, thousands of pieces and kilograms according to the type of tobacco products.
In the case of transports started in the Czech Republic, the termination of which could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database or for which the information on the quantity of products transported did not match, the accompanying documents were checked.
The documents accompanying 487 shipments of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were scrutinized.
The audit of these documents was performed at the customs offices where the SAO-CR performed the audit.
For transport authorised by other customs offices, the accompanying documents were requested through the DG.
The Czech side asked the Slovak side to verify the implementation of 141 shipments for which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic did not provide certified copies No. 3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products stated on the accompanying document did not match the quantity of products listed in the database.
Furthermore, data on transports registered in the Slovak database were transmitted to the Slovak side, but not contained in the transport database of the Czech Customs Administration.
The SAO SR searched the database of the Slovak Customs Administration for 95 shipments.
The remaining 46 shipments were requested to be verified by the locally competent customs authorities, who provided copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak side provided the Czech side with copies of the accompanying documents, on the basis of which the transports were also identified in the Czech database, with the exception of transports carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of commenced transports.
The follow-up of these cases revealed:
- 11 transports of alcohol in a total of 276.7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 transports of alcohol in a total of 404.66 litres of alcohol carried out in 2005 were registered in the Slovak transport database.
The SAO-Czech Republic found that it concerned the transport of taxed products, for which the sender does not need the consent of the tax administrator.
The sender informed the tax administrator in writing about the start of the transport. It carried out the transport on the basis of accompanying documents used for the transport of products under suspension of duty;
- a total of 94 transports of mineral oils, Combined Nomenclature code 2710 11 21, were registered in the Slovak Transport Database, with a total volume of 173 thousand litres carried out by the Czech tax entity between September 2004 and December 2005.
The SAO-CR found that between May 2004 and June 2005, the tax entity transported 102,000 litres of untaxed mineral oils without the proper authorization.
The taxable person held a special authorisation to receive and use exempt products, under which he could supply untaxed products only to the holder of the same authorisation.
It did not notify the Customs Office of the start of the transports in the Czech Republic and did not provide tax security for the transported products in the amount of CZK 1,207,680.
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the tax subject transported 71,000 litres of taxed mineral oils to the territory of Slovakia. In those cases, too, he failed to fulfil a legal obligation by failing to notify the customs office of the start of the transport operations.
The transport of products put into free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State may be initiated by the consignor in the Czech Republic without the consent of the customs office, but he is obliged to inform the customs office of this fact in writing before the transport begins.
A taxable person receiving products put into free tax circulation in another Member State is required to declare the quantity and secure the tax before withdrawing them.
Products may be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the particulars of which are laid down in Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also allows the use of an accompanying document for movement under suspension of excise duty, which must clearly indicate that it is a "simplified accompanying document for fiscal control purposes (excise products)."
The same legislation on the transport and reception of products put into free tax circulation in another Member State applies in Slovakia.
In those cases, the tax subjects transported the products put into free tax circulation with an accompanying document for transport under the conditional exemption regime, the 3rd and 4th copies of which the recipient submitted to the tax authorities in Slovakia for verification.
The customs authorities in Slovakia registered these transports in the transport database under the duty suspension scheme because the accompanying documents did not state that it was a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO SR compared the transport database of the Czech Customs Administration with the transport database of the Slovak Customs Administration and found:
- the quantities of products transported were inconsistently indicated in the databases, e.g. mineral oil was given in litres, in hectolitres or in kilograms; alcohol was given in litres or litres of alcohol, making it difficult to compare the quantities transported;
- the quantity of alcohol transported indicated in the invoices did not coincide with the quantity recorded in the databases,
- not all related invoices were listed in the databases,
- in the database of the Slovak Customs Administration were registered two transports of alcohol from the Czech Republic to Slovakia carried out in November 2004 in a total volume of 47 237 litres of alcohol, which were not in the database of the Czech Customs Administration.
The Slovak side handed over copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
The conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for the administration of excise duties were governed, until 30 June 2005, by Council Directive 77/799/EEC concerning mutual assistance by the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and taxes on insurance premiums.
On 1 July 2005, Regulation No 2073/2004 entered into force, laying down rules and procedures enabling the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office to ensure contacts with other Member States in the field of excise administration and to be responsible for the exchange of information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, the "Excise Liaison Office" (hereinafter referred to as "ELO ČR") was established at the DGC to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between the Member States of the European Union.
The tasks related to the administration of systems for controlling the movement of excise goods (SEED, ISA, EWSE) and the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and Slovakia were carried out by the ELO office at the Poprad Customs Office with effect from 1 May 2004.
With effect from 1 July 2005, the tasks of ELO are carried out by the ELO Unit (based in Poprad) of the Excise Department of the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "ELO SR").
According to the provisions of Article 3 (2). Pursuant to Article 3 of Regulation No 2073/2004, the central liaison office is responsible in particular for: - the exchange of data held in the SEED electronic register, - the Early Warning System Excise ("EWSE"), - requests for verification of movements of excise goods sent to or received from other Member States by the Movement Verification System ("MVS").
The content, scope and functions of SEED, EWSE and ISA are regulated in Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073/2004.
SEED - a system for the exchange of information on tax subjects trading in excise goods.
The system consists of national registers of excise duty payers and enables tax authorities in the territory of the European Union to ascertain whether products subject to excise duty are traded by a person authorised to do so.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States for excise purposes only.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union can obtain confirmation of the information held in that database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Act No. 98/2004 Coll., Section 39 of Act No. 104/2004 Coll., Section 46 of Act No. 105/2004 Coll., Section 40 of Act No. 106/2004 Coll. and Section 39 of Act No. 107/2004 Coll., ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, authorised recipients and tax warehouses - the SEED database.
Customs offices in the Slovak Republic contribute to the SEED database by registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorized recipient in the SysNed application software, which is automatically connected to ELO SR.
