For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, authorised consignee or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the related data is automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO SR found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Slovak Customs Administration and the Czech Customs Administration took place usually once a month, exceptionally more than once a month.
The Slovak Customs Administration received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
Data to the database SEED in the Czech Republic are transferred from the national register, in which are registered all persons authorized to dispose of products subject to excise duty and issued authorizations to dispose of these products.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Requests from customs authorities to provide information from the SEED database of other member countries are obtained only through ELO CR.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods, through which the transport of risky consignments is announced.
Transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits set by the European Commission Regulation and transport that is assessed as risky by the tax administrator are considered to be risky consignments.
The exchange of information is carried out in two forms:
- information - is sent when the specified limits are exceeded,
- warning message - is sent if the transport of goods is assessed as risky.
When evaluating the risk level of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database to send a warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data contained in the accompanying document.
In case the data in the SEED database does not match the data in the accompanying document (e.g. the registration number of the consignee of the goods or the registered office of the consignee does not match), ELO SR draws up a warning message which it sends to the ELO office of the consignee's Member State.
In drawing up the reports, the ELO is governed by the regulations of the Taxation and Customs Commission CED 317 and CED 457, which determine, inter alia, the type and quantity of goods in the relevant units of measurement for drawing up the information and warning reports.
In the audited period of ELO SR, ELO CR sent one warning message.
In the Czech Republic, information on commenced shipments of products exceeding the specified limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database during transport approval.
If the tax administrator in the Czech Republic evaluates the consignment as risky on the basis of its own analysis, it prepares a so-called warning message, which it sends to the relevant Member State through ELO CR.
In 2005 ELO CR sent two warning reports to ELO SR.
The ISA - the system for controlling the movement of goods - makes it possible, by means of ISA applications, to control individual movements of excise products as well as the control of a specified route of transport between the operators mentioned in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information takes place on the basis of a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system shall be used in particular in cases where the consignor accepts the certified copy No 3 of the movement document and requests, for example, a refund of excise duty, and in cases where the information contained in the movement document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
In the audited period ELO SR sent 33 ISA applications to ELO CR.
ELO CR sent 25 ISA requests to ELO SR.
Customs authorities in the Czech Republic most often checked the data contained in the accompanying documents, in particular the quantity of products received or dispatched or whether the consignor of the products listed in the accompanying document was entitled to dispose of products subject to excise duty if this fact could not be verified in the international SEED database.
The ISA application received was forwarded in both countries to the customs offices with territorial jurisdiction for the consignee or consignor of the products subject to excise duty.
The customs authorities examined the data requested and communicated the outcome of the investigation via ELO to the other Member State.
6th Summary
The cooperation of the SAO-Czech Republic and the SAO SR made it possible to compare the basic legislation governing the area of excise duties in both countries, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the initiation and termination of the transport of products under the conditional exemption regime between both countries, the records of these transports and to compare the exchange of information between customs authorities within the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 Comparing the legislation governing excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, the following differences were found:
(a) the procedure followed by tax entities and tax authorities when commencing the transport of products under a duty suspension arrangement.
Transport of products under the conditional exemption regime may be initiated by a tax subject in the Czech Republic only with the consent of the tax administrator, who will authorise the start of transport on condition that the transported products have been provided with tax security in the amount of the tax applicable to them.
The commencement of transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme in the Slovak Republic is not subject to the authorisation of the tax administrator.
During the audited period, the tax subject was obliged to notify the tax administrator of the start of transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
He could start transporting mineral oils, beer and wine without informing the tax authorities.
In 2006, amendments to all Acts on Excise Duties were gradually adopted in Slovakia, according to which the consignor of goods under the duty suspension regime is obliged to send a copy of Copy No. 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office competent locally for the consignor prior to the start of transport;
(b) within the time limits for sending copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The consignee in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copies no. 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification no later than the following working day after completion of the transport.
Certified copy No. 3 must be sent to the sender no later than the next working day after receiving it from the tax administrator.
The consignee in Slovakia is obliged to send the consignor of the products copy no. 3 confirmed by the tax administrator and the recipient of the products no later than the 15th day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in Slovakia and the Czech Republic keep electronic records of shipments of products under the conditional exemption regime.
The content and method of keeping such records are not regulated by legislation in the Czech Republic or Slovakia.
Customs authorities in both countries enter in the register all data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport is carried out.
For the monitoring of the movement of goods under suspension of excise duty between the Member States of the European Union, there is currently no single electronic system allowing excise authorities in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the movement of goods.
Pursuant to Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003, an electronic system for monitoring the movement of excise products is foreseen from 1 July 2009.
On the basis of an agreement on cooperation in control activities, the Czech side handed over to the Slovak side a database of shipments of products under the duty suspension regime started in Slovakia and ended in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5 876 items concerning transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak side provided the Czech side with a database of shipments of products under suspension of duty initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in Slovakia.
The database contained 3 319 items concerning transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared data on transports listed in the register of commenced transports in the Czech Republic with the register of transports terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared data on transports of goods under suspension of tax initiated in Slovakia and terminated in the Czech Republic.
Comparability of the data was hampered by the fact that the quantities of goods transported were not reported uniformly in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to clearly attribute data on individual movements in both registers, the accompanying documents were checked and no infringements of the suspension scheme or cases of tax evasion were detected.
On the basis of the findings of parallel controls, it can be concluded that Member States can obtain valuable information from the transport register for improving the administration of excise duties.
The establishment of an electronic system for the movement and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow the electronic transmission of the movement document and more effective control of movements under suspension of excise duty within the territory of the European Union.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak.
The report was signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic.
Administration of value added tax in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the follow-up
Introductory word
Taxation is generally a key source of public revenue.
So it goes without saying that the Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) should focus their attention on this area.
An example is value added tax (VAT) fraud.
They are estimated to lose €100 billion each year in the European Union (EU).
As early as 2005, the participants of the VI EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
Within the framework of this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for supervisory cooperation as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "SAO") and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, also referred to as "BRH") carried out the first parallel audit operation in the field of VAT in 2006.
The report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not confined to a single country but is widespread across the EU, close cooperation between SAIs is needed to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the steps being taken to address this problem.
Both SAIs therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a parallel follow-up.
1st Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Administration of value added tax (D) Bilateral audit with the SAO (ex-post audit)
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the auditing operation was to examine the procedures of the financial authorities in the administration of VAT, in particular the procedure for dealing with selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany") and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The auditing operation was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and the BRH.
The intention was also to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting control findings were intended to be compared with identified good practice (if any).
The audited period covered the years 2006 to 2008, in case of relevant connections also the preceding and following periods until the completion of the audit.
2nd Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
Subsequent inspection of the VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
Suspected cases of intra-community transactions have been identified during previous parallel controls.
Some of them required further screening.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations concerning VAT administration.
The follow-up action carried out served to evaluate the actions taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspected cases.
The audit also focused on selected cases of high-risk intra-Community transactions, mutual assistance in recovering receivables and VAT inspections of large tax entities.
During the audit of VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, the auditors reached the following audit findings:
1st Recommendations from previous inspection
• Recommendation 1: Payer registration conditions should be harmonised across the EU
In previous parallel inspections, a comparison of VAT registration systems in both countries revealed differences.
As different registration methods cause problems, both SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions for the registration of payers within the EU.
This recommendation was presented at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 (hereinafter "Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003") called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including a database of VAT identification numbers.
It also amended common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
The SAIs expected EU Member States to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of the document agreed by the EU Member States in the framework of ECOFIN no longer contains this issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to regard this intention as a relevant preventive tool in the fight against VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous follow-up action recommended that all EU Member States introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements in order to allow for an earlier examination of the values of intra-Community transactions.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions reduces the period for submitting recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it was implemented from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit monthly recapitulative statements was not introduced within the deadline in line with the applicable EU rules, while in the Czech Republic it was.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany in order to improve the reliability of VIES data and to consider linking the two VAT return and recapitulative statements systems
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level Based on the results of the previous control action, both SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
Successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches need to be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, the perpetrators of fraudulent activities will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The audit revealed that our two Member States use different risk management systems, which have their strengths and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO performed an audit of the EUROCANET system, which enables the exchange of information within the EU, while the BRH focused on the German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2nd Follow-up of selected cases of intra-community transactions
During the previous auditing operation, business transactions were jointly scrutinized where there were doubts about their realization or discrepancies in the reporting of business transactions in tax returns or summary reports by taxpayers from both countries.
Both SAIs selected for follow-up nine cases involving intra-community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The inspections carried out by the tax authorities of the countries concerned had not been concluded by the date of completion of our previous joint inspection operation.
The subsequent auditing operation verified that most of the tax proceedings in connection with the above-mentioned selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany were concluded and that adequate measures were taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional assessments of VAT or prevention of refund of input tax).
3rd Control of selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
High-risk cases of intra-community transactions carried out by EU payers and included in EUROCANET were selected for inspection.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting risky taxpayers within the EU.
Member States" participation in the scheme is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active scheme member if some Member States refuse active participation.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration was not involved in the EUROCANET data exchange, it was not possible to obtain any information on which suppliers with German VAT ID were assessed as risky.
As part of the auditing operation, the SAO found cases of common business transactions as well as cases with suspected involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent conduct concerning VAT.
Tax administrations have limited possibilities to control risky transactions, in particular as regards so-called missing traders, while the mere physical examination of documents can hardly prove any fraudulent conduct to the taxpayer.
A similar situation arises for tax administrations when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intra-Community carousel trades.
In such cases, it would be advisable to ensure greater cooperation between customs and tax authorities in order to identify goods and inconsistencies in the transport documentation, as well as to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the final consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is reluctant to participate actively in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
In Germany, other tools are used to detect risky taxpayers, which have so far worked well for the German tax administration.
There is a need for communication and exchange of experience between EU Member States in this area.
The Council of the EU reached political agreement on a draft regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation is the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far from the use of EUROCANET should feed into the creation of this new network to combat VAT fraud.
4th Mutual assistance in debt recovery
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of processing requests for international assistance in the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and the BRH compared statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
Both SAIs consider it useful to renegotiate the statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent mismatches.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, SAIs agree that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to carry out an analysis on the basis of more detailed statistics to help Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the view of both SAIs, this means helping Member States with low recovery rates to increase recovery rates to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should be actively involved in this process.
5. Control of large tax entities
The SAIs analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control of large tax entities (hereinafter also referred to as "VDS") in both countries.
In addition, they collected information from tax administrations in the form of a questionnaire on areas considered by SAI to be essential for the management of this issue.
It is clear from the responses received that the situation in both countries is developing differently.
The Czech Republic has a system for guiding the selection of risk-prone cases based on a large volume of relevant data (e.g. information from tax audits, data from balance sheets and profit and loss accounts, etc.).
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
A dedicated financial authority for the management of VDS is planned to be established in 2012.
In Germany, a similar system does not yet exist, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT control in general.
To date, Germany has concentrated more on the selection of the individual cases in question, in particular on the basis of data from the VAT return and the recapitulative statement.
The analysis of these data relies on different components of risk management, which will be strengthened.
3rd Progress of control action
3.1 Progress of the auditing operation in the Czech Republic
The auditing operation was performed from May 2009 to February 2010 by Department II. - the separation of State budget revenues and territorial departments IX. Plzen, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited bodies were: Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "Czech Ministry of Finance") and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter referred to as the "FÚ"): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ in Břeclav, FÚ in Domažlice, FÚ in Hodonín, FÚ in Hradec Králové, FÚ in Cheb, FÚ in Jablonec nad Nisou, FÚ in Karlovy Vary, FÚ in Kralupy nad Vltavou, FÚ in Kraslice, FÚ ÚT Ostrava I, FÚm Ostrava III, FÚT in Píkov, FÚ in Píkov
The audit conclusion of this auditing operation was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 Conduct of the audit operation in Germany
The audit was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the Audit Service for Indirect Taxes and the staff of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
Following the selection of a sample of cases, a number of Länder were informed of the mission of the monitoring operation.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, an audit mission was carried out in the following Länder: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hesse, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
The tax files of the following tax authorities were included: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central Tax Office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, discussions were held with the Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-South) and with the financial directorates in Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
A report on the audit findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two audit institutions
In preparation for parallel audit actions, a meeting of representatives of both audit institutions took place in September 2008 to discuss and define the topics of the audit.
Finally, in December 2008, the highest representatives of the two SAIs signed an agreement on cooperation in carrying out parallel controls.
At the meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the control teams informed each other of the initial results achieved during the preparation of the control, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on the way forward.
The second meeting took place in Prague on 2. - 4 December 2009.
The review teams exchanged the findings accumulated so far and agreed on a timetable for drawing up the joint report.
In carrying out parallel audits, both SAIs decided to focus on: • follow-up of the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report, • review of selected cases of intra-Community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were not resolved during the previous parallel audit, • review of selected cases of intra-Community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were classified as high-risk cases, • review of the procedure of tax administrations in the area of international assistance in recovering VAT receivables, • tax audits of large companies.
A report on the results of the parallel control actions was prepared during a workshop in June 2010.
4th Control of VAT administration in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of the recommendations of the previous audit
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Payer registration conditions should be harmonised across the EU
Based on the results of the previous auditing operation, the SAO recommended modifying the conditions for VAT registration and introducing a new rule for deregistration in the Czech Republic.
The revised conditions should make it possible to reduce the risk of possible VAT evasion more effectively.
In this context, it was found that in some cases the tax authorities did not use the right to cancel the VAT registration of payers who did not comply with obligations arising from Act No.235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as the "VAT Act").
The Czech Ministry of Finance has not yet proposed a change to the provision consisting in introducing an obligation for tax administrators to cancel VAT registration for payers in case of repeated failure to submit a VAT return.
According to the VAT Act, the tax administrator may cancel the registration of the tax payer ex officio in cases where: a) the payer has not made a transaction to the tax administrator for twelve consecutive months without announcing the reason, b) the payer fails to fulfil his obligations under this Act, c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous auditing operation, it was found that the applicable legislation allowed the FVO for Prague 1 to cancel VAT registration as of 31 January of the following calendar year to so-called non-established payers who did not incur any obligation to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
The FVO for Prague 1 often did not cancel VAT registration for these payers, as the relevant provision set an insufficient deadline for deregistration.
This problem was eliminated by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of a non-established tax payer if the tax payer did not supply any goods or services subject to tax or exempt goods or services with the right to deduct VAT in the previous calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous follow-up action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements.
The Council Directive reduces the period for submitting recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
There is also a new obligation to submit summary reports in electronic form.
The summary report must be submitted by the payer even if the services for which the place of performance is determined pursuant to Section 9 para. 1 of the VAT Act, supplied to another Member State to a person registered for tax purposes in another Member State and where the recipient of such services is obliged to declare and pay the tax.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in order to improve the reliability of VIES data This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration performs the comparison of data on intra-Community transactions reported in VAT tax returns and summary reports of Czech payers automatically in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level
Proper collection of VAT is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU's internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore a priority area and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is evidenced, inter alia, by the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, in which an external evaluator attempted to establish the difference between the eligible and actually collected levels of VAT in the 25 EU Member States (EU-25) during the period 2000-2006.
On the basis of an analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concludes that the estimated loss of uncollected VAT over this period is between EUR 90 and 113 billion, with an average of 12% of eligible VAT not collected annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was even estimated at 18%.
In the framework of international cooperation, a previous follow-up exercise noted that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO performed an audit of the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU.
Cases of risky intra-Community transactions carried out by EU taxpayers included in the EUROCANET system were selected for audit (see Chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved through the establishment of the EUROFISC network, which should improve the cooperation of the responsible authorities in a way that allows fraud to be detected from the outset.
This network should later become an important source of information for the risk assessment of intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council already approved the creation of EUROFISC on 7 October 200812, while setting out the basic principles governing the network.
EUROFISC is modelled on the EUROCANET rapid and selective information exchange system already in place, developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky commercial transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of the recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations of the first report led to the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Payer registration conditions should be harmonised across the EU
The German tax administration has set up a well-functioning system for registering taxpayers, based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance brought the scheme to the attention of the Commission in October 2007.
Improvements to the system are being made on an ongoing basis.
Currently, the questionnaire data are processed electronically and will subsequently be used for the survey as part of risk management during registration.
The Commission submitted a proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure the level of standards already reached in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
A law on the transposition of EU directives into national law was adopted on 8 April 2010.
This law contains provisions concerning the monthly submission of recapitulative statements on intra-Community supplies.
Those provisions entered into force on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements to achieve higher reliability of VIES data and consideration of linking the two VAT return and recapitulative statements systems
A joint working group composed of staff from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance was set up.
The group developed a strategy for the automatic comparison of data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
This strategy is still being discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the working group dealt with an instrument designed to optimise the control procedure for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany participates in this exchange in the framework of the so-called Risk Management Platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of such a platform and, following a written consultation of 18 October 2006, the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 Action Plan.
The members of the platform are further divided into sub-groups that deal with individual topics such as: • risk management tools, • influencing conduct, • evaluation, • updating the risk management guide.
Reports on the results of the work of these sub-groups were published in early 2010.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of VAT registration conditions and deregistration in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included an extension of existing databases within the EU, including a database of VAT tax identification numbers.
It also regulated common minimum standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
For the time being, the issue of registration and deregistration has been left to the national legislation of the EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
The BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already reached in Germany does not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached a political agreement on the draft Regulation.
The intention of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States must implement national procedures and are only obliged to inform the Administrative Cooperation Committee of these procedures.
Both SAIs regret that the Commission has failed to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, as both SAIs consider this measure to be an important preventive element in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome further efforts by the Commission in this direction.
Monthly reporting of recapitulative statements
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous follow-up action recommended that all EU Member States introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements, allowing for an earlier examination of the values of intra-Community transactions.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions reduces the period for submitting recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented by means of the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it took effect on 1 July 2010.
Germany has not introduced an obligation to submit monthly recapitulative statements according to a specified calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in line with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve higher reliability of VIES data and consideration of linking the two VAT return and recapitulative statements systems
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO performed an audit of the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU (see chapter No. 4.3).
In this area, the BRH focused on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected intra-Community transactions
The previous auditing operation jointly scrutinized the implementation of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their realization, i.e. discrepancies in the way payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their VAT tax returns or summary reports.
Both audit institutions selected for follow-up nine cases involving the intra-community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany, the audit of which was not completed by the tax administrations of both countries during the previous joint audit operation.
(1)
The Czech payer acquired at 1. goods worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer in the quarter of 2005.
This acquisition of goods was not declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return because the German payer was not assigned a VAT ID during that period, but only a tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator received information that, according to the German VAT Act, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order for an intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
Subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that on the basis of an audit carried out by the Czech tax administrator, the Czech payer filed an additional VAT return in which he declared the acquisition of goods in the stated value and at the same time claimed a VAT deduction of the same amount in this tax return.
(2)
The Czech payer had a 4. quarter 2004 to acquire goods worth EUR 12 561 from the German payer.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of these goods and did not mention them in his VAT return.
Upon request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax authorities refused to cooperate as the turnover of the transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax authority did not obtain evidence, it terminated the inspection without a finding and the tax liability remained unchanged.
Subsequently, the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator had received two spontaneous information from Germany pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German payer had invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer purchased the goods from the Slovak payer and stated this acquisition in the regular VAT return for October 2004.
(3)
The Czech payer had a 4. quarter 2004 to acquire from the German payer a passenger car worth EUR 48 500.
The Czech taxpayer did not declare the acquisition of the goods in question.
This payer has not filed VAT returns since August 2004, therefore the tax administrator assessed VAT in the amount of CZK 0 for the quarter in question.
On the basis of information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 from Germany, in March 2007 the tax administrator invited the payer to submit an additional VAT return, which the payer did not submit.
Subsequent inspection revealed that the tax administrator carried out further tax proceedings in 2007, which showed that the Czech payer had sold the car in question to a car dealership in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator issued a payment notice for the December 2004 tax period, which additionally assessed VAT on the acquisition of goods from another Member State and their subsequent sale in the amount of CZK 295 379.
By order of the Regional Court, the Czech payer was dissolved with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of enforceable executions of the taxpayer's assets, that arrears appear to be irrecoverable.
(4)
The Czech payer was to carry out the delivery of new means of transport (passenger cars) to Germany within 4. 2004 quarter and 1. 2005 quarter with a total value of EUR 198 167.
A reply to a request for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 revealed that tax-criminal proceedings were pending against the German entity in Germany.
During a subsequent inspection, the BRH obtained information that, after the completion of the tax procedure in Germany, it was demonstrably established that the German taxpayer had been involved in fraudulent activities.
Intra-Community acquisitions of goods were taxed at a value of EUR 182 424 (year 2004) and EUR 369 690 (year 2005).
The SAO found that the Czech payer was involved in carousel transactions with new means of transport.
On the basis of information from the German tax administration concerning the examination of supplies of goods, a VAT inspection was initiated at the Czech tax entity for the tax periods April, May and June 2005.
On the basis of the audit findings and information obtained during the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additionally assessed VAT for the period May 2005 in the amount of CZK 703,031 and for the period June 2005 in the amount of CZK 726,551.
5)
In February 2005, Czech payer A was to acquire a machine with a total value of EUR 58 000 from the German payer.
This German payer was supposed to deliver at 3. 2004 quarter to Czech payer B machine worth 88 027 EUR, but payer B denied this acquisition of goods.
Subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that payer B acquired the machine from a German company that had an organizational unit established in the Czech Republic.
Czech payer A did not declare the acquisition of the goods from the German payer in his VAT return.
The reply from the German tax authorities to the request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that the German payer did not make an intra-Community supply of a machine worth EUR 58 000, but a supply of goods within the Czech Republic.
Subsequently, the BRH found that, following a tax inspection, the intra-Community supply of the machine was reclassified as a domestic supply of the machine and the VAT exemption was revoked.
(6)
The German tax payer had 3. to deliver goods worth EUR 11,600 to the Czech payer in the quarter of 2004.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
Subsequently, the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator had assessed the submitted additional VAT return, which unjustifiably stated the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State, including the acquisition of goods with the stated value.
The BRH found that after receiving a reply to a request for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax authorities corrected the German taxpayer's VAT return and additionally assessed VAT worth EUR 1 600.
The continued movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany are subject to fiscal supervision.
The recapitulative report of the German payer has not yet been corrected, because corrections of recapitulative reports in Germany can only be made by the payer who submitted the recapitulative report.
(7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 as to whether the Czech tax payer acquired a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German tax payer in February 2005.
After tax proceedings for the February 2005 tax period, the Czech tax administrator assessed the Czech payer with a tax liability of CZK 0 and informed the German tax administrator that it could not confirm the acquisition of the car by the Czech payer.
Subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was cancelled for non-compliance in 2007 and the Czech tax administrator sent the documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
Subsequently, the BRH found that the German payer had changed its registered office and the new locally competent tax administrator had revoked its VAT exemption on the supply of the car in question to the Czech payer.
The German tax payer has not yet corrected the data in the summary report and has filed an appeal against the tax administrator's decision.
8)
According to data from the VIES system, the German payer supplied the Czech payer with taxes in the period from 3. 2004 quarter to 1. goods with a total value of EUR 33 205 in the 2005 quarter.
Subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that the Czech tax administrator attempted to determine the causes of differences incurred by the Czech tax payer in the acquisition of goods in the period from 3. quarter 2004 to 1. 2005 quarter.
The Czech tax payer has repeatedly filed an additional VAT return for 1. 2005 quarter.
The Czech tax administrator did not explain the difference in the value of the goods acquired in the amount of CZK 134 273 for the period 3. quarter 2004 to 1. quarter 2005, because according to the statement of the Czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture business transactions for individual quarters and therefore the tax administrator accepted the submitted additional tax returns.
(9)
The German tax payer delivered at 3. quarter of 2004 to the Czech payer of goods worth EUR 46 854.
During the same period, the Czech payer declared an intra-Community acquisition of goods worth only EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of deliveries made as part of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of the delivery of goods of EUR 31,998, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT return and the data entered in the VIES system.
Subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that after many requests from the tax administrator, the Czech payer filed an additional VAT return for the July 2004 to January 2007 tax period.
In that tax return, the taxpayer also claimed the right to deduct VAT, which left the tax liability for that tax period unchanged.
The subsequent audit verified that in selected cases of business transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most of the tax proceedings were completed and that the tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Germany took adequate measures (i.e. additionally charge VAT or avoid repayment of input tax).
4.3 Control of selected cases of risky intra-Community transactions
4.3.1 Results of the audit in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET can be an important source of information for the detection of risky entities within the Member State of acquisition.
In the Czech Republic, signal information obtained from EUROCANET was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with data on purchasers.
Since the 1st quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic has been sending data on risky transactions and tax entities acting as suppliers to EUROCANET.
Within the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system were selected for the audit.
These operators acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax administrations from other Member States were captured in EUROCANET.
As the German tax administration was not involved in the EUROCANET data exchange, it was not possible to obtain any information that would help to establish whether suppliers with a German VAT ID were assessed by the German tax administration as risky entities.
The auditing operation revealed cases of routine commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent VAT-related conduct.
Where relevant, tax administrations have used the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• Tax administrations did not reveal any suspicions of involvement in risky transactions when verifying signal information.
The tax authorities continuously monitor such tax entities for inclusion in EUROCANET.
• During the verification of risky transactions, the tax authorities did not show deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax and VAT bases in the accounting records submitted, despite finding irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or uncovering business relationships with suspect or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• Verification of commercial transactions was complicated as some taxpayers did not cooperate with tax authorities and could not be contacted.
The locally competent tax authorities mostly examined risky tax entities and risky transactions identified in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax administrations have limited possibilities when examining risky transactions, in particular in relation to the examination of missing traders , and only a physical check of documents makes it difficult to prove fraudulent conduct to the tax subject.
Stricter VAT registration requirements and more flexible deregistration would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of tax subjects involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT registration takes place for the purpose of reporting fictitious supplies of goods within the EU or for the purpose of issuing formally correct tax documents to payers who improperly deduct input VAT on the basis of them.
In cases where tax authorities are suspected of being involved in carousel and other fraud and where goods are imported and exported from third countries, greater cooperation between customs and tax authorities should be ensured.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help to identify goods and inconsistencies in the transport documentation and to monitor the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the final consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in EUROCANET was assessed by the European Parliament at the end of 2008 as a weakness of the system which should be addressed by setting up a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Results of the audit in Germany
The BRH analysed the information available at the Federal Central Financial Office, which contained data from EUROCANET.
These figures were a criterion for the selection of six German taxpayers" files for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, has refused to participate actively in EUROCANET.
Germany thus has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but is only the recipient of EUROCANET data.
The justification for this position is contained in the following statement:.in the government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
There is currently no legal basis for breaching the applicable rules on the confidentiality of tax information.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on how such data are used within EUROCANET by other Member States.ç17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has carried out analyses of EUROCANET data and forwarded them to the Länder tax authorities in accordance with an agreed procedure.
The German tax authorities receive control information on the direct business relationships of payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in EUROCANET.
However, the German tax authorities do not receive any information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relationships with traders from other Member States who also have business relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
As a result, control in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences in the detection of VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
The tax administrations of both countries have a number of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to establish a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The Council of the EU reached a political agreement on a draft regulation, the main contribution of which lies in the establishment of EUROFISC.
The experience gained from the use of EUROCANET data should also be part of the envisaged VAT fraud network.
Member States should therefore communicate their experience at European level.
On the other hand, the cases brought before the courts at national and European level show that a discussion between the Member States and the Commission on the conditions for tax exemptions in intra-Community transactions seems necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for debt recovery
4.4.1 International assistance in the recovery of receivables in the Czech Republic
The basic arrangements for international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU are in particular the following directives:
• Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44/EC amending Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and customs duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94/EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive 76/308/EEC was implemented by Act No 252/2000 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims.
After the adoption of Council Directive 2001/44/EC, it was necessary to implement this Directive into the Czech legal order and at the same time to amend Act No 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims, was adopted.
A new regulation in the system governing international cooperation for the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU is Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28. 11th 2008
The Annex to the Regulation sets out the new application models to be used from 1 January 2008. 1st 2009, the obligation of electronic communication and the obligation of the requesting authority to confirm the conformity of the documents sent with the original document are newly laid down.
Key principles for the provision of international cooperation in the recovery of claims:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance shall always be provided only on the basis of a request containing the prescribed particulars;
3. the assistance does not cover financial claims which have the character of a criminal sanction in the requested State;
4. the provision of international recovery assistance shall be carried out in accordance with the domestic law of the State requested;
5. foreign claims do not have priority in recovery;
6. assistance shall be provided only for the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. the principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has unsuccessfully used all available means to recover a claim under its law).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. defines three forms by which assistance is implemented, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
The locally competent tax authority shall electronically send a request for information, a request for delivery or a request for recovery of claims together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance via the Financial Directorates.
The Czech Ministry of Finance shall arrange for the translation of the application into the relevant language, scan it, including the attachments, and send it via the CCN/CSI network to the competent tax authority of the designated State.
There are two basic requirements for recovery: the claim must be more than EUR 1 500 and not more than 5 years old.
If those requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse recovery.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
When receiving an application from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm receipt of the application as soon as possible and within seven days at the latest.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to grant the request, it shall inform the requesting authority of the reasons for the refusal and indicate the specific provisions of the Directive on which it relies.
Such notification shall be sent no later than three months after the date of acknowledgement of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the application, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify that the application meets all the requirements under the law and should immediately forward the application via the Financial Directorate to the locally competent tax authority for processing.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax administrator examines, among other things, the debtor's assets, e.g. by obtaining extracts from the Land Register, checking accounts in banks, verifying the registration of vehicles at the Transport Inspectorate, etc.
After a period of six months from the date of acknowledgement of receipt of the request, the Czech Ministry of Finance should inform the requesting authority of the outcome of the investigation carried out to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities where recovery is not possible, the applicant authority should also be informed thereof.
Any sum recovered by the tax administrator shall be transferred to the applicant authority in CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not excluded that a Czech tax administrator recovering foreign receivables may allow a delay in its payment or payment in instalments if the consent of the state which requested the recovery is given.
During the period of enforcement, the debtor is ordered to pay interest or penalties in accordance with Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
Such interest or penalty shall be due to the State which requested recovery.
In the case of accepted requests for recovery, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not forward the requests for processing to the locally competent tax administrators in time, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the framework of international assistance in the recovery of receivables as well as in the case of requests received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The auditing operation revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not proceed in accordance with Act No. 191/2004 Coll. because it did not inform the locally competent authority of the Member State about the progress in recovery within six months from the date when the request was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistical data
In accordance with the provisions of Section 13 para. 191/2004 Coll., processes statistical data for the European Commission by 15 March each year, indicating the number of requests for information, delivery or recovery sent or received in the past year, indicating the amount of claims to which the requests relate.
On the basis of the evidence provided by all EU Member States, the European Commission draws up a report on the state of recovery and submits it to the Council of the EU and the European Parliament.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistical data as a result of an error in the item of recovered receivables in 2008 by EUR 5,250 thousand, stating the incorrect value of the recovered receivable on VAT (it was a shift of the decimal point after conversion of the receivable from Czech crowns to the value in euros).
This error was subsequently reflected in the statistics of the European Commission.
Information on mutual assistance, including the amounts recovered, is provided in the table below.
4.4.2 International assistance for debt recovery in Germany
The legal authorisation for international administrative assistance in tax matters derives from European Community law, Council Directive 2008/55/EC of 26 May 2008 (EC Recovery Directive) and the Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In the interests of more accessible wording and better readability, the EC Recovery Directive codifies Council Directive 76/308/EEC of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Recovery Directive was transposed into national German law by the Act (EC) on the collection of State taxes of 3 May 2003.
The recovery procedure in Germany is governed by the German Fiscal Code.
Article 117.2 of the Code emphasises that tax authorities may provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities which are applicable in national jurisdiction and on the basis of the EC Law on Administrative Assistance.
Part Six of the German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) lays down statutory provisions governing the recovery procedure.
The administrative acts of the tax authorities are governed in particular by the instructions for execution and the instructions for enforcement.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with the representatives of the highest tax authorities of the Länder on the principles of administrative assistance for the assessment of taxes and transferred its own responsibility in this regard to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general prerequisites for making requests for recovery are as follows:
• Legal requirements must be fulfilled (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic means of enforcement have already been exhausted.
• Claims which are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be final.
• From the issue of the enforcement order or the date on which the claim becomes final (i.e. is no longer subject to appeal), no more than 5 years may elapse before the date of submission of applications.
• The total amount of the claim must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
German requests for recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the implementing departments of the tax authorities to the relevant foreign office, such as the Czech CLO, through the intermediary office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The further procedure is governed by the Methodological Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Recovery of Claims) of 19 January 2004.25 Currently, the Working Group of the Federal Government and the Land Governments is reviewing this methodological guideline in order to adapt it to the Recovery Directive.
The application, including the annexes, shall be submitted electronically by the Financial Office to the Intermediate Office.
That authority shall check the correctness of the application in terms of content and form.
If the application is not correct, it shall be returned to the competent tax authority.
If it meets all the requirements, it is referred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Revenue Office will then ensure the necessary communication with the relevant foreign office and will also provide a translation of the application.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Requests for recovery received from other Member States are registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and an acknowledgement of receipt is sent within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check that the formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office submits these requests to the Intermediary Office, which then forwards them to the competent tax authorities and monitors their execution.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
If the processing of the application takes more than 6 months, the Intermediate Office shall invite the submission of an interim report to be submitted pursuant to Article 16 of Commission Directive 2002/94/DG.
Once the formal and factual elements of the request have been checked, the implementing services shall notify the method of recovery.
Any sums recovered must be transferred to the bank account specified in the application within one month of their receipt.
Statistical data
Information on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims between Germany and the Czech Republic in 2006-2008 (as of 31. 12. 2008) are shown in the table below.
4.4.3 Monitoring of recovery, case studies
Within the framework of international cooperation, 21 requests for international assistance in the recovery of receivables between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for audit.
The examination of ten selected cases revealed, inter alia:
1st
On the 20th. 10 a.m. 2006 the Czech Ministry of Finance received from Germany a request for recovery of VAT receivable for the years 2004 and 2005 in the total amount of EUR 3,883, i.e. CZK 109 820, with the Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the tax administrator a request for recovery until 26. 2nd 2008
In order to secure the enforced claim, the Czech tax administrator established a lien on real estate owned by the Czech tax entity.
Since it was not possible to pay the entire enforced debt even by pledging the real estate, a repayment schedule was agreed with the Czech tax entity with instalments of at least CZK 2,000 per month.
On 31. 8th 2009 information on the state of recovery was sent to the German tax administration, stating that as of 25. 8th In 2009 this receivable was partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49 600.
That sum was sent to Germany and then on 28. 8th In 2009, another instalment of CZK 3 000 was sent to Germany.
2nd
The Czech Ministry of Finance received on 7. 1st 2008 application for recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed EUR 180 869 in Germany, i.e. 4 434 915 CZK, for VAT and income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the tax administrator until 27. 11th 2008
By examining the ownership of accounts with banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movable property, the tax administrator found that the debtor does not own any exequatable assets.
Furthermore, a local investigation found that the debtor had not resided at his permanent address for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6 June 2005. 4th 2009 and on 16. 4th 2009 the tax administrator's reply was sent to the German tax administration.
3rd
The Czech Ministry of Finance received from Germany on 21. 11th 2007 request for recovery concerning tax arrears on turnover tax and accessories of the Czech tax entity in the amount of EUR 3 139, i.e. 84 846 CZK.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery of this claim on 6 June 2005. 8th 2008 to the tax authorities, although already on 18. 2nd 2008 The Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the receivable in Germany.
The Czech Ministry of Finance on 9. 12. 2008 informed the tax administrator that the request for recovery is settled by payment of the receivable by the Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also paid in the context of recovery in the Czech Republic and paid to Germany on 27 July 2005. 10 a.m. 2008
Due to the long time periods within which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the authorized tax administrators, the receivable was paid twice in this case - by the entity itself in Germany and by the Czech tax administrator's recovery of the receivable.
In cooperation with the BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been included in the claim arising from a further recovery request of EUR 6 649 to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance only registers a request for recovery of a claim of EUR 3 139 with this company; the request for recovery of a claim of EUR 6 649 does not appear in the records of the Czech Ministry of Finance with the company in question.
4th
The Czech Ministry of Finance received on 15. 9th 2008 from Germany an application for recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity which owed in Germany in respect of income tax and VAT and accessories the amount of EUR 39 957, i.e. 956 654 CZK.
On 19. 12. 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax administrator.
On 1. 6th In 2009, the recovery procedure was initiated, execution was ordered for the ordering of the receivable in accounts with banks in the Czech Republic and for the deduction from wages (the deduction amounted to CZK 7,000).
During negotiations with the tax administrator, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the claim and considered it questionable.
The Czech tax authority found that the tax entity had been willing to repay EUR 250 per month in the past, which was not accepted by the German tax authority.
The tax entity promised to discuss the application with the German tax authorities with a view to obtaining a change in the amount of its claim.
Enforcement of the receivable continued during the SAO audit operation.
5.
On 19. 11th 2007 The Czech Ministry of Finance received from Germany a request for recovery concerning a Czech tax entity that owed income tax for 2005 and turnover tax for the period 2003-2007 and accessories totalling EUR 113,444, i.e. 3 116 304 CZK.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the ÚO for Prague 1, which is responsible for administering the tax for non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, until 14. 11th 2008, because it was not possible to identify the locally competent tax administrator on the basis of the tax entity's address.
During the investigation, the FCA obtained information that the debtor had on 19. 9th 2008 income in the amount of EUR 4 704; however, the FCA could no longer issue an execution order for this amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance submitted the request for recovery only after this date.
On the 26th. 1st 2009 The Czech tax administrator initiated the recovery of the receivable and issued an execution order for the attachment of the receivable to the debtor's funds in accounts held with banks and savings and credit unions.
Enforcement of the receivable continued during the SAO audit operation.
6th
The Czech tax administrator requested international cooperation in recovering the VAT claim and the costs of the proceedings in the total amount of CZK 146 223 742 on 3. 10 a.m. 2006.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send this request for recovery to the German tax authorities until 13. 5. 2008
The German tax authorities of 8. 9th 2008 transferred to the Czech authorities through the Federal Bank the amount obtained from the execution of funds in the debtor's account in the amount of EUR 17 700, i.e. 439 226 CZK.
An error in the recalculation of the amount recovered was found during the verification of the amount recovered.
The amount recovered was CZK 146 223 742 converted at the rate of EUR 1 = CZK 25,065 erroneously to EUR 583 378.
The correct conversion of the amount to be recovered is EUR 5 833 781,83.
A request for recovery was therefore sent to Germany which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7th
The Czech tax administrator on 1. 3rd 2007 sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance to recover the tax arrears from the Czech tax entity, which owed CZK 1,970,632 for VAT and accessories, i.e. EUR 79 847.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the German tax authorities until 10. 11th 2008
The German tax authorities of 4. 2nd 2009 called on the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant declines in the company's turnover in the second half of 2008 and in particular in the first half of 2009 and the related liquidation situation of the company, the following payments were made to cover the arrears: 4th 2009 amount of EUR 4 600, 6. 5. 2009 amount of EUR 3 000 and on 16. 6th 2009 amount of EUR 2 500.
These payments were sent to the tax administrator's account in the Czech Republic.
On the 23rd. 6th 2009 the German tax administrator agreed with the debtor that by 30. 6th 2009 will pay a further instalment of EUR 2 500.
8th
Request for recovery of a total amount of EUR 398 653, i.e. CZK 9 832 779, including a claim for real estate transfer tax, was delivered from the Czech tax administrator to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22 June 2017. 5. 2008
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request for recovery to the German tax administration on 2 February 2005. 10 a.m. 2008
On 3. 4th In 2009, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a communication from the German tax administration that the application had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax authorities justified the refund on the ground that the transfer tax was not a tax within the meaning of Article 2 (b) of the Sixth Directive. (e), (f), (g) and (b) (h) Council Directive 2008/55/EC.
The German tax authorities further stated that Article 2 (b) of the Sixth Directive provides: (g) relates to claims relating to income tax and wealth tax.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive 2008/55/EC applies to taxes on income and capital, which are listed in Article 1 (2). 3 in conjunction with par. 4 of Council Directive 77/799/EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed to prepare and submit a new request for recovery, excluding arrears of real estate transfer tax in the amount of CZK 61 759 and indicating arrears of VAT, corporate income tax and personal income tax, which will be resent to the German tax administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has received a new request from the Czech tax administrator for the recovery of tax arrears concerning the same tax entity that owes CZK 7,079,735 in income tax and VAT.
9th
On 6. 2nd In 2006, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed CZK 3,445,782 in personal income tax and VAT, i.e. EUR 123 328.
Of this amount, VAT accounted for CZK 1 133 967.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the German tax authorities until 18. 4th 2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded to the Czech tax authority a reply from the German tax authority dated 9. 7th 2007 to 11. 11th 2008
The reply stated that the German tax authorities had issued the tax on 11. 6th 2007 an execution order to a bank account at the bank, which however stated that it had no business relations with the tax entity.
The German tax authorities therefore considered the application to be settled.
10 a.m.
On the 26th. 9th 2005, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of VAT arrears totalling CZK 1,296,845, i.e. EUR 43 591.
The request from the Czech tax administrator was delivered to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10. 10 a.m. 2005.
Czech Ministry of Finance on 15. 12. 2005 sent a request to the German tax authorities.
Before sending the request for recovery, the Czech tax administrator executed an execution on the debtor's funds in bank accounts and a deduction from wages and established a lien on the immovable property.
The request for recovery was preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authorities on 16 June 2008. 3rd 2005.
From the reply to the request for information received by the Czech tax authority 16. 9th 2005, it emerged that the Czech tax entity resides in Germany and had an income of EUR 8 437 from non-business activities.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a reply to the request for recovery on 20. 4th 2006, but did not forward it to the Czech tax administrator until 12. 2nd 2008
The reply stated that no recovery procedure could be initiated in Germany because of the debtor's insolvency - he had not been found to have any assets and his non-business income was already subject to another enforcement procedure.
The German tax authorities therefore considered the request for recovery to be completed.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of processing requests for international assistance in the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and the BRH compared statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In a 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay more attention to keeping their statistics.
In the 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of discrepancies in statistics had decreased even though the number of applications had increased.
Both SAIs consider it important to revisit statistical issues at EU level.
