This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent mismatches, otherwise the data reported by individual EU countries in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, both SAIs agree that reliable statistics should show the annual number of claims as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amount of claims recovered by each Member State.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by the Member States, as this can assist Member States in assessing their own effectiveness in combating VAT fraud.
The fact that the recovery rate can be calculated broken down by Member State is seen by both SAIs as useful for Member States with lower recovery rates to step up their efforts to improve the recovery rate at least to the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should be actively involved in this process.
In particular, in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for recovery of receivables to the locally competent tax authorities on time.
A similar situation was found for requests for international assistance received from tax authorities from the Czech Republic.
The auditing operation revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not proceed in accordance with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of receivables, because it did not inform the locally competent authority of the Member State about the progress in recovery within six months from the date when the request was confirmed.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General Information Inc.
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as those of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for the inspection of VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons who were established or established for business purposes and whose net turnover for the tax period stated in the personal/corporate income tax return amounted to CZK 2 billion. CZK or higher.
The inclusion of the tax entity in the VDS took place after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant tax period, for the first time in 2003.
A tax entity ceased to be classified as a VDS if, in three consecutive tax years from the end of the period in which it submitted the tax return on the basis of which it was classified as a VDS, its net turnover for the tax year fell below that threshold.
A tax subject could not be excluded from the VDS register without carrying out a tax inspection of at least one tax per tax period.
All VDS were checked at least on a five-yearly basis until the end of 2009.
Since 2010, a written evaluation of the tax subject must be carried out at least every 2 years and the tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax must be eliminated by the chosen follow-up procedure.
The SAO audit is focused on at least one type of tax; the tax administrator usually chooses several tax periods at once.
The VDS were audited by the specialised audit units, which are set up at a total of 13 FCAs, or by the staff of the audit units of the locally competent FCAs.
The Specialised Inspections Unit shall carry out tax inspections within the limits of the powers laid down by the Director of the Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• tax entities operating in unusual and specific lines of business;
• entities for which it is extremely technically and time-consuming to carry out a tax audit;
• entities with a large territorial and organisational structure;
• entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• Entities linked in chains and networks suspected of large-scale tax evasion and undue evasion of excess deductions.
The number of tax audits carried out by the specialised audit units of the FCA and the results of these audits are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed an amendment to Act No.531/1990 Coll., on Territorial Financial Authorities, which consists in establishing a specialized FCO with nationwide competence for selected tax entities (including legal entities established for business purposes which have a turnover of more than CZK 2 billion). CZK).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General Information Inc.
VAT inspections of large companies are governed by the same rules as tax inspections in general, i.e. The relevant provisions are laid down in the following regulations: • the German Fiscal Code (AO), • the Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), • the Tax Control Regulations (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory provisions on inspection are laid down in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - On-the-spot tax inspection. In particular, these articles lay down rules on the admissibility of on-the-spot tax inspections (i.e. on the premises of the undertaking), their scope in terms of subject matter, the rules on the allocation of responsibilities, the form and content of the inspection notice, the principles of inspection, the taxpayer's obligation to cooperate and the prerequisites for carrying out the final examination and communication of the inspection report.
On-the-spot tax inspections are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Administration Act According to Article 5.1 (1) in connection with Art. Participation in on-the-spot tax inspections carried out by the tax authorities is compulsory for the Federal Central Revenue Office.
The nature and extent of the Federal Central Tax Office's participation in tax inspections shall be agreed between the participating authorities on the spot.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that specific undertakings which it selects be subject to inspection at a time to be determined by it.
In that case, it may promulgate rules on the conduct and content of the inspection at the premises of those companies.
Rules on tax inspections According to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the rules on tax inspections (German abbreviation BpO 2000) were approved by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, the upper house of the German Parliament, in which the Länder governments are represented).
These administrative provisions apply to on-the-spot checks carried out by the Länder tax authorities and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The undertakings are classified according to size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of the BpO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to ex post control (Article 4.2 BpO).
Under Paragraph 33.1 of the BpO 2000, each informed tax authority must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in the BpO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, the following guidelines set out the additional methodology for tax administration:
• A single manual for special VAT inspections in Germany;
• a USLO manual setting out the methodology for the use of VIES data on intra-Community business relations;
• a ZAUBER manual setting out the methodology for the use of the ZAUBER database;
• Working aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits depending on the type of business.
The figures are published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the following three years.
The number of companies to be inspected - not just large enterprises - must be determined at regular inspection intervals.
As a general rule, checks on large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Inspections are usually announced including VAT inspections.
This means that during the audit, checks will be carried out definitively in particular on income taxes, excise duties and VAT - i.e. checks on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT inspections may be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisational structure of the Länder.
The number of tax years covered by inspections is usually between three and five years.
BpO 2000 foresees a control period of three years.
The subject of the examination is all taxes of the company.
4.5.3 Control management of large tax entities
Both SAIs decided not to examine individual cases of VDS inspections carried out, but focused on management issues in order to obtain an overview of how tax administrations manage the issue of VAT inspections at VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they gathered information from tax administrators on areas they consider essential for managing this issue.
• What statistical records and analyses concerning VAT control at VDS are available to the management of tax administrations?
In particular:
• Are there any statistics or rate records distinguishing between the fight against VAT fraud and VAT control in general?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such a distinction in the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between an inspection designed to combat VAT fraud and a general VAT inspection.
• Are there any statistics or records on the timeliness of VAT checks (linked to the time period of the transactions audited)?
Czech Republic: Records on the timeliness of inquiries with relevance for intra-Community acquisitions of goods for selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, data such as how long the interview took are also part of the information recorded in ADIS.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors contain only information on the average time of the last check (year information).
This data does not provide an overview of selected control periods with regard to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the most recent tax assessment period; they also have the right to carry out VDS inspections.
However, the statistics produced at federal level for the special VAT inspection services do not provide information concerning the classification of tax entities.
• Are there any statistics or records on the nature of the additional tax revenues generated, broken down e.g. according to the following criteria:
i. net increase in tax liability (e.g. in cases where the tax subject has unduly applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
(ii) only a nominal increase in tax liability (e.g. moving a fully qualified VAT case to another tax year);
(iii) additional collection of tax revenue (payment of additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech tax administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the volumes of additionally assessed tax broken down by type of tax, by the number of audited tax subjects and by the number of audited tax periods.
Other tax procedures (local enquiries, accusation procedures) are followed in the same way.
Time data and amounts of additional taxes paid are recorded as a separate task.
General debt statistics are also kept broken down by type of tax, but not by declared tax or tax recorded by the tax administrator.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and for VAT special inspection services do not distinguish between these criteria.
Moreover, most of the tax administrations visited do not distinguish between these differences either.
• Are the control areas resulting in high additional revenues recorded?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administrator has the right to select tax payers for verification on the basis of criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in special sections of ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection services do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach between the Finance Ministers of the Länder and the Federal Government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must enter their assessed increased tax (VAT) liability if it exceeds a certain amount.
In such a case, it must specify, for example, the nature of the tax increase charged.
• What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- VDS claim an unjustified right to deduct input tax for supplies and services:
• which have not been used to carry out any economic activity pursuant to § 72 para. 1 of the VAT Act;
• which have been used for representation pursuant to § 75 para. 3 of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents that did not meet the requirements set out in Section 73 para. 1 of the VAT Act;
- VDS did not declare output VAT pursuant to Section 21 para. 1 of the VAT Act.
Germany: It has been noted that there are no rules at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection services do not provide such data.
VAT findings are not separately recorded by the Länder in so far as they result from VDS tax inspections.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder have to enter their assessed increased tax (VAT) liability if it exceeds a certain amount, the Federal Central Revenue Office is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration carry out analyses of areas of control that give rise to a high "revenue" and draw consequences for management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they are launching nationwide audits focused on risky commodities or on the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
Uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection services do not provide data on audit areas that generate high "revenue."
There are different views on the analysis process as well as on the materiality management of cases.
Some regional tax authorities provide special information, but its use is at the discretion of the tax authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
Differences in the replies of both Member States show that the Czech Republic ensures a system that collects a wealth of data from tax audits carried out, as well as data from financial statements - balance sheets and profit and loss accounts.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to guide the selection of risk-prone cases.
The same applies to the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, it is planned to establish a specialised financial authority in the Czech Republic for the management of VDS.
In Germany, the tax authorities do not collect this information.
This makes it more difficult to carry out these tasks in a similar way.
However, Germany's philosophy places greater emphasis on the selection of individual cases on the basis of data from the submitted tax returns.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to assess the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAIs agree that Member States should be able to ensure adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help to reduce VAT gaps.
As a result, the revenue from VAT collection will increase and the rate of risk detection for unreliable entrepreneurs will improve.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of both SAIs on parallel audits of VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and the BRH.
Both SAIs have gained a better understanding of each other's systems in the following areas: • intra-Community transactions; • VAT risk management, in particular as regards the selection of risk-prone transactions; • assistance with the recovery of VAT claims; and • VAT control for large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in VAT fraud detection strategies as well as differences in the above-mentioned areas of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany were revealed.
The control findings were compared and good practices were identified.
In addition, the two SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to launch a debate on approaches and strategies within the Member States, including at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of both SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT administration.
6th Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Editorial deadline: June 2010.
